*v118 - Session 116 CLOSE — Mux video migration for the learning platform + Operations Doc-1 invoice bug fixes (logo-upload RLS, expense-receipt-on-invoice opt-in). One new §-rule (§155); §1–§154 hold (with a correction to §154's branding-bucket claim, below). **(1) §155 NEW — a storage bucket needs a SELECT policy for authenticated uploads to succeed, not just INSERT.** The Supabase storage upload path reads the object back after writing it, so an authenticated upload to a bucket that has INSERT/UPDATE/DELETE policies but NO SELECT policy is rejected with "new row violates row-level security policy" even though the INSERT with_check evaluates true. operations-branding was created S115 (§154) with insert/update/delete but no select (the §154 claim that branding + documents "each got 4 storage.objects policies" was wrong for branding — it had 3); operations-documents and operations-receipts each have the SELECT policy and upload fine. Fix S116: added ops_branding_select (FOR SELECT TO authenticated USING bucket_id='operations-branding' AND (storage.foldername(name))[1]=current_org_id()::text — identical org-path shape to the siblings); branding now has all four. RULE: every org-scoped storage bucket that authenticated users upload to needs the full 4-policy set including SELECT; an upload RLS failure is as likely to be a missing SELECT policy as an INSERT one. DIAGNOSTIC LESSON: a direct SQL INSERT into storage.objects as the authenticated role passing RLS does NOT prove the storage upload will pass (it does not replicate the read-back); compare the full policy sets across sibling buckets before theorizing about clients or tokens. The earlier opsSupabase-stale-token theory for this bug was WRONG — the client (opsSupabase vs the main supabase client) was never the cause; both fail without the SELECT policy and both succeed with it. **(2) Mux video pipeline (learning platform, replaces storage-served video for real content).** content_items gained mux_asset_id / mux_status / duration_seconds (nullable). Playback read RPC get_content_item_video_playback(uuid) (SECDEF search_path '') mirrors the existing video access gate (auth/self/admin/mentor + module-published + curriculum-assignment) and returns null playback while a video is still preparing. Four Edge Functions: mux-create-upload (verify_jwt true, super-admin; brokers a Mux direct-upload URL, signed playback policy, passthrough=content_item_id, 1080p; sets mux_status='preparing'); mux-webhook (verify_jwt FALSE, Mux-Signature HMAC-SHA256 over `${t}.${rawBody}`; on video.asset.ready writes mux_asset_id + video_source_id=signed playback id + duration_seconds + mux_status='ready' and flips video_source_type='mux'; idempotent; unsigned→401); get-content-item-video-url v4 (verify_jwt true; mux branch mints an RS256-signed Mux playback JWT — claims sub=playback_id, aud='v', exp=now+7200, kid — supabase_storage branch unchanged); mux-ingest-existing v3 (verify_jwt true, super-admin, one-time URL-pull ingest, CORS preflight, optional exclude_ids[]). **DEVIATION (record): the Mux JWT is signed with `npm:jsonwebtoken@9`, not Web Crypto** — jsonwebtoken accepts the PKCS1/PKCS8 PEM Mux issues (the signing key is a base64 PEM decoded via atob), matching Mux's own SDK; Web Crypto's stricter key import was the reason for the switch. **Mux source-id exemptions:** both the upsert RPC and the content_items_video_required CHECK constraint exempt video_source_type='mux' — a mux item's video_source_id (the playback id) arrives asynchronously from the webhook, not at save, so requiring it at save time would block authoring; the constraint had previously exempted only supabase_storage. Re-saving a mux item with an empty source-id field preserves the webhook-set playback id (the upsert RPC coalesces). record_video_progress is unchanged. Frontend: the trainee viewer uses @mux/mux-player-react (signed token, onTimeUpdate+onEnded → record_video_progress); authoring upload uses @mux/upchunk against the brokered upload URL and polls mux_status. 19 real videos live as mux/ready; 5 test items intentionally left on supabase_storage. NOTE for any future bulk flip: the asset.ready handler overwrites video_source_id with the playback id, erasing the original storage-asset pointer, so snapshot content_item→content_asset mappings before flipping if rollback is desired. **(3) Expense receipts attach to the invoice email via an opt-in flag.** public.ops_get_invoice_expense_receipts(p_invoice) (SECDEF search_path '', org-gated: invoice.org_id must equal current_org_id() or it raises) returns receipt_storage_path + a derived suggested_filename ('Receipt-'||basename with the uuid prefix stripped) for each billable, invoiced expense on the invoice that has a receipt; the invoice→expense linkage is expenses.invoice_line_id → document_lines(document_type='invoice', document_id=invoice). authenticated+service_role, anon/PUBLIC revoked. ops-invoice-send v9 gained an opt-in include_expense_receipts body flag (default OFF, so the prior single-PDF-attachment behavior is unchanged): when true it calls the RPC via the caller's client (authorization holds), downloads each receipt from the private operations-receipts bucket via the service-role client, and appends them to the Resend attachments alongside the invoice PDF, with a 38MB total-size guard (skips overflow, logs which) and returns {attached, pdf_attached, receipts_attached, receipts_skipped}. PATTERN: server-side derives the attachments from the invoice itself (the frontend only passes the invoice id + the boolean), so no receipt paths cross the client; the frontend uses the same RPC purely to show a count and gate the opt-in checkbox. Edge fn versions: mux-create-upload v1 NEW, mux-webhook v1 NEW, mux-ingest-existing v3 NEW, get-content-item-video-url v4, ops-invoice-send v9; all other ops + platform fns unchanged. Close artifacts (markdown only, Session-74): build-queue v124, this v118 entry, session-116-to-117.md.*

*v117 - Session 115 CLOSE — Operations Doc-1 P3 conversions + P1 in-app refund + P5 Reports + P6 PDF engine & branding. One new §-rule (§154); §1–§153 hold. **(1) §154 NEW — branded-document generation is client-side; email attachment is client-generate → upload-to-private-bucket → server-download-and-attach (ONE generator).** A client jsPDF generator (`src/lib/operations/documentPdf.ts`) is the single source of document layout for invoices/estimates/receipts: one engine, three template configs (standard/corporate/detailed) differing only in header treatment, table-head fill, and totals itemization; brand identity from operations.organizations, recipient block from the customer record; jsPDF lazy-imported; logo fetched from the public operations-branding bucket → dataURL → addImage in try/catch. Because the customer email is sent server-side (Resend in `ops-invoice-send`), a browser-generated PDF is not present at send time; the reconciliation is: the client generates the same PDF, uploads it to the private operations-documents bucket at path `{org_id}/Invoice-{id}.pdf`, then invokes the send fn with `attachment_path`; the fn validates the path begins with the invoice's own `org_id/` segment (it downloads via service role, bypassing RLS, so that prefix check is the guard), downloads, attaches base64 via Resend, and returns `{attached}`; it falls back to send-without-attachment if the file is missing. RULE: never build a second server-side layout engine to satisfy an attach/print requirement — generate once on the client, persist, attach server-side. **(2) Refund initiation and ledger writing are separated.** The in-app refund path (`ops-issue-refund` v1, verify_jwt true) authorizes via `ops_get_refundable_payment` and calls `stripe.refunds.create` ONLY — it writes no ledger rows. The existing `ops-stripe-webhook` v3 `charge.refunded` branch → `ops_handle_stripe_refund` stays the sole, idempotent, delta-based writer of `payments.refunded_amount` + invoice reopen. PATTERN: a Stripe-mutating ops action initiates at the edge fn and lets the webhook reconcile the ledger; never double-write the ledger from both the initiator and the webhook. `refundable_amount` = amount − excess_amount − refunded_amount; a payment is refundable in-app only when its intent is `pi_`-prefixed AND mode ∈ {stripe_card, stripe_ach}. **(3) Operations report fact-view pattern (P5).** Reporting reads from thin security_invoker views (report_invoices / report_invoice_lines / report_payments / report_time / report_expenses), each carrying org_id, LEFT JOINed to customers/items/projects/users for names, org scope enforced by the underlying tables' RLS (security_invoker=true), GRANT SELECT to authenticated+service_role only (NO anon → not in any anon-revoke sweep). Derived money is computed in-view (expense billable = amount×(1+markup/100); time cost via project_users.cost_rate; running timers excluded). Reuse the existing project_financials_rollup + customer_balance_summary rather than re-deriving profitability/AR. UI reads them via `opsSupabase.from(view as any)` (operations-types.ts is untyped for them) and Number()-coerces numeric-as-string columns. **(4) organizations branding read/write split.** operations.organizations gained identity/branding columns (legal_name, address jsonb, email, phone, tax_id, website, logo_url, brand_color DEFAULT #021F36, accent_color DEFAULT #F5741A) seeded for BrainWise. RLS exposes SELECT to authenticated scoped to current_org_id() (so the client reads branding directly for the generator) but has NO update policy — writes go through `ops_update_org_branding` (SECDEF, admin-only via current_user_role()='admin', partial patch via COALESCE on a p_patch jsonb so omitted keys preserve prior values; address overwrites wholesale since the form round-trips it). **(5) Two org-scoped storage buckets, receipts pattern.** operations-branding (public-read, for the logo so the client can fetch+embed it) and operations-documents (private, for generated PDFs the edge fn attaches) each got 4 storage.objects policies keyed on `bucket_id` AND `(storage.foldername(name))[1] = current_org_id()::text` — identical to operations-receipts; path segment 1 is the org id. **(6) Estimate conversion guards.** estimates carries converted_invoice_id / converted_project_id / converted_retainer_id; the three convert RPCs are mutually exclusive (each guards all three before acting); convert→project under billing_method='none' copies estimate lines to billable project_charges, while hourly methods copy budget only (0 charges) so an hourly project never double-bills the estimate work. **(7) Stale-CDN verification lesson.** raw.githubusercontent.com can serve byte-identical STALE content even with a ?cb cache-bust param, producing a false "ship failed" signal; GitHub MCP get_file_contents (API, returns the commit SHA) is the authoritative post-ship check — never conclude a Lovable ship failed from the raw CDN alone. Edge fn versions: `ops-issue-refund` v1 NEW, `ops-invoice-send` v3; all other ops fns unchanged from S113/S114; no platform-fn work. Close artifacts (markdown only, Session-74): build-queue v123, this v117 entry, session-115-to-116.md.*

*v116 - Session 114 CLOSE — Operations P2-extras (time/expense frontend depth + 4 supporting migrations) + a PTP psychometric reverse-scoring correction, historical-rescore pattern, and a tiered-auth Edge Function fix. One §-rule corrected (§152), new reusable patterns; §1–§153 otherwise hold. **(1) §152 CORRECTED — point it at §140.** v114/v115 attributed the anon-grant-survives-revoke behavior to a "grant reconciler that re-applies anon EXECUTE within the creating session." That was a misdiagnosis. Real mechanism: the new public RPCs had NO direct `anon` grant — anon held EXECUTE via the implicit `PUBLIC` grant Postgres puts on every new function. `REVOKE EXECUTE … FROM anon` is therefore a no-op (you cannot revoke a grant the role never directly held); `REVOKE EXECUTE … FROM PUBLIC` is the fix (this is §140). Verified live S114: `session114_p4_revoke_public_eight_rpcs` revoked PUBLIC on all 8 Phase-4 RPCs and `has_function_privilege('anon', oid, 'EXECUTE')` returned false for all 8, authenticated still true. STANDING RULE (folds §152 into §140): to lock an authenticated-only public RPC, `REVOKE EXECUTE FROM PUBLIC` (not FROM anon); anon's access is inherited through PUBLIC, not a direct grant. The earlier "must baseline into a prior session" claim is void. **(2) Debrief-capable AI generators must mirror tiered auth (generate-all-facets v6).** `generate-all-facets` (the 89-row `facet_insights_all` master builder) had an owner-only JWT auth path, so a super-admin (or linked coach) viewing another user's PTP report 403'd and the master never built. Fix: added a super-admin (`users.account_type='brainwise_super_admin'`) + linked-coach (`coach_clients`) branch to its JWT path, mirroring `generate-facet-interpretations`'s tiered auth; internal-secret + owner paths unchanged; verify_jwt=false. PATTERN: any narrative/facet generator that a super-admin or coach can legitimately trigger from a debrief view must carry the same tiered-auth branch as the per-context generator, or the master/section silently never builds for non-owner viewers. OPERATIONAL NOTE: generate-all-facets self-chains in batches of 10 across a ~110s budget via EdgeRuntime.waitUntil and the self-chain is unreliable (stalls mid-build, needs an accordion re-open to resume); it short-circuits if `facet_data length >= facet_insights_all_total`. For batch regeneration prefer a server-side fire with the internal secret (resumable) over babysitting the frontend chain. **(3) PTP reverse scoring reads the per-response SNAPSHOT, not the live items flag.** `assessment_responses.is_reverse_scored` is stamped at submit by `AssessmentFlow.tsx` from `items.reverse_scored`. Scoring (`calculate-scores`, mean = round(avg(reverse?100-rv:rv),2) trim_scale) consumes the snapshot. Consequence: flipping the items flag corrects NEW assessments only; historical reports need a snapshot backfill. `get_item_aggregate` reads the live flag, so until a backfill runs it diverges from individual reports (which read the snapshot) on any newly-flipped item. **(4) Rescore-in-place + parity-gate is the standing pattern for scoring corrections on historical data.** `calculate-scores` INSERTs a new result row (not upsert) and facet narratives are cached per `assessment_result_id` (FK `facet_interpretations.assessment_result_id` ON DELETE CASCADE — the only FK to `assessment_results`; a `both` result = 16 sections, a split-pair professional row = 11 because combined sections live on the professional row, a single-context = 6). So a clean historical rescore does NOT re-run calculate-scores; it is pure SQL: PARITY GATE (recompute fed the CURRENT pre-backfill snapshots must reproduce stored `dimension_scores` exactly — gate before any mutation) → backfill the affected `is_reverse_scored` snapshots → set-based in-place UPDATE of `dimension_scores`/`overall_profile` (stable result ids, no dupes) → DELETE `facet_interpretations` for the result → reset `narrative_status=null` (null is treated as "ready" by the frontend self-heal) → regen via the report's on-view self-heal. `trim_scale(round(avg,2))` matches JS `parseFloat(toFixed(2))` for parity. Applied S114 to 15 real result rows (73/73 dim-row parity, 0 mismatch). **(5) PSYCHOMETRIC RULE — never expose the reverse-scoring flip mechanic at the per-item level.** The per-item callout may warn that a question's labels run opposite from its neighbors, but must NOT explain that the score is flipped — telling a respondent the math invites pre-compensation (answering to game the flip), which corrupts the data. Normalization is explained conceptually only at the acknowledgement level, paired with an explicit anti-compensation instruction ("answer based on the two labels shown; our scoring takes care of the rest"). The acknowledgement copy is data-driven in `assessmentAcknowledgments.ts` keyed by instrument+rater (`INST-001:self`), and editing the body auto-rebumps the content-version hash. **(6) Frontend completeness gate trusts in-memory state, not DB persistence.** `AssessmentFlow.tsx`'s `allAnswered` (`items.every(it => responses[it.item_id] != null)`, `!= null` so a real 0 counts) gates Submit on the in-memory `responses` map, which is set before the DB write — so it blocks a user from advancing without answering, but does NOT catch a silent dropped per-item save (the cause of the one 69/89 result found this session). A server-side completeness guard in `calculate-scores` would close that residual; it was considered and DECLINED this session (front-end gate deemed sufficient). **(7) Operations P2-extras facts.** `operations.project_financials_rollup` (security_invoker view): cost = Σ(time hours × cost_rate) + expenses, revenue = invoiced-to-date EXCLUDING draft/void/written_off, plus margin, margin_pct, and a `cost_untracked_hours` flag for hours logged by members without a cost rate; GRANT SELECT authenticated + service_role (reuses the §-canonical read-as-view pattern). `ops_start_timer`/`ops_stop_timer` enforce a server-side single-running-timer invariant (start auto-stops any prior running entry for the user). `project_users` joined the direct-CRUD default set (org_id DEFAULT current_org_id(), created_by DEFAULT auth.uid()). Frontend reads ops tables via `opsSupabase`; public RPCs via the default supabase client (`supabase.rpc("name" as any)`); numeric-as-string view columns must be Number()-coerced; local date helpers use getFullYear/getMonth/getDate, never toISOString (UTC drift). Close artifacts (markdown only, Session-74): build-queue v122, this v116 entry, session-114-to-115.md.*

*v115 - Session 113 CLOSE — Operations Platform Phase 4 backend (recurring expenses + retainers + credit notes + overpayment-to-credit). One new §-rule (§153); §152 extended with an in-session reconciler finding; §1–§152 hold. **(1) §153 NEW — credit application reduces an invoice through a payment + allocation via one shared internal helper.** Every path that applies non-cash credit to an operations invoice — retainer apply, credit-note apply, customer-credit/overpayment apply — routes through operations._ops_apply_credit_to_invoice(p_org,p_invoice,p_amount,p_reference) (SECDEF, search_path ''), which inserts a payments row with payment_mode='credit' + reference + a payment_allocations row, then bumps invoices.amount_paid and recomputes status (partially_paid/paid) + paid_at, returning the new status. RATIONALE: invoices.balance_due is a generated column (total − amount_paid) and status is driven by amount_paid, so the ONLY mechanism that reduces an invoice's outstanding balance is amount_paid; modeling credit application as a payment+allocation keeps all balance math uniform and surfaces credit applications in the same payments view as cash. payment_mode CHECK extended to add 'credit' (now stripe_card|stripe_ach|ach|check|cash|wire|credit|other). The helper validates not-void/written_off/paid + amount<=outstanding and is the SOLE writer of credit payments. EXECUTE revoked from PUBLIC+anon+authenticated — it trusts a caller-supplied org and runs as definer, so leaving it callable is a multi-tenant hole; the outer SECDEF public RPCs invoke it as definer regardless of grant (same discipline as §113's _ops_emit_from_sel). Source-of-truth split: customer_credits is the wallet ONLY for overpayments (source_type='overpayment') and future refund-to-credit; credit_notes apply DIRECTLY from their own generated balance (total − amount_applied − amount_refunded) and retainers from their own generated available_balance (amount − applied_amount) — NO double-ledger; each document tracks its own applied counter and the helper only touches the invoice side. **(2) §152 EXTENDED — the anon-revoke reconciler re-grants WITHIN the creating session.** v114's §152 established that REVOKE EXECUTE … FROM PUBLIC does not drop anon on a public-schema function (Supabase ALTER DEFAULT PRIVILEGES grants anon directly) and a dedicated REVOKE … FROM anon is required. Session 113 established the sharper rule: for a NEWLY-CREATED, authenticated-EXPOSED public function, the explicit anon revoke does NOT hold within the same session — verified across same-migration, dedicated-follow-up-migration, and single-function-isolated-migration attempts on 8 new RPCs, all still anon=true afterward. The revoke holds only when (a) the function was created in a PRIOR session (ops_record_payment standalone revoke → held; ops_mint_public_token a session later → held), OR (b) authenticated is ALSO revoked, marking the function non-API (ops_run_recurring_expenses revoked from anon+authenticated+PUBLIC → held). The reconciler re-applies the default anon grant to functions it treats as freshly-created-and-API-exposed; baselining into a prior session's migration is what lets a later anon-only revoke stick. OPERATIONAL RULE: when you create an authenticated-only public RPC the frontend must call (so authenticated cannot be revoked), schedule the anon revoke as an S(N+1) opener, not an S(N) close item. NOT a security gap in the interim — these RPCs self-gate on current_org_id() returning NULL for anon and raise before any data access (the same posture ops_create_estimate has shipped with since S112). **(3) Recurring runners.** public.ops_run_recurring_expenses() mirrors ops_run_recurring_invoices (one generation per cron run, advance schedule by frequency×interval_count, deactivate past end_date; inserts a non-billable overhead expense). Both are pure-DB SELECT public.fn() crons running as postgres (jobid 26 '15 0 * * *' for expenses), so REVOKE PUBLIC+anon+authenticated + GRANT service_role is safe (superuser bypasses grant checks). The S108 invoice runner ignores its auto_email + auto_charge_stored_card columns by design (v1 generates drafts only). ops_run_recurring_invoices was patched this session to derive each generated line_total = COALESCE(line_total, quantity*unit_price - discount_amount) for both the per-line value and the invoice subtotal, so it consumes the frontend's template_lines shape (which stores quantity/unit_price/discount_amount, not a precomputed line_total); without this the runner read a missing line_total and generated $0 invoices. **(4) Retainer + credit-note lifecycles.** retainer_invoices status draft→sent→paid→applied|refunded (apply requires paid; flips to applied when available_balance drains; refund only when applied_amount=0). credit_notes status draft→open→closed|void (issue opens; apply/refund close when balance drains; void only when amount_applied=0 AND amount_refunded=0). Both carry their own applied/refunded counters with generated balance columns; numbering types 'retainer' (RET-) and 'credit_note' (CN-) seeded S108. **(5) Overpayment-to-credit.** ops_record_payment(uuid,jsonb) body-only CREATE OR REPLACE (same signature → no overload, §59/§125 not triggered) now allocates least(amount,balance), stamps payments.excess_amount, and mints a customer_credits overpayment row for the excess; ops_apply_customer_credit_to_invoice draws it down via the §153 helper. payments.excess_amount + customer_credits.source_type (overpayment|credit_note|refund) were pre-wired S108. **(6) Test discipline reinforced.** Functional tests ran as one execute_sql DO block: set_config('request.jwt.claims', json_build_object('sub',<ops admin uuid>,'role','authenticated'), is_local:=true) at the top so current_org_id()/auth.uid() resolve inside the txn, then fixtures + RPC calls + assertions, then RAISE EXCEPTION encoding the assertion values into the error text (surfaces results AND rolls back — a DO-block RAISE NOTICE does not surface under MCP). Zero document numbers consumed, zero residue. Migrations (snake_case): session113_p4_recurring_expense_runner_and_cron, session113_p4_payment_mode_credit_and_apply_helper, session113_p4_retainer_rpcs, session113_p4_credit_note_rpcs, session113_p4_overpayment_to_credit_and_apply, session113_p4_revoke_anon_record_payment, session113_p4_revoke_anon_explicit_followup, session113_p4_revoke_anon_retry_isolated, session113_p4_recurring_template_org_created_defaults, session113_p4_recurring_invoice_runner_derive_line_total. No Edge Function work; Phase 4 frontend shipped via 5 Lovable cycles (each verified against the repo). Close artifacts (markdown only, Session-74): build-queue v121, this v115 entry, session-113-to-114.md.*

*v114 - Session 112 CLOSE — Operations Platform Phase 3 (estimates + accept-by-link + convert + public customer pay page + estimate-send email). New architectural facts + one new §-rule (§152); §1–§151 hold. **(1) Shared public tokenized-access model (NEW §152).** operations.public_access_tokens (id, org_id FK organizations, document_type CHECK invoice|estimate, document_id, purpose CHECK pay|accept, token_hash text UNIQUE, expires_at nullable, created_at, created_by, revoked_at, last_accessed_at; idx on org and on (document_type,document_id,purpose); RLS on, 4 policies; anon has NO table grant). **HASH-ONLY:** the raw 32-byte token (64 hex via extensions.gen_random_bytes) is returned once by mint and never recoverable — only sha256 (extensions.digest) is stored. Consequence: there is no "resend the same link" — minting revokes any prior live token for the same (document, purpose) and issues a fresh one, so re-sending an invoice/estimate email invalidates the previously-emailed link (secure default; behavior change worth stating). No hard expiry by default; validity gated on document status instead (invoice read hidden when void/written_off; estimate read hidden when draft; accept allowed only from sent/viewed). Five public-schema SECDEF functions, search_path '': **ops_mint_public_token(p_document_type, p_document_id, p_purpose, p_expires_in_days DEFAULT NULL) RETURNS text** — resolves the document's org, gates current_org_id()=that org, revokes prior live token, mints + stores hash, returns raw; **AUTHENTICATED-ONLY**. **ops_get_public_document_by_token(p_token) RETURNS json** — hashes, validates live, bumps last_accessed_at, for an estimate flips sent→viewed, returns a SANITIZED bundle (amounts/lines/customer display_name/org name/status — NO email, address, staff, or internals); ANON+authenticated. **ops_accept_estimate_by_token / ops_decline_estimate_by_token(p_token[, p_reason])** — validate (estimate+accept, live), require status sent/viewed, set accepted/declined, idempotent on already-terminal; ANON+authenticated. **GRANT discipline gotcha (part of §152): `REVOKE EXECUTE ... FROM PUBLIC` does NOT remove anon on a public-schema function, because Supabase's `ALTER DEFAULT PRIVILEGES` grants EXECUTE directly to the named `anon` (and `authenticated`) roles, not via PUBLIC. To lock mint to authenticated-only you must `REVOKE EXECUTE ... FROM anon` explicitly (the named role); verify with has_function_privilege('anon', oid, 'EXECUTE').** This is the sharper form of the v113 note ("internal SECDEF helpers must REVOKE from authenticated+anon"). Verified: mint anon_exec=false; the three public RPCs anon_exec=true; table anon grant=none. **(2) Token-validated full-bundle RPC for public checkout.** The sanitized read deliberately omits email/address/stripe_customer_id/tax codes, so the public pay page's checkout needs a separate **ops_get_invoice_checkout_bundle_by_token(p_token) RETURNS json** — SECDEF, anon-granted, token-gated (pay+invoice, live, not void/written_off), returning the SAME full shape as ops_get_invoice_checkout_bundle (incl. customer email/billing_address, stripe_customer_id, per-line stripe_tax_code). PATTERN: a public Stripe-checkout edge function gets its privileged read via a token-validated SECDEF bundle RPC — never the sanitized public read, never raw service-role table access. **(3) Estimate lifecycle RPCs (mirror the invoice RPCs).** ops_create_estimate(p_header,p_lines) / ops_update_estimate(p_id,p_header,p_lines) / ops_set_estimate_status(p_id,p_action: mark_sent|mark_accepted|mark_declined|mark_expired) / ops_convert_estimate_to_invoice(p_estimate). Estimates have NO shipping_amount/payment_terms_days/due_date; total = subtotal − discount + adjustment; they carry expiration_date. document_lines is polymorphic on document_type='estimate'. Convert is allowed from accepted OR sent/viewed, blocks double-convert (converted_invoice_id guard), copies header+lines to a fresh-numbered draft invoice and flips the estimate to invoiced. All authenticated-only (anon revoked). Numbering type 'estimate' (EST-YYYY-NNNN). **(4) Two new edge functions + one repoint.** ops-public-invoice-checkout v1 (**verify_jwt FALSE** — possession of a live pay token is the authorization; calls the by-token bundle RPC, gates balance>0 + not void/written_off/paid, get-or-create Stripe customer, pre-tax line_items w/ per-line tax_code + automatic_tax, success/cancel → ${APP_ORIGIN}/pay/${token}?paid=1|canceled=1). ops-estimate-send v1 (verify_jwt true — org-gated read via NEW ops_get_estimate_send_bundle(p_estimate) SECDEF returning estimate header + customer email, mints an accept token via the USER client, emails a respond link → ${APP_ORIGIN}/estimate/${token}, marks sent only when status=draft; from estimates@mail.brainwiseenterprises.com). ops-invoice-send v1→v2 (single change: mints a pay token via the user client and repoints the email button from /operations/invoices/{id} to /pay/{token}; otherwise byte-identical). **(5) Public routes are unauthenticated + noindex.** /pay/:token (PublicInvoicePay) and /estimate/:token (PublicEstimateRespond) live in App.tsx's top public-routes block OUTSIDE ProtectedRoute, use the DEFAULT supabase (anon) client for the public RPCs and functions.invoke, and inject `<meta name="robots" content="noindex,nofollow">`. STATIC_ROUTES in newsletter-sitemap deliberately NOT touched — a per-customer tokenized page does not belong in a public sitemap (overrides the carried "add /pay to STATIC_ROUTES" instruction). **(6) Frontend client split holds:** operations table reads via opsSupabase; all public-schema RPCs + edge functions via the default supabase client (supabase.rpc("name" as any, …)). Estimate surfaces (EstimateForm/OperationsEstimates/OperationsEstimateDetail) mirror the invoice surfaces; StatusBadge in operations/_shared gained accepted/declined/invoiced/expired keys. **(7) Production-publish diagnostic (process note):** Lovable "ship" updates repo + preview, but a custom domain serves the last PUBLISHED build — new routes 404 until publish. Distinguish stale-deploy from code-bug by fetching the live index.html → its hashed /assets/index-*.js → grep for the new route path strings vs known-old strings. Edge fn versions at 112 close: ops-invoice-send **v2**, ops-public-invoice-checkout **v1**, ops-estimate-send **v1**, ops-invoice-checkout v1, ops-stripe-webhook v3, ops-payment-receipt v1, ops-payment-reminder-cron v1; platform stripe-webhook v31 untouched. Close artifacts: build-queue v120, this v114 entry, session-112-to-113.md.*

*v113 - Session 111 CLOSE — Operations Platform invoicing depth (edit/delete of billable inputs + Way B customer-level invoicing + invoice detail levels). New architectural facts + patterns; no §-renumbering (§1–§151 hold). **(1) operations.invoiceable_candidates** (security_invoker VIEW, GRANT SELECT authenticated) is the pick-and-assemble source for customer-level invoicing: one row per selectable unit — charge, expense, rated task (task-rate), project (project-rate), and person (staff-rate; amount NULL when the person has no billing rate). 14 cols incl. candidate_type, project_id/project_name, ref_id, ref_user_id, quantity/unit/unit_price/amount, currency_code, candidate_key. Read via opsSupabase (operations schema). Being a UNION-ALL view it is not updatable, so the schema's default authenticated write grants are inert on it. **(2) public.ops_create_invoice_from_selection(p_customer, p_selection jsonb, p_detail text DEFAULT 'itemized')** SECDEF search_path '' GRANT authenticated — the multi-project composer: recomputes every amount server-side from the source rows (never trusts the client), validates each id against customer+org+billable+uninvoiced, blocks mixed currencies, sets invoice.project_id to the lone project or NULL when the selection spans projects, and raises on any stale/ineligible item via an expected-vs-found unit count. p_selection shape {charge_ids[], expense_ids[], task_ids[], project_time_ids[], staff_time:[{project_id,user_id}]}. Called via the default supabase client (public-schema RPC); typed in public types.ts, NOT operations-types.ts. **(3) public._ops_emit_from_sel(p_org, p_invoice, p_detail, p_uid)** SECDEF search_path '' — the shared line-emission helper for BOTH composers (ops_create_invoice_from_project and ops_create_invoice_from_selection). Each composer first populates a pg_temp._sel component temp table (kind/project_id/project_name/descr/quantity/unit/unit_price/amount/currency/charge_ids/time_ids/expense_ids/task_id), then calls the helper. Itemized emits one document_line per component, description "Project - Item" (separator is " - ", a hyphen, not an em dash). Summary emits one line per project (GROUP BY project_id, summing the already-rounded component amounts, so the summary total equals the itemized total to the penny by construction). The helper flips every consumed source row (project_charges/time_entries/expenses) to is_invoiced + invoice_line_id. **EXECUTE revoked from PUBLIC, authenticated, AND anon** — the helper trusts a session temp table and runs as definer, so leaving it callable is a multi-tenant hole (a user could craft their own pg_temp._sel and manipulate invoices/source rows across orgs); the outer SECDEF composers invoke it as definer regardless of the grant. The PostgREST one-statement-per-request model already blocks the exploit (no mid-request temp-table creation), but the REVOKE is the correct floor. **PATTERN: internal SECDEF helpers that trust caller-provided temp-table state must REVOKE EXECUTE from authenticated+anon — schema default privileges auto-grant EXECUTE on every new public function, so the REVOKE is required, not implied.** **(4) Both composers gained p_detail via DROP+CREATE** (adding a parameter creates an overload, §59/§125) with DEFAULT 'itemized', so pre-existing callers are unaffected; ops_create_invoice_from_project's itemized output now carries the project-name prefix (intended behavior change). public types.ts Args gained p_detail?: string on both; operations-types.ts Functions block stays [_ in never]: never (these are public-schema RPCs). **(5) document_lines** confirmed shape: source_project_id (NOT project_id), source_task_id, and uuid[] arrays source_charge_ids / source_time_entry_ids / source_expense_ids; a summary line legitimately carries all three arrays at once. invoices.customer_id NOT NULL, project_id nullable (lone-project or NULL). **(6) Edit/delete lifecycle for billable inputs:** time entries, expenses, and tasks are editable/deletable only while uninvoiced; invoiced rows are read-only until void/delete releases them (existing release patch). Expense delete also removes the receipt from operations-receipts storage; task delete is FK-aware (logged time blocks it, surfaced from Postgres 23503). **PATTERN reinforced:** functional tests run as ONE execute_sql DO block (set_config request.jwt.claims → fixtures → call the SECDEF RPCs → assert → RAISE to roll back the whole txn) consume no document number and leave zero residue; reset the source rows between in-block compose calls so each call sees uninvoiced inputs. Close artifacts: build-queue v119, this v113 entry, session-111-to-112.md.*

*v112 - Session 110 CLOSE — Operations Platform Phase 2 (time + expenses + charges into billing). New architectural facts + patterns (no §-renumbering; §1-§151 hold). **(1) COMPOSABLE BILLING supersedes single-mode (amends v111 product model).** projects.billing_method no longer names the whole billing scheme; it names the HOURLY scheme ONLY — one of project_hours | task_hours | staff_hours | none. Fixed fees are no longer a billing_method; they live as operations.project_charges rows. Expenses are always independent of billing_method. A single project can therefore carry, at once, a fixed fee (charge) + hourly tasks (task_hours) + reimbursable expenses. Chose Option B (separate project_charges table) over Option A (boolean flag on project) for clean composition and independent invoiced-state tracking. projects_billing_method_check now admits 'none' ('fixed' kept valid defensively; no live projects existed to migrate). **(2) operations.project_charges** (org_id default current_org_id() FK organizations, project_id FK projects ON DELETE CASCADE, customer_id nullable FK customers, date default today, description NOT NULL, amount default 0, currency_code default USD, is_billable default true, is_invoiced default false, invoice_line_id, notes, timestamps, created_by default auth.uid(), updated_by) — canonical 4-policy RLS (select/insert/update same-org, DELETE admin-only via current_user_role()='admin'), GRANT authenticated. Follows the v110 canonical operations RLS pattern exactly. **(3) Rollup-as-view.** operations.project_time_rollup is a security_invoker VIEW at project grain (entry/billable/nonbillable/invoiced/uninvoiced/unbilled-billable hours, with customer_id/customer_name for customer-level aggregation), GRANT SELECT authenticated. Chosen over an RPC for step-2 rollups: a view composes into PostgREST selects and inherits RLS via security_invoker without a SECURITY DEFINER surface. Pattern: read-only cross-row aggregations over RLS-protected operations tables should be security_invoker views, not SECDEF RPCs. **(4) operations-receipts private bucket** with 4 org-path-scoped storage.objects policies keyed on bucket_id='operations-receipts' AND (storage.foldername(name))[1] = operations.current_org_id()::text — the same first-path-segment = org_id ownership pattern used elsewhere; receipts upload at `${orgId}/${uuid}-${name}`. expenses + expense_categories got org_id DEFAULT current_org_id() + created_by DEFAULT auth.uid() (extends the v111 direct-CRUD default pattern; their org_id is made optional in operations-types.ts Insert types accordingly). **(5) Invoice composition RPC + source-consumption model.** public.ops_create_invoice_from_project(p_project, p_date_from, p_date_to) (SECURITY DEFINER, search_path '', GRANT authenticated) is the composer: for only is_billable AND NOT is_invoiced rows in range it emits charges (one free_form line each), time (per billing_method: task_hours = one line per rated task, untasked/rate-less time EXCLUDED and left uninvoiced; project_hours = one line at project_hourly_rate, excluded if null; staff_hours = one line per user at coalesce(project_users.billing_rate, users.default_billing_rate) and RAISE EXCEPTION if any billable user lacks a rate; fixed/none = no time billed), and expenses (one line each at amount x (1 + markup%/100)). It sets invoice.project_id, writes per-line provenance arrays (document_lines.source_time_entry_ids / source_expense_ids / source_charge_ids — source_charge_ids NEW this session), and flips every consumed source row to is_invoiced=true + invoice_line_id=<line>. If zero lines compose it RAISES (rolls back, releasing the just-consumed document number). Reuses next_document_number_for_org and mirrors ops_create_invoice total math (tax 0). **(6) Source-release on delete/void; write_off does NOT release.** ops_delete_draft_invoice and ops_set_invoice_status(void branch) now release sources BEFORE the delete/void: UPDATE time_entries/expenses/project_charges SET is_invoiced=false, invoice_line_id=NULL WHERE invoice_line_id IN (the invoice's document_lines). Verified both paths revert all three source types; the voided invoice remains as a record. write_off intentionally leaves sources consumed (the invoice still stands as billed); mark_sent unchanged. Standing implication: any future terminal-state transition that voids the billing relationship must release sources; any that preserves it (write_off) must not. **(7) Multi-FK embed disambiguation.** time_entries has 4 FKs into operations.users (user_id, created_by, updated_by, approved_by), so PostgREST member-name embeds MUST name the constraint: users!time_entries_user_id_fkey. **(8) Customer-pay architecture gap (recorded, fix slotted P3).** ops-invoice-send emails a branded pay button pointing at /operations/invoices/{id}, which is RoleGuard brainwise_super_admin gated — external customers cannot pay from the email. The Stripe path (ops_get_invoice_checkout_bundle / create-checkout / webhook) is fully built; only a public, tokenized landing page is missing. Decided fix = Option A: a public /pay/:token route with a tokenized read + on-demand Stripe checkout, repointing the email button (slotted into Phase 3, not pulled forward). When it ships, STATIC_ROUTES in newsletter-sitemap needs the manual add. No ops Edge Function versions changed this session (ops-stripe-webhook v3, ops-payment-receipt v1, ops-invoice-send v1, ops-invoice-checkout v1, ops-payment-reminder-cron v1; platform stripe-webhook v31 untouched). Close artifacts: build-queue v118, this v112 entry, session-110-to-111.md.*

*v112b - Session 110 PARALLEL PLATFORM FIX (run alongside the Operations Phase 2 session; main-platform subsystem, NOT operations). Architectural deltas + reusable patterns; no new §-numbered rules; §1-§151 hold. **(1) $0 super-admin comp coach orders carry a sentinel payment ref.** A $0 Stripe Checkout produces no PaymentIntent, so the client "coach paid" gate (which keys on `coach_clients.stripe_payment_intent_id IS NOT NULL`, read via `coach_clients_client_view WHERE client_user_id = auth.uid()`) used to drop comped clients into self-pay. `stripe-webhook` (live v31) now, in `checkout.session.completed`, writes `comp_<session.id>` into `stripe_payment_intent_id` on the `coach_clients` + coach-owned `assessment_purchases` rows in the `coach_order` and `coach_bulk_order` branches only (self-pay + subscription branches untouched). Sentinel format is `comp_*`; real PaymentIntents are `pi_*`. **VERSION RECONCILIATION:** v111 recorded platform stripe-webhook "v31, untouched"; live is v31 and now carries this fix, so the pre-fix version was actually v30 and this is the deploy that produced v31. Live `get_edge_function` is truth; the v111/v117 "untouched" note is superseded for stripe-webhook only. **(2) Comped clients must have `client_user_id` linked** for `coach_clients_client_view` to return their row (the view is scoped to `auth.uid()`). **(3) CoachInvoices excludes sentinels.** `CoachInvoices.tsx` coach-scoped query adds `.not("stripe_payment_intent_id","ilike","comp_%")` so a $0 comp does not render as a fake N x $29.99 invoice + total. The `CoachClients.tsx` "Paid" badge rendering `comp_` rows as Paid is intended UX (the seat was comped, just at $0). **(4) No unique index/constraint on `stripe_payment_intent_id`** in `coach_clients` or `assessment_purchases` (confirmed via `pg_index`), so a deterministic `comp_<session.id>` cannot collide (bulk orders already share one real PI across rows). **(5) `consume_assessment_purchase` is non-blocking for coach-paid clients** (`AssessmentFlow.tsx` try/catch), so a comped client needs no client-owned (`coach_client_id` NULL) purchase row to reach results. **(6) No refund worker exists** in Postgres or any edge function; the `refund_*` columns on `assessment_purchases` are recorded values only, not driven by a Stripe-calling worker. STANDING IMPLICATION: if a refund worker is ever added it must gate on `amount_paid > 0` or `stripe_payment_intent_id LIKE 'pi_%'` before `stripe.refunds.create`, so `comp_` sentinels never reach Stripe. **(7) `generate-facet-interpretations` (live v44) parseAiJson has a `jsonrepair@3.14.0` fallback** — on a parse throw it tries `JSON.parse(jsonrepair(candidate))` before re-throwing. The four combined `section_type` rows (`profile_overview_combined`, `personal_summary_combined`, `dimension_highlights_combined`, `cross_and_action_combined`) are required by the `PTPNarrativeSections` self-heal completeness check; a single malformed-JSON throw on the combined path used to 500 the invoke and leave the Combined tab self-healing forever. jsonrepair is a safety net; the durable fix is moving the combined paths to Anthropic tool-use (typed JSON). No new §-numbered rules; close artifacts shared with v112 (build-queue v118b, this v112b, session-110-to-111.md).*

*v111 - Session 109 CLOSE — Operations platform went frontend + Phase 1 money path complete. New architectural facts + patterns (no §-renumbering; §1-§151 hold). **(1) Locked operations product model.** Customer to invoice via nested in-context creation: customer has many named projects; `projects.billing_method` is one of `fixed` (rate from `fixed_cost_amount`), `project_hours` (from `project_hourly_rate`), `task_hours` (rate lives on each `project_tasks.task_hourly_rate`), `staff_hours` (rate lives on `project_users.billing_rate`). `project_tasks` is the rate-bearing unit for task-hours billing and is DISTINCT from `items` — `items` is a fixed-price catalog for invoice/estimate lines; there is no FK between tasks and items; `time_entries` reference a project + optional task, never an item. Roll-up: time to project to customer, invoiced on any cadence. UX principle: in-context modal creation, multiple intuitive entry points allowed, customer-detail = hub, project-detail = sub-hub, no orphan destination pages. **(2) Phase 1 invoice/payment RPCs (all public-schema, SECURITY DEFINER, search_path '').** `ops_record_payment(p_invoice uuid, p_payment jsonb)` mirrors `ops_handle_stripe_checkout_payment`'s record-allocate-update-status logic for OFFLINE payments (modes ach/check/cash/wire/other), supports partial payments, guards void/written-off + over-balance, rejects overpayment for now (overpayment-to-credit deferred to Phase 4); granted authenticated. `ops_set_invoice_status(p_id, p_action)` does mark_sent/void/write_off with transition guards, org via `current_org_id()` (so the frontend never passes org, unlike the older `ops_mark_invoice_sent(p_invoice,p_org)`). `ops_clone_invoice(p_id)` copies header + `document_lines` to a fresh-numbered draft via `next_document_number_for_org`. `ops_delete_draft_invoice(p_id)` draft-only guarded delete. All granted authenticated; frontend calls via the DEFAULT supabase client (public RPCs), not `opsSupabase`. **(3) Refund reflection pattern.** `ops_handle_stripe_refund(p_event_id, p_event_type, p_payload, p_payment_intent, p_amount_refunded)` (SECDEF, granted service_role only) is idempotent via `stripe_webhook_events`, finds the operations payment by `stripe_payment_intent_id` (NOT metadata), reduces the allocated invoice's `amount_paid` by the newly-refunded delta, reopens status (paid/partially_paid/sent) and clears `paid_at` when no longer paid, and records `payments.refunded_amount`. `ops-stripe-webhook` v2 to v3 adds a `charge.refunded` branch AHEAD of the `metadata.source==='operations'` guard, because a charge object does not carry the checkout session's metadata — refunds must be identified by payment-intent lookup in `operations.payments`, not by the source tag. The existing `checkout.session.completed` handler and source guard are unchanged; `verify_jwt` stays false (Stripe signature). **Standing implication:** any future ops Stripe event whose object lacks session metadata (refunds, disputes) must be identified by DB lookup and handled before the source guard, not gated by it. **(4) `ops-payment-receipt` v1 (NEW Resend fn, verify_jwt true)** emails a receipt summary (total / paid-to-date / balance) via `ops_get_invoice_checkout_bundle` RLS read; `ops-invoice-send` (pre-existing v1) emails a View-and-Pay message and marks sent. Both are USER-TRIGGERED (button-invoked), never automatic — aligns with send-on-explicit-action. **(5) Direct-CRUD default pattern extended.** `org_id` DEFAULT `operations.current_org_id()` + `created_by` DEFAULT `auth.uid()` now also on `projects`, `project_tasks`, `time_entries` (time_entries also `user_id` DEFAULT `auth.uid()`); `is_approved`/`is_billable` already default true and `is_invoiced` false, so manually-logged time lands approved-and-uninvoiced (the v1 "implicitly approved" decision is baked into the schema). Each direct-CRUD table whose `org_id` gets a default must have its `org_id` made optional in the hand-maintained `operations-types.ts` Insert type. **(6) Numbering-drift learning.** Resetting `numbering_schemes.next_number` to 1 after a backend test is only safe with zero real invoices; once real invoices exist it desyncs and the next allocation collides. Correct practice: after any number-consuming test, restore `next_number` to max+1 (and set `last_reset_at=now()` so the yearly reset does not snap back). Never reset to 1 once production data exists. Edge fn versions at 109 close: ops-stripe-webhook **v3** (was v2), ops-payment-receipt **v1** (new), ops-invoice-send v1, ops-invoice-checkout v1, ops-payment-reminder-cron v1; platform stripe-webhook **v31** untouched. Close artifacts: build-queue v117, this v111 entry, session-109-to-110.md.*

*v110 - Session 108 CLOSE — Operations platform (Zoho replacement, Doc 1) backend foundation through Phase 3 money + Phase 4 partial. New architectural facts + reusable patterns (no §-numbered rule renumbering; §1–§151 hold). **(1) Schema-isolated multi-tenant subsystem.** All operations data lives in a single `operations` schema (dot-notation), tenant root `operations.organizations` (NOT `public.organizations` — Doc 5 §2.3 Rule 1 forbids cross-schema FK ops→public; a `platform_organization_id` plain-uuid column bridges to the platform with no FK). `operations.users.id` is PK = FK to `auth.users.id` (shared Supabase auth). **(2) Canonical operations RLS pattern (reuse for every ops table):** two SECURITY DEFINER helpers `operations.current_org_id()` and `operations.current_user_role()`, both `SET search_path=''` and non-recursive (resolve from `operations.users WHERE id = auth.uid()`); each table policy filters `org_id = operations.current_org_id()` for SELECT/INSERT/UPDATE, DELETE additionally requires `current_user_role()='admin'` — EXCEPT line/child tables (`document_lines`, `payment_allocations`) which permit same-org DELETE since editing is routine. Authenticated + service_role only; anon NEVER granted. Proven both directions via simulated JWT. **(3) Numbering engine dual-entry.** `operations.next_document_number_for_org(p_org, p_type)` holds the atomic row-locked allocator (yearly/monthly reset, prefix + segment + zero-pad → `INV-2026-0001`); the user-facing `next_document_number(p_type)` delegates using `current_org_id()`. The org-explicit form exists because cron/SECDEF contexts have no `auth.uid()`, so JWT-derived `current_org_id()` returns null there — any future cron that allocates numbers must call the `_for_org` form. **(4) Stripe isolation under one shared account (Gap 5=A).** A SECOND webhook endpoint (`ops-stripe-webhook`, its own `OPS_STRIPE_WEBHOOK_SECRET`) handles only objects tagged `metadata.source=operations`; it acks-and-ignores anything else. Operations reuses the shared `STRIPE_SECRET_KEY`. The platform `stripe-webhook` (v29) branches on `metadata.checkout_type` and falls through harmlessly on an untagged ops object, so cross-delivery is safe both ways. Platform `stripe-webhook`/`create-checkout` are never modified — preserves the corporate-invoice/zero-Stripe boundary. **(5) Mixed-taxability design.** Stripe Tax is authoritative for calculation: `items` and `document_lines` each carry `stripe_tax_code`; `ops-invoice-checkout` builds PRE-TAX line_items each passing its own tax_code with `automatic_tax.enabled=true`, so Stripe computes tax on top per line at checkout (handles Cole's services-plus-digital mix without a global category). **(6) Webhook-writes-via-public-RPC pattern.** Edge Functions cannot use supabase-js `.schema('operations')` unless the schema is EXPOSED in the API settings; to stay independent of that, ALL operations writes from Edge Functions route through public-schema SECURITY DEFINER RPCs (`ops_handle_stripe_checkout_payment`, `ops_upsert_stripe_customer`, `ops_mark_invoice_sent`) that touch `operations.*` internally. Reads that must respect RLS use a SECURITY INVOKER public RPC (`ops_get_invoice_checkout_bundle`) called with the user's JWT. **(7) Operations cron taxonomy.** Pure-DB jobs (overdue flag, recurring generation) run `SELECT public.fn();` directly via pg_cron; only email-sending jobs (payment reminders) use the `net.http_post` + `X-Dispatcher-Secret` (vault `departure_dispatcher_shared_secret` → function reads `DISPATCHER_SHARED_SECRET`, constant-time compare) dispatch pattern. **(8) Operations email = Resend-direct.** Ops functions send via the Resend API directly from `invoices@`/`reminders@` on the already-verified `mail.brainwiseenterprises.com` domain (domain-level verification covers any From address), rather than modifying the shared `send-email` fn — preserves the platform boundary; per-sender-subdomain reputation isolation is an optional future step. **(9) MCP test-hygiene learning.** Simulated-JWT functional tests (`SET LOCAL ROLE authenticated` + `set_config('request.jwt.claims',...)`) AUTO-COMMIT under the MCP execute_sql tool — test rows persist and must be explicitly cleaned, and any consumed document number reset, after every test. Multi-statement execute_sql returns only the last statement's result. Edge fn versions unchanged on the platform side (check-ai-usage v50, stripe-webhook v29, ai-chat v40, create-checkout v60); NEW ops Edge Functions: ops-stripe-webhook v1, ops-invoice-checkout v1, ops-invoice-send v1, ops-payment-reminder-cron v1. Close artifacts: build-queue v116, this v110 entry, session-108-to-109.md.*
*v109 - Session 107 CLOSE — Queue-hygiene + scope-verification session. NO architectural changes: no backend, schema, or Edge Function changes (Supabase MCP read-only); no new §-numbered standing rules; §1–§151 all hold unchanged. *v108 - Session 106 CLOSE — Session-105 verification pass + DB-backed plan-copy single source + out-of-credits messaging fix + super-admin consolidation (Phase A/B). Narrative records + reusable patterns; no new numbered standing rules. **(1) plan_tiers single-source (NEW table).** Per-tier (tier PK free|base|premium, display_name, features jsonb array, ai_coaching_limit int, one_time_credit_grant int, sort_order, is_active). RLS: public read {anon,authenticated} qual=true (logged-out marketing reads it), service_role write. Chosen per-tier (NOT a column on subscription_plans) because subscription_plans is keyed per price-point (base/premium each have monthly+annual rows + a one_time row) — a features column there would duplicate per billing period and drift. 'free' lives here (no price/billing-period, never belonged in subscription_plans). useSubscriptionPlans hook fetches BOTH subscription_plans (priceFor/oneTimePrice, pre-existing) AND plan_tiers (NEW featuresFor(tier)/limitsFor(tier)) — purely additive. Four render sites read featuresFor(tier) ?? PLANS[tier].features (DB primary, lib/stripe.ts constant as fallback kept honest = correct copy on DB-read failure). **CRITICAL display-vs-enforcement split: plan_tiers.ai_coaching_limit + one_time_credit_grant are DISPLAY-ONLY mirrors. Enforcement of the 200/400 monthly cap lives in check-ai-usage; the granted +10 per assessment lives in stripe-webhook. The DB table does NOT drive enforcement. Any change to the enforced numbers must update BOTH the Edge Function AND the display mirror by hand.** This is the same decoupling class as the §105 displayed-price-vs-charged-price caveat. **(2) AI-chat entry points + credit awareness.** TWO surfaces invoke chat: the standalone /ai-chat page (renders LimitReached card) and the per-result Ask-AI bubble on MyResults.tsx. BOTH ultimately enforce via ai-chat (v40) → check-ai-usage (consuming call). MyResults previously gated its bubble on hasActiveAccess (subscription only) → credit-holding non-subscribers were wrongly blocked; fixed to canUseChat = hasActiveAccess || credit_balance>0 via a non-consuming check_only preflight. PATTERN: any new chat entry point must gate on credits-OR-subscription, never subscription alone, and must route through ai-chat so consumption/limits stay centralized in check-ai-usage. **(3) check-ai-usage v50 — subscription_active is now explicit on EVERY individual-branch response.** Root cause of the out-of-credits bug: FREE_TIER_DENIAL omitted subscription_active, and the frontend coerces undefined via `subscription_active !== false` → true → LimitReached rendered the active-subscriber monthly branch (false 'resets on [date]' copy + upgrade) for a non-subscriber. Fix: inactive-individual denial returns subscription_active:false; the monthly-exhausted + race-guard responses now set it explicitly too (were correct only by undefined→true coincidence). PATTERN: when a frontend uses `x !== false` to read an optional boolean, the backend MUST send that boolean explicitly on every branch or the default silently flips. **(4) Out-of-chat UX decision (Cole):** ALWAYS steer to Upgrade to Premium (not 'buy another assessment'), across all surfaces. LimitReached non-subscriber branch = 'You're out of AI chat messages / Subscribe to Premium for {premiumLimit}...' + Upgrade button, no false monthly-reset copy. **(5) Super-admin consolidation.** Per-individual feature override RELOCATED from the standalone Features page into the Members drawer as a new 'Access' tab (MemberDrawerAccess.tsx), gated member.organization_id===null (non-corp = individuals + coaches). The Features page renamed 'Global Features & Settings', now holds only the platform-wide instrument flags (Card 1). Per-coach actions (Mark Certified, View PTP Report) MOVED into the drawer Coach tab; the coaches page slimmed to invites-only, renamed 'Coach Invitations' (/super-admin/coaches route kept, no redirect). DESIGN PRINCIPLE established: per-entity actions (override a user, certify a coach) belong on that entity's drawer; population-level tooling (bulk/Excel coach invites that onboard not-yet-users) stays on its own page — do not force population tooling into the per-member Members view. **(6) member-drawer tab pattern + a gotcha:** adding a drawer tab requires updating the TabId union in BOTH MemberDrawer.tsx AND the parent super-admin/Members.tsx (which has its own TabId + VALID_TABS validator that coerces unknown ?tab= values back to 'learning'); the parent's `as TabId` cast suppresses the type error so a missed update passes build but the tab won't activate at runtime. Grep ALL TabId/VALID_TABS when adding a tab. Edge fn versions at 106 close: check-ai-usage v50, stripe-webhook v29, ai-chat v40, create-checkout v60.*
