*v107 - Session 105 CLOSE — Platform feature-flag system, instrument-visibility gating, one-time chat credits, and DB-sourced dynamic pricing. Narrative architecture records + reusable patterns; no new numbered standing rules.

**Feature-flag / instrument-visibility model (three layers).** A feature key is the string `instrument:<uuid>`. Three sources of truth resolve through `user_has_feature(p_user, p_feature)` (SQL, STABLE, SECURITY DEFINER): (1) super_admin → always true, before any gate; (2) CORPORATE users → `org_has_feature(org_id, feature)` is the ceiling and a `member_feature_overrides` row may only SUBTRACT (an override of false hides; an override of true is a no-op against an org that lacks it); (3) NON-CORPORATE (individual) users → a `member_feature_overrides` row wins in either direction, else the `platform_features` default, else true for an unflagged feature (un-flagged features are NOT hidden). `platform_features` (feature PK, enabled, label, category, updated_at, updated_by; RLS super_admin + service_role) holds the platform-wide individual defaults: PTP enabled, NAI/EPN/AIRSA/HSS disabled, all category='assessment'. `member_feature_overrides` (user_id, feature, enabled; UNIQUE(user_id,feature)) RLS: super admin reads all, same-org admin reads own org, user reads own, service_role all. Corporate entitlement lives in the contract, surfaced by `organization_features_view`.

**`org_has_feature(p_org uuid, p_feature text) → boolean`** reads `organization_features_view` for the org and, for an `instrument:<uuid>` key, returns `instruments_included ? <uuid>` (jsonb `?` existence). It also handles `ai_chat` (→ ai_chat_enabled) and `dashboard_access` (→ dashboard_access_level IS DISTINCT FROM 'none'); any other key raises. **`organization_features_view`** (RLS-scoped to the caller's org, single row) exposes: organization_id, tier_id, tier_name, **instruments_included (jsonb ARRAY of instrument UUID strings)**, monthly_ai_pulls_allowance, monthly_chat_allowance_per_user, monthly_coaching_query_allowance, ai_chat_enabled, dashboard_access_level, seat_count, data_retention_mode, supervisor_dashboard_enabled, start_date, end_date. instruments_included is an ARRAY (e.g. `[\"02618e9a-...\"]` for a PTP-only contract), not an object — frontend membership is `arr.includes(uuid)`.

**New gating RPCs (Session 105).** `user_has_features_bulk(p_user uuid, p_features text[]) RETURNS TABLE(feature,enabled)` plpgsql STABLE SECDEF — one round-trip wrapper over user_has_feature; a caller may only bulk-check their OWN features (p_user=auth.uid()) unless they are super_admin. Replaces the N-parallel-call anti-pattern on the instrument picker. `platform_feature_set(p_feature,p_enabled,p_reason) RETURNS jsonb` SECDEF — super-admin-only writable setter for platform_features (assert_super_admin + assert_impersonation_allows('permission_change'), reason>=10, 'platform_feature_not_found' for unknown key, changed:false no-op when unchanged, stamps updated_at/updated_by, audited as action_type 'platform_feature_set' under category usage_management). `individual_feature_override_set(p_user,p_feature,p_enabled,p_reason)` SECDEF (Session 105) — super-admin-only per-individual override; rejects corporate targets; p_enabled NULL clears; audited as 'individual_feature_override' under user_management. **The `super_admin_action_types.category` CHECK whitelist is fixed: impersonation, org_management, user_management, admin_role_management, contract_management, content_authoring, platform_observability, usage_management, mfa_management, audit_reporting** — there is no \"configuration\" bucket, so platform_feature_set was filed under usage_management.

**Individual instrument-gating predicate (frontend).** A non-corp, non-super-admin individual sees an instrument iff `isPTP(uuid) || user_has_feature('instrument:'+uuid) || hasEntitlementSignal(uuid)`. PTP is always visible; super-admins bypass. The entitlement-signal OR is mandatory and prevents regressions: a coach-invited, purchased, subscribed, cert-pool, assigned, completed, or in-progress instrument stays visible even when the platform flag is off. Surfaces gated: InstrumentSelection.tsx (picker; hidden non-PTP cards roll up into one BriefingModal request-access card, source=\"individual_instrument_access_request\"), Assessment.tsx (autostart/direct-URL useEffect mirrors the predicate and clears params → picker on miss). MyResults is NOT filtered (existing data shows). AiChat is NOT changed (peer-instrument toggle is corp-only; own-results context selector intentionally untouched).

**Corporate dashboard gating (frontend).** The three corp dashboards (CompanyDashboard=NAI, PTPDashboard=PTP, AirsaDashboard=AIRSA) were ROLE-gated only; Session 105 added a CONTRACT gate via useOrgInstrumentAccess() reading organization_features_view.instruments_included. Sidebar children + parent are gated by inclusion; each page redirects to /dashboard when not included; super-admins bypass (no org row → must short-circuit to allowed). Route-level RoleGuard is unchanged.

**Super-admin platform-wide user search.** `search_impersonation_targets(p_query text, p_limit int, p_offset int, p_account_types text[], ...)` RETURNS TABLE(user_id, email, full_name, account_type, organization_id, ... total_count) is the typed, super-admin-scoped platform-wide user search (used by Members.tsx and the new PlatformFeatures page; pass p_account_types:[\"individual\"] to scope to individuals).

**One-time chat credits.** `users.one_time_chat_credits` (int, default 0) is a non-resetting balance. `chat_credit_grants` is an append-only ledger (user_id, amount, source, source_ref) with a PARTIAL UNIQUE INDEX on source_ref WHERE NOT NULL for idempotency (RLS enabled, no policies → definer/service-role only). `grant_one_time_chat_credits(p_user,p_amount,p_source,p_source_ref)` inserts ON CONFLICT(source_ref) DO NOTHING and bumps the balance only when a row was actually inserted; `consume_one_time_chat_credit(p_user)` atomically decrements WHERE balance>0 (returns -1 if none). Grants are issued by stripe-webhook (v29) in the payment branch only, +10 per assessment/instrument, source_ref `${payment_intent}:${instrumentId}`. Consumption order in check-ai-usage (v49): subscribers spend the monthly allowance first then credits; non-subscribers spend credits; individual limits are 200 base / 400 premium; ai_usage is always incremented for analytics. check-ai-usage returns additive fields credit_balance, subscription_active, used_credit. ai-chat (v40) delegates enforcement+increment to check-ai-usage via usage_type 'chat_message' — it is NOT inlined in ai-chat.

**Pricing is DB-sourced, not Stripe-synced.** `subscription_plans` (id, plan_name, tier, billing_period, price_usd, stripe_price_id, is_active, timestamps) is the display source; nothing syncs price_usd from Stripe. The page reads price_usd (via useSubscriptionPlans → priceFor/oneTimePrice) with a static fallback in stripe.ts; checkout still uses the stored stripe_price_id. The \"public read\" RLS on subscription_plans was broadened to {anon,authenticated} so the logged-out /pricing page is dynamic. **Decoupling caveat: the displayed price (price_usd, ours) and the charged price (Stripe under the price_id) are independent — a price change must update BOTH.** Current values: Base $10/mo + $90/yr, Premium $15/mo + $130/yr, per-assessment $29.99.

**Typing posture for new DB objects.** DB objects created this session — platform_features (table), user_has_features_bulk, platform_feature_set, individual_feature_override_set — are not yet in src/integrations/supabase/types.ts, so the frontend casts: `(supabase.rpc as any)(\"name\", {...})` and `supabase.from(\"platform_features\" as any)`. This mirrors the existing get_my_epn_assignments cast pattern and is the interim convention until types.ts regenerates.

*v106 - Session 104 CLOSE — Newsletter SEO/AEO/RSS (G3+G9) + email dispatch (G8 a/b/c) shipped. No new numbered standing rules; the additions below are narrative architecture records plus two reusable patterns worth noting.

**NEW RPC `list_public_published_articles()`** (SQL, STABLE, SECURITY DEFINER, search_path public+extensions+pg_temp; EXECUTE granted anon + authenticated + service_role per the §140 grant-discipline pattern). Single source of truth for "what newsletter articles are publicly live": filters `status='published' AND archived_at IS NULL AND gate='public' AND published_at IS NOT NULL AND published_at <= now()`. Returns slug/title/excerpt/seo_description/canonical_url/published_at/updated_at. Consumed by the three public discovery Edge Functions below; any future public article surface (e.g. a public index page) should consume this RPC rather than re-deriving the filter, so the public-visibility predicate lives in exactly one place.

**THREE NEW public Edge Functions (verify_jwt:false — crawler endpoints, return only already-public data, fail-soft to a minimal valid document on any error):** `newsletter-sitemap` (application/xml; STATIC_ROUTES array of marketing routes + live article URLs with lastmod), `newsletter-feed` (application/rss+xml; RSS 2.0, description from seo_description/excerpt — deliberately NOT full body, both because body is TipTap JSON and to avoid scrape-bait), `newsletter-llms` (text/plain llms.txt; site summary + key pages + live article list). All three render live from `list_public_published_articles()` each request, so newly published articles appear with no redeploy. **Maintenance caveat (record):** the `STATIC_ROUTES` list inside `newsletter-sitemap/index.ts` is HARDCODED. Article URLs are automatic; new public *marketing pages* are not — adding one requires a manual STATIC_ROUTES edit + redeploy. Discovery is wired via `public/robots.txt` (`Sitemap:` + `LLMs:` lines pointing at the function URLs) and `public/index.html` head (`<link rel="alternate" type="application/rss+xml">`). G3 rendering strategy resolved as Option A: Lovable platform-native prerendering for verified crawlers + the platform markdown surface for AI engines (both confirmed active via Lovable's verified-position Discoverability scan and an independent LinkedIn Post Inspector live scrape reading real per-article Title/Type/Author). No SSR proxy, no Edge-Function SSR. Per-article meta/OG/JSON-LD was already injected client-side by `NewsletterArticle.tsx` via `setPageMeta`; prerendering serves that rendered markup to JS-less crawlers.

**Newsletter email dispatch architecture (G8).** Consent model: explicit opt-in only, demonstrable consent (`consent_evidence` + `confirmed_at` + `linked_user_id`), no silent auto-subscribe — built strictest-fits-all for US+EU+UK+Canada (GDPR/CASL/CAN-SPAM). Becoming a paid user does NOT create newsletter consent. One unified `newsletter_subscribers` list; status enum `pending_confirmation|confirmed|unsubscribed|bounced|complained` (existing). Suppression is by status: dispatch loads only `status='confirmed'`. (Not legal advice; a real compliance review is warranted before EU/CA scale.)

- **Schema (G8a):** `newsletter_settings` (singleton id=true, `dispatch_trigger_mode` CHECK manual|automatic, seeded manual), `newsletter_dispatches` (one row per send: article_id, triggered_by_user_id nullable, trigger_type, status pending|sending|completed|failed|partial, recipient/sent/failed counts), and additive `email_logs` columns `dispatch_id` (FK), `opened_at`, `clicked_at`. RLS = inline super-admin EXISTS + service_role_all, matching the established table-policy pattern.
- **`newsletter-dispatch` Edge Function (DUAL-AUTH, v2).** Accepts EITHER a super-admin JWT (UI manual-send path: getClaims + users.account_type check + impersonation gate 'outbound_user_communication') OR a valid `x-dispatcher-secret` header matching `DISPATCHER_SHARED_SECRET` (cron/service path: skips JWT/super-admin/impersonation, records triggered_by_user_id=null, forces trigger_type=automatic). Because the secret path can't carry a JWT, `verify_jwt` is FALSE at the gateway and BOTH auth paths are enforced in-function — same pattern as `dispatch-grace-reminders` and `resend-webhook`. Perimeter verified: no-auth→401, wrong secret→falls through to JWT path→401, bad JWT→401, OPTIONS→204. Per recipient: generates a fresh raw unsubscribe token, stores its sha256 hash in `newsletter_subscribers.unsubscribe_token_hash` (Option 3 — reuses the existing `unsubscribe_from_newsletter(p_token)` RPC unchanged), embeds the raw token in the email link; sends via Resend direct POST (from `BrainWise Newsletter <newsletter@mail.brainwiseenterprises.com>`); logs each recipient to `email_logs` (email_type='newsletter', dispatch_id). Email opening text = first 4 paragraph/heading TipTap blocks rendered to inline-styled email-safe HTML (full rich body stays on-site behind the button). SCALE NOTE: sends in one invocation; very large lists (thousands) would risk the 150s edge timeout and should move to a queued/paginated model — premature now.
- **`resend-webhook` v5:** additive `email.opened`→opened_at and `email.clicked`→clicked_at mapping; all prior delivery/bounce/complaint handling + subscriber-status flips byte-preserved; verify_jwt:false (Svix signature is the gate).
- **In-product opt-in RPCs (G8b, SECDEF, authenticated+service_role, NOT anon):** `opt_in_to_newsletter()` upsert-by-email on the caller's `users.email` (email has a UNIQUE constraint, so it's upsert not insert): no row→insert confirmed+linked+consent; unsubscribed→re-confirm+relink; confirmed/pending→idempotent ensure-linked; **bounced/complained→DO NOT auto-resurrect** (link for record only, return error 'delivery_problem'). `opt_out_of_newsletter()` token-free for the settings toggle. `get_my_newsletter_subscription()` for toggle state. All call `_sync_to_resend_audience_internal(id,'add'|'remove')` on state change, matching the existing confirm/unsubscribe RPCs.
- **Scheduled-publish engine (G8c).** Latent gap found+fixed: `schedule_article` set status='scheduled'+scheduled_for but nothing published due articles. NEW `newsletter_articles.scheduled_by_user_id` captures the scheduler so the cron auto-publish can attribute the version snapshot + audit log to a real super-admin. `schedule_article` sets it (one-line additive). `_snapshot_article_version` gained a scheduled-actor fallback: when `auth.uid()` is null, read `current_setting('app.scheduled_article_actor')` before hard-failing — byte-identical for every existing (authed) caller, mirroring the fallback `log_super_admin_action` already uses for scheduled assignments. NEW `process_due_scheduled_articles()` (SECDEF, service_role only) loops due scheduled articles in a per-article exception block (one bad article can't abort the batch), sets the actor session settings, performs the publish transition mirroring `publish_article` (conservative duplication — the working authed RPC was deliberately NOT refactored), and returns dispatch_ids for articles to auto-send (mode=automatic). NEW `cron_publish_and_dispatch_due_articles()` calls it then fires `newsletter-dispatch` via `net.http_post` with the dispatcher secret for each dispatch_id; cron job `publish_and_dispatch_due_articles` runs every 15 min. Frontend: manual UI publish in automatic mode triggers dispatch from the already-authenticated browser in `runTransition`, gated on `prevStatus ∈ {draft,scheduled}` so re-publish (from unpublished) never auto-blasts; fully decoupled from publish success (own try/catch, unconditional dialog cleanup after).

**Reusable pattern — dual-auth Edge Function (JWT OR shared-secret).** When a function must serve both an interactive super-admin caller and a server/cron caller: check the shared-secret header first (constant-time compare against the env secret); if it matches, take the service path (no user context, skip user-scoped gates); otherwise run the full JWT+super-admin+impersonation path unchanged. Set verify_jwt:false at the gateway (a JWT-required gateway would reject the secret-only cron call) and enforce BOTH paths in-function. Re-verify the perimeter after the flip: a wrong secret must fall through and still be rejected by the JWT path, not silently pass. Precedents: dispatch-grace-reminders, resend-webhook, now newsletter-dispatch.

**Reusable pattern — cron-context attribution for SECDEF functions that call auth.uid()-dependent helpers.** A pg_cron-invoked SECDEF function has no `auth.uid()`. To let helpers that hard-require it (snapshots, audit logs) run in that context, capture the responsible user at action-setup time (store a `*_by_user_id` column), and in the cron function `set_config('app.<scope>_actor', that_id, true)` so the helper can fall back to the session setting. The helper's fallback must be additive: only consult the setting when `auth.uid()` is null, so every existing authed path is unchanged. Precedent: `log_super_admin_action`'s `app.scheduled_assignment_actor`; extended this session to `_snapshot_article_version` via `app.scheduled_article_actor`.

**Edge Function `_shared` module path under the MCP deploy tool (record/correction).** The MCP `deploy_edge_function` tool co-locates bundled files under the same root as the entrypoint (`source/`). A shared module passed as `{name:"_shared/x.ts"}` must be imported as `./_shared/x.ts`, NOT the `../_shared/x.ts` convention seen in older repo functions. Using `../_shared/` fails to bundle ("Module not found"). Confirmed by deploy-fail-then-success this session.

**Data/constraint facts confirmed Session 104:** (1) `newsletter_subscribers.email` has a UNIQUE constraint — in-product opt-in must upsert-by-email, not insert. (2) `newsletter_articles_scheduled_consistency` CHECK = `((status='scheduled' AND scheduled_for IS NOT NULL AND scheduled_for>now()) OR status<>'scheduled')`; a scheduled article whose time has passed sits valid (CHECK is write-time only) and the publish UPDATE passes because status leaves 'scheduled'. Can't directly force a past scheduled_for while status='scheduled' (test-harness gotcha). (3) `super_admin_audit_log` is immutable — a trigger blocks UPDATE/DELETE; one test audit row from G8c verification remains and cannot be removed (harmless, accurate). (4) `_sync_to_resend_audience_internal(p_subscriber_id uuid, p_action text)`. (5) Verified Resend sender domain `noreply@mail.brainwiseenterprises.com`; newsletter uses `newsletter@mail.brainwiseenterprises.com` on the same verified domain. No standing rules through §151 modified; all referenced and held.*

*v105 - Session 103 CLOSE — PTP PDF export rebuild finalized + PTP narrative-status reconciliation + super-admin coachee report-access feature. No new §-numbered standing rules; the additions below are narrative architecture records. **NEW RLS policy `assessment_responses: super admin can read all`** — `FOR SELECT TO authenticated USING (current_user_account_type() = 'brainwise_super_admin')`. This was the last of the four report-source tables lacking a super-admin read policy (`assessment_results`, `assessments`, `facet_interpretations` already had the identical pattern). `assessment_responses` is read by the charts, the Assessment Responses accordion in `PTPNarrativeSections`, and `MyResults` itself; without this policy the super-admin coachee report rendered with silently-empty per-item sections. RLS policies for the same command are OR-combined, so adding a super-admin SELECT disjunct cannot restrict any existing access — user self-read, practitioner-coach client-read, and `service_role` full-access (used by `calculate-scores` and the generation Edge Functions) all evaluate their own policies unchanged. Verified post-apply via `pg_policies` and a live read confirming 89 response rows per completed coach PTP. **NEW super-admin feature: coachee PTP report access.** `src/pages/super-admin/CoachReport.tsx` is a thin two-level page reachable at `/super-admin/coach-report/:coachUserId` (wrapped `RoleGuard[brainwise_super_admin]` + `SuperAdminSessionProvider`, identical to every other `/super-admin/*` route). Level 1 lists the coach's own completed PTP results via a direct `assessment_results` query by `user_id` (NOT through `coach_clients` — the coach is the report subject, not a coaching client), reusing the paired-professional+personal collapse algorithm that already exists in ClientResults' direct-by-user_id branch (mutual `paired_assessment_id` collapse keyed on the professional row). Level 2 renders `MyResults` with `isCoachView adminView targetUserId=<coach> preSelectedAssessmentId=<id> coachUserId=<super admin> permissionLevel="full_results"`, deliberately skipping the `resolvePermission` resolver (`coach_clients`/`permissions` lookups) that `CoachResultsView` runs, because super admin reads everything via RLS. Entry point is a "View PTP Report" button in `CoachManagement.tsx` Active Coaches Actions cell, shown when `coach.certifications.some(c => c.certification_type==='ptp_coach' && (c.status==='in_progress'||c.status==='certified'))`; added inside a wrapper `<div className="flex gap-2">` so the existing `<TableCell>` line and the existing "Mark Certified" button stayed byte-for-byte unmodified. **NEW `MyResults` prop `adminView?: boolean` (default false).** `MyResults`'s coach-view share filter (`if (isCoachView && coachUserId && shareWithCoach === false)`) assumes any coach view is a coach-views-their-client situation governed by `share_results_with_coach` and `coach_clients` membership. Certification coaches took the PTP as trainees: `share_results_with_coach=false` and zero `coach_clients` rows, so the filter emptied the list and the report flashed then collapsed to "No completed assessments found." `adminView` guards that filter (`!adminView`) and the `setShareWithCoach` fetch line so the super-admin debrief view bypasses the share gate, mirroring how the debrief gate (`if (!isCoachView ...)` populating `debriefPendingIds` from `coach_clients_client_view.results_released`) is already bypassed in coach views. The `clientName` fetch is preserved so the header name shows. There are exactly FOUR `MyResults` call sites (App.tsx my-results owner, SharedResults.tsx peer share, ClientResults.tsx coach→client, CoachReport.tsx); only CoachReport passes `adminView`, so default-false guarantees no behavioral change at the other three BY CONSTRUCTION. Both the share filter and the debrief gate are frontend-only presentational gates, not security boundaries — the owner can read their own `assessment_results`/responses via RLS regardless; the "pending debrief" card is a UI courtesy. **NEW read-time reconciliation in `usePtpNarrativeStatus` (`MyResults.tsx`).** The hook polls `narrative_status` and gates the report render. It now also selects `ai_narrative` + `facet_insights_all_total` and reads the `facet_insights_all` row's `facet_data` array length, then treats the row as `ready` whenever `ai_narrative` is non-empty AND the facet array is present and `>= facet_insights_all_total` — regardless of the raw flag. The reconciliation only ever flips TOWARD ready (it cannot hide a row that renders today); the `generating`/`pending` spinner path is preserved when `ai_narrative` is genuinely absent. This is the read-side fix for the server-side fan-out status bug (see build-queue v111). **Data-model facts confirmed Session 103:** (1) PTP `both` is stored as a single `assessment_result` row with `context_type='both'` and `paired_assessment_id=null` (the certification cohort's rows); the report renders personal/professional/combined tabs from that one row. Split-pair PTPs (separate professional + personal rows) reference each other via `paired_assessment_id` and are collapsed in list views. `CoachReport` handles both via the reused collapse logic. (2) `facet_insights_all` is ONE `facet_interpretations` row whose `facet_data` is a JSONB array of 89 elements — NOT 89 rows (a count query maxes at 1 and was the cause of a first-pass reconciliation predicate bug). (3) Per-context narrative sections (`profile_overview_${ctx}`, `personal_summary_${ctx}`, `dimension_highlights_${ctx}`, `cross_and_action_${ctx}`, `facet_insights_${ctx}`) generate LAZILY on first view; the `calculate-scores` pre-warm fan-out was meant to create them at completion but is failing cohort-wide (build-queue BQ-FANOUT-COLDFAIL). (4) `narrative_status` is written ONLY server-side: `calculate-scores` inserts `'generating'`, then the fan-out wrapper writes `'ready'`/`'failed'` from `failures.length`; `generate-report` and `generate-all-facets` write the narrative and the 89-facet array on separate fire-and-forget paths; `retry-ptp-narratives` only NULLs the status. There are zero frontend writes to `narrative_status`. **Impersonation cleanup pattern (record):** to clear a stuck `impersonation_sessions` row, set `ended_at=now()` and `end_reason` to one of the CHECK-whitelisted values `manual | timeout | forced` (the normal exit-impersonation flow uses `manual`). The server-side clear frees a new session immediately; the browser tab may need a refresh to drop client-held impersonation state. **PTP PDF generator (`src/lib/generateResultsPdf.ts`) final state:** section headers protected by universal keep-with-next in `sectionHeading` (default reserve `MIN_BLOCK_SPACE`=30mm) plus a reduced `renderFacetScoreTable` reservation (`Math.min(facets.length,3)*7`); `renderFacetBarChart` fits charts to the ~234mm available page height with balanced multi-page splitting for high bar counts (`barsPerPage=ceil(rowCount/nPages)`, row height clamped 3.0–7.0mm). Margins unchanged. No standing rules through §151 were modified this session; all referenced and held.*

Session 102 H5 Follow-up cycle revealed the original wording overgeneralized when characterizing the "wrapper-strict-child" composite node class as unfixable via parseHTML alone. The corrected understanding: paired-rule patterns (parent class fallback rule + child class fallback rule shipped together at priority 51) DO satisfy strict content expressions of the form `newsletterChildType+` because ProseMirror runs both rules during parse and the child matches feed the parent's content expression. The genuinely-unfixable subset is narrower: (a) exact-count content expressions without `+` quantifier (`A A`, `A A A`, `A A A A`) — examples TwoColumn/ThreeColumn/FourColumn parents — and (b) heading-first content expressions where the first child must be a heading — example StepList's `heading block*` requirement. KeyMoments uses `newsletterKeyMoment+` quantifier and should be re-evaluable under the paired-rule pattern (not yet implemented). The pattern shipped Session 102 in DomainGrid (parent: `div.domain-grid` / `section.domain-grid`; child: `div.domain-row`) and IndexRow (parent: `div.index-row`; child: `div.index-card`) with TEXT_NODE-filtered child getAttrs reading from rendered DOM text rather than `data-*` attrs. Both nodes were reversed from Cycle 2's initial skip decision after Cycle 2's secondary investigation. **9 composite nodes initially impacted by §151 (Session 102 final classification)**: REVERSED to fixable via paired-rule pattern: DomainGrid+Row (SHIPPED Follow-up), IndexRow+Card (SHIPPED Follow-up); STILL FIXABLE under paired-rule (not yet shipped): KeyMoments+Moment, Disclosure+Summary (Cycle 2 SHIPPED), Checklist+Item (Cycle 2 SHIPPED), Citations+Entry (Cycle 2 SHIPPED); GENUINELY UNFIXABLE via parseHTML alone (would need preprocessing layer in ImportHtmlModal upstream of generateJSON): TwoColumn+Pane, ThreeColumn+Pane, FourColumn+Pane, StepList+Step. ImageGallery and StatGrid documented separately as "wrapper-only with strict heterogeneous content" — different failure mode from the §151 class, also genuinely unfixable via parseHTML alone for the same content-expression-coercion reason. **§151 pattern requirements for paired-rule shipped fallback (locked Session 102)**: (a) both parent + child fallback rules at priority 51 (one above default 50 per §144); (b) parent rule canonical `data-newsletter-*` selector preserved as default-priority match; (c) child getAttrs callbacks read from visible content via TEXT_NODE filtering on `el.childNodes`, NOT from `data-*` attrs (external markup won't carry those); (d) renderHTML output unchanged — round-trip behavior unaffected; (e) class names used in fallback selectors are the most common external conventions (e.g., `div.domain-grid` and `section.domain-grid` for "either tag is reasonable"; `div[class~="footer-meta"]` and `footer.footer-meta` for "div or footer element with class"). **Cross-element parseHTML semantics example (FootnoteRef mark, Session 102 H5 Cycle 1)**: mark's parseHTML rule for `sup > a[href^="#fn-N"]` walks `el.ownerDocument.getElementById(id)` inside the getAttrs callback to read footnote_text from the corresponding footnote body element in a separate Footnotes block elsewhere in the document. This is the first H5 example of getAttrs reading from cross-element content rather than only the matched element's own attributes/text. Future mark parseHTML rules that need bidirectional cross-element data resolution should follow this precedent (mark side reads the body via ownerDocument lookup; mark id and body id remain coupled via the href fragment). **H6 v1 architectural shape (Session 103 work)**: AI co-pilot integration. *v103 - Session 101 CLOSE — Group H Cycle H4 SHIPPED (Image-only Edge Function + ImportHtmlModal client-side refactor). Two new standing rules locked: §150 (SSRF defense in HTTP-fetcher Edge Functions: redirect:"manual" with per-hop URL re-validation); §151 (parseHTML rules optimized for round-trip do NOT automatically import — verify import paths separately when shipping schema). One correction filed against Session 100's phantom-file lesson: `tipTapDocToPlainText.ts` exists at `src/components/newsletter/versions/tipTapDocToPlainText.ts` (3.4KB, two consumers). Session 100 retrospective searched tiptap/, editor/, lib/ but not versions/. New file-verification discipline: grep the entire src/ tree when verifying file existence, not just the obvious directories. **§150 SSRF defense pattern**: when an Edge Function fetches user-supplied URLs (HTML imports, OEmbed resolution, image proxying), the fetch MUST use `redirect: "manual"` and the SSRF-block check (private IPv4 ranges + IPv6 + .local mDNS + cloud metadata IPs) MUST be re-run at every redirect hop. `redirect: "follow"` is vulnerable to DNS-rebinding attacks where the initial URL resolves to a public IP that passes SSRF check, then issues a 302 to an attacker-controlled private-network IP that the runtime follows without re-checking. Pattern shipped Session 101 in import-html-images v1's `fetchWithSafeRedirects(initialUrl, signal)` helper: loop hops 0..max (5), at each hop parse URL, reject non-http(s) schemes, run SSRF block check on hostname (DNS-resolve to IPv4+IPv6, fail-closed on resolve error), then `fetch(url, {signal, redirect: "manual"})`, branch on 3xx (re-loop with Location header) or 2xx (return response) or other (return response). Old convert-html-to-tiptap v2 used implicit `redirect: "follow"` (Deno fetch default) on image src URLs — vulnerable in principle; not actively exploited because the function is super-admin-gated, but defense-in-depth gap. Future Edge Functions that fetch arbitrary external URLs (RSS/Atom polling, podcast feed enrichment, embed unfurling) MUST follow this pattern. Companion convention: prefix Error messages with FailureKind:detail (`ssrf_blocked:hostname_X`, `redirect_loop:max_5_hops_exceeded`, `scheme_rejected:protocol_ftp`) so the caller can map error->FailureKind cleanly without re-parsing message text. **§151 NEW (locked Session 101)**: parseHTML rules optimized for round-trip do NOT automatically import. When a node ships with renderHTML emitting `data-newsletter-*` attribute sentinels and parseHTML matching ONLY those sentinels, the node round-trips cleanly (BrainWise saves + reloads own content) but FAILS to import from external sources (Substack, Medium, Ghost, hand-built HTML) where those attributes are absent. Verifying schema correctness via round-trip ("does the doc reload identically?") is necessary but NOT sufficient — separately verify "does external HTML matching this node's visual pattern import as the right node type?" Pattern shipped Session 101 in H4: the architectural shift from server-side DOM walking to client-side `generateJSON` exposed that 41 of 47 node schemas across the H2 vocabulary are round-trip-only. Test article `ptp_test_article.html` (the Group H spec's canonical reference, 522 lines) imported with eyebrow + deck + lede styled correctly (those 3 nodes have class-based fallback selectors) but domain grid + index cards + callout box + pullquote + footer-meta all flattened to plain paragraphs (no class-based fallbacks; rules require data-attr sentinels). Fix shape (deferred to H5 in Session 102+): add import-fallback parseHTML rules at priority 51 (one above default 50 per §144) using generic class selectors or bare-tag matches that external sources emit. Canonical `data-newsletter-*` rule stays as the primary match; renderHTML output is unchanged. `getAttrs` callbacks in import-fallback rules must read from visible content (rendered text children) rather than `data-*` attrs since external markup won't carry those attrs. Pre-audit script `/home/claude/h4/audit_parsehtml.py` classifies every node + mark file by import-friendliness; 41 round-trip-only node schemas, 2 round-trip-only mark schemas need extension. Use as the H5 scoping input. **Pattern locked Session 101 H4 backend**: Class A Edge Functions with super-admin gate enforce auth in two layers — gateway-level (verify_jwt:true checks JWT signature + decodes; rejects malformed/expired with `UNAUTHORIZED_INVALID_JWT_FORMAT`) and function-level (auth.getClaims extracts claims; super-admin check via users.account_type lookup). Important diagnostic frame: gateway rejection responds with `{"code":"UNAUTHORIZED_*", "message":"..."}` envelope; function-level rejection responds with `{"error":"..."}` envelope. When debugging curl test results, the envelope shape tells you which layer rejected. apikey header is NOT a gateway requirement — Authorization alone (when it's a valid signed JWT) passes the gateway; the gateway only checks JWT signature + expiry, not super-admin status. Implication: super-admin-protected Edge Functions are gateway-safe against unauthenticated callers but rely on function-level body code to enforce super-admin authorization. Future Edge Function Class A deploys should test both layers explicitly in curl matrix at deploy time. **Pattern locked Session 101 H4 frontend**: when the schema's parseHTML rule matches a composite element (`figure[data-newsletter-image]`, NOT bare `<img>`), client-side import must rewrite source DOM into the expected composite shape BEFORE calling generateJSON. ImportHtmlModal's `rewriteImgsToSyntheticFigures` helper handles three cases: (a) skip if already inside a target composite (round-trip case); (b) replace enclosing non-target figure (Substack/Medium standard pattern: `<figure><img><figcaption>`); (c) replace bare img. Preserves alt + figcaption text; synthesizes data-asset-id (on success) or data-import-failed-src (on failure) attrs. Pattern generalizes to any future node whose parseHTML rule expects a composite shell — if external HTML emits the bare element without the shell, client-side import must wrap it before generateJSON sees it. **§107/§142/§144/§147 all referenced + held without exception Session 101**. Standing rules §136/§140/§143/§145/§146/§148/§149/§150 NEW/§151 NEW all current. **On the horizon Session 102**: H5 cycle (parseHTML import-fallback rule extensions across 41 round-trip-only node schemas + 2 mark schemas) — scope at session open from `/mnt/user-data/outputs/H5_AUDIT_RESULTS.txt`. Decision Session 101: full audit completed (Cole's pick C+C), cycle plan deferred to Session 102. Likely shape: one or two Lovable cycles depending on whether composite parents+children are bundled or staged. Convert-html-to-tiptap Edge Function deletion via Supabase MCP after Cole confirms ≥1 successful real-article import through new path (D6=a). Plus all carryforward items from Session 100 still pending (Poll phantom audit-row, Masthead/FooterMeta published_label, results_available firing, AIRSA facet gap, messaging subsystem, etc.).*

§150 + §151 NEW (Session 101). §150: SSRF defense in Edge Functions that fetch user-supplied URLs MUST use `redirect: "manual"` with per-hop URL re-validation. Implementation contract: wrap fetch in a helper that loops 0..max-hops, at each hop (a) parse URL via `new URL(currentUrl)`, reject non-http(s) schemes with prefixed error message like `scheme_rejected:protocol_X`, (b) run hostname check against private-IP-range allow-deny: IPv4 (10/8, 127/8, 169.254/16, 172.16-31/12, 192.168/16, 0/8), IPv6 (::1, ::, fc00::/7, fe80::/10, IPv4-mapped `::ffff:a.b.c.d` extract trailing IPv4 and re-check), `.local` mDNS suffix; DNS-resolve hostname to A + AAAA records and check each resolved IP against the private ranges; fail-closed on resolve error (treat as private); (c) `fetch(currentUrl, {signal, redirect: "manual"})`; (d) branch on response status: 3xx with Location header → resolve relative-to-absolute via `new URL(location, currentUrl)`, continue loop; 3xx without Location → throw `redirect_loop:no_location_at_hop_N`; 2xx or other → return response. Max hops 5 standard. Pattern shipped Session 101 in `import-html-images` v1's `fetchWithSafeRedirects`. Companion convention: prefixed error messages (`ssrf_blocked:hostname_X`, `redirect_loop:max_N_hops_exceeded`, `scheme_rejected:protocol_Y`) let the caller's catch block map e.message via `startsWith` to FailureKind enum values without regex or message-content parsing. Old convert-html-to-tiptap v2 had this vulnerability since it used implicit `redirect: "follow"` (Deno fetch default); not actively exploited because super-admin-gated, but represents real defense-in-depth gap that v1 of every new fetcher Edge Function MUST close. Pairs with §107 (verify_jwt:true preservation) for full auth+SSRF Edge Function ship discipline. §151: parseHTML rules optimized for round-trip do NOT automatically import. When a node's renderHTML emits `data-newsletter-*` attribute sentinels and parseHTML matches ONLY those sentinels, the node round-trips cleanly but FAILS to import from external sources where those attributes are absent. Verifying schema correctness via round-trip is necessary but NOT sufficient — separately verify import paths. Standing requirement: when shipping a new TipTap node schema in Group H or later vocabulary expansions, parseHTML should include BOTH (a) canonical `data-newsletter-*` rule for round-trip and (b) at least one import-fallback rule matching the visual class names external sources are likely to emit (or bare-tag match for native HTML elements). Import-fallback rules use priority 51 (one above default 50 per §144) so they're checked AFTER the canonical rule but before any unrelated default-priority rules. `getAttrs` in import-fallback rules reads from visible content (rendered text children) rather than `data-*` attrs since external markup won't carry those attrs. The renderHTML output is unaffected — `data-newsletter-*` sentinels still emit; round-trip behavior unchanged. Pre-audit script `/home/claude/h4/audit_parsehtml.py` classifies every existing node + mark file as round-trip-only or import-friendly; outputs at `/mnt/user-data/outputs/H5_AUDIT_RESULTS.txt`. Use as the H5 cycle scoping input + as the import-fidelity reference for future node additions. Pairs with §144 (parseHTML priority discipline) and §145 (selector specificity rules).

Discriminated-union state shape unnecessary at this scale (single useState + boolean toggle for Mode 3 sufficed). P7b RelatedArticles applies same pattern: Mode 1 by_tags / Mode 2 by_category / Mode 3 manual, with mode-specific config UI rendered conditionally below a shared 3-segment pill picker. **Pattern locked Session 99 P7a**: when an editor NodeView needs preview chrome matching reader visuals, reuse the reader CSS classes via the `.newsletter-prose` container rather than forking a parallel editor-only class system. CTA NodeView preview button calls real `.newsletter-cta--primary/secondary/ghost` classes (which inherit because `.newsletter-prose` wraps editor body). Visual parity guaranteed by construction. Subscribe Block uses different approach (disabled-look-alike static skeleton in editor, real <SubscribeForm> in reader via separate SubscribeBlockReaderNodeView wrapper) — the reader-NodeView-wrapper pattern was already established for Image and Embed nodes with provider-resolution complexity. P7b RelatedArticles inherits both: editor preview calls same RPC the reader does (resolved cards rendered identically); reader-NodeView wrapper for sourceArticleId injection via `addOptions()`. **Pattern locked Session 99 P7c**: bubble menu Mode union extension pattern for marks with editable text. Definition (P7a) and FootnoteRef (P7c) both extend the union with `{ kind: "definition" | "footnote_ref"; <attrs> }` strictly additively; no refactoring of the union to a generic shape. Empty input on Apply unsets the mark (mirrors Abbr precedent). Future marks with editable text should follow this pattern. For multi-line text inputs (FootnoteRef textarea), Cmd/Ctrl+Enter is the Apply shortcut — plain Enter would prevent newlines in multi-line content. **Pattern emerging Session 99 (not §-locked yet)**: TypeScript type-escape patterns in TipTap/Supabase integration. Two recurring escapes observed: (a) NodeViewContent `as` prop accepts only `"div"` per TipTap library types, but our composite rendering uses `<ol>` and `<span>` — `as any` cast required (CodeBlockNodeView precedent extended via Citations and AuthorBio); (b) PostgREST `Json` return type from supabase.rpc() requires `as unknown as T` two-step cast to assign to a typed local interface (single-step `as T` triggers TS structural mismatch on the Json wildcard). Both patterns are recurring necessities, not code smells. Worth folding into a future §-rule covering "acceptable TypeScript type-escape patterns in this codebase" once a third instance surfaces. **Pattern locked Session 99 P7a**: <details>/<summary> native click-collapse behavior is SUPPRESSED in editor NodeView (onClick preventDefault on summary) but ALLOWED in reader path (reader doesn't mount the NodeView, so native browser behavior is preserved). The "Open/Closed by default" pill in NodeView controls is the only path to mutate default_open state in the editor. This pattern — editor NodeView intercepts a native interaction that would harm authoring UX while the reader keeps the native behavior — should generalize to other native-interactive elements (e.g., future expandable cards, slide-show navigation). **Pattern verified Session 99**: Supabase action_type CHECK constraint whitelist requires extension migration BEFORE referencing in INSERT (§142/§99 pattern). Caught mid-apply when H2-MIG-10a-1 initially INSERTed with category='newsletter_management'; CHECK constraint `super_admin_action_types_category_check` rejected; re-applied with `content_authoring` which is the closest fit among existing 10 whitelisted categories (impersonation, org_management, user_management, admin_role_management, contract_management, content_authoring, platform_observability, usage_management, mfa_management, audit_reporting). Newsletter category management semantically fits under content_authoring — no schema change required, no extension migration. Session 99 backend mid-apply pattern observed twice: (1) set_user_avatar INSERTed into wrong audit log table name on first draft (super_admin_action_log doesn't exist; actual is super_admin_audit_log) — root cause: drafted from memory rather than pulling update_user_bio body via pg_get_functiondef first; (2) newsletter_management category violated whitelist. Both caught and fixed in-session. Lesson reinforced: when drafting an RPC meant to mirror an existing one, pg_get_functiondef the existing body BEFORE drafting. Diagnosis-before-prescription applies to SQL RPCs the same way it applies to TypeScript code. **End of Session 99.* 

§136 + §142 + §147 CORRECTIONS (Session 99): §136 column count is now 8, not 7 — content_asset_refs has nullable parent FK columns: content_item_id, lesson_block_id, module_id, curriculum_id, certification_path_id, resource_id, newsletter_article_id, and the NEW user_id (added H2-MIG-9b for avatar uploads). The standing rule §136 itself is unchanged in spirit; only the column count is corrected to 8. Future content_asset_refs additions still require updating column + Sweep 2 enumeration + cascade function in same migration. §142 column-list correction: the boolean columns on super_admin_action_types are NOT requires_reason / requires_target / is_destructive / surfaces_in_recent_actions as §142 originally documented. The actual columns are requires_mfa (boolean), requires_justification (boolean), is_mutation (boolean), and denylist_during_impersonation (boolean). Confirmed via Session 99 query of an existing row (user_avatar_set) before drafting H2-MIG-10a-1. The §142 rule (always query information_schema.columns before INSERT, and the CHECK constraint on category requires migration to extend) remains valid; only the boolean column names are corrected. The shipped pattern Session 99: mirror an existing row's column values verbatim via `SELECT * FROM super_admin_action_types WHERE action_type = '<existing>'` before drafting the INSERT for the new one. §147 (NEW, locked Session 99): SQL RPC signature changes require Edge Function audit. When a SQL RPC's signature changes (new param, removed param, renamed param), every Edge Function that calls it via `.rpc(name, {...})` must be audited and redeployed. Edge Functions hardcode the param object passed to `.rpc()` — they don't pick up signature changes from SQL. Pattern observed twice: Session 95 Bug 1 (convert-html-to-tiptap v1→v2 dropped p_reason after finalize_asset_upload signature changed) and Session 99 v5→v6 deploy (request-asset-upload v5 didn't forward p_user_id after H2-MIG-9c added the param to request_asset_upload). Diagnose-before-prescribe protocol expands to: after every SQL RPC signature change, run `list_edge_functions` and check each function's source via `get_edge_function` for `.rpc('<rpc_name>'` to find callers. Audit BEFORE applying the SQL migration ideally; or immediately after as a follow-up migration / Edge Function deploy. Pairs with §107 (verify_jwt:true preservation on Edge Function redeploy) and §140 (triple-grant pattern on DROP+CREATE).

*v99 - Session 96-97 CLOSE — Group H Cycle H2 Backend SHIPPED (7 migrations + types regen + end-to-end smoke test against fresh smoke article + poll lifecycle + bio set/clear roundtrip) + Group H Cycle H2 Frontend Pass 1 + Pass 4 SHIPPED across three Lovable cycles (Bundle A1a + A1b-1 + A1b-2, all type-check clean, Cole runtime-verified end of Session 97). Six new §-numbered standing rules locked Sessions 96-97 (§140-§145) covering Supabase function-grant defaults on DROP+CREATE, Postgres CHECK constraint subquery prohibition, super_admin_action_types insert schema discipline, atom-node-plus-NodeView shipping discipline, parseHTML priority for selector collisions, and utility-class selectors banned from parseHTML. Standing rules §61-§139 unchanged. §136 staleness correction surfaced: `content_asset_refs` has 7 nullable parent FK columns, not 8 — `podcast_episode_id` does not exist (G7 podcast scope closed Session 94 per Session 91 Anchor RSS pull architecture). Sessions 96 + 97 happened in one continuous chat per Cole's preference to push through after backend smoke-tested clean; next session number is 98.

§136 CORRECTION (Sessions 96-97): The §136 entry as originally written enumerates 8 nullable parent FK columns on `content_asset_refs` including `podcast_episode_id`. That column was never added. The actual table has 7 nullable parent FK columns: `content_item_id`, `lesson_block_id`, `module_id`, `curriculum_id`, `certification_path_id`, `resource_id`, `newsletter_article_id`. The G7 podcast platform scope (which would have introduced the 8th column) was formally closed in Session 94 per §G7-close documented in v97 ship narrative — the Anchor RSS pull architecture replaces DB-side podcast authoring. The standing rule §136 (orphan-sweep parent enumeration discipline) remains valid; only the parent-column count is corrected to 7. Future arch-ref edits to §136 itself should update the column list.

§140 — Supabase default `EXECUTE TO PUBLIC` re-applies on DROP+CREATE. When recreating an RPC with a changed signature (e.g., adding parameters), the DROP-then-CREATE pattern (vs CREATE OR REPLACE) re-runs Supabase's default privileges, which include `GRANT EXECUTE ON FUNCTION ... TO PUBLIC` for new functions in the `public` schema. Consequence: `REVOKE EXECUTE FROM anon` on the new function is insufficient — the PUBLIC pseudo-role still holds EXECUTE, and PostgREST exposes the function as anon-callable through that grant. Discovered during Session 96 H2-MIG-2 when `upsert_article` was DROP+CREATEd to expand from 17 to 25 parameters; the existing `REVOKE FROM anon` migration was carried over but PUBLIC retained EXECUTE post-recreation. Complete defensive pattern locked: `REVOKE EXECUTE ON FUNCTION public.<fn>(...) FROM PUBLIC;` first, then `REVOKE EXECUTE ON FUNCTION public.<fn>(...) FROM anon;`, then `GRANT EXECUTE ON FUNCTION public.<fn>(...) TO authenticated, service_role;`. The triple-statement REVOKE PUBLIC + REVOKE anon + explicit GRANT is the safe habit on every RPC create-or-replace migration, even when using CREATE OR REPLACE (which preserves prior grant state and would not strictly require it) — defensive re-application avoids drift if the function ever gets DROP+CREATEd later. Verified via `has_function_privilege('anon', 'public.<fn>(args...)', 'EXECUTE')` returning false post-migration. Pairs with §137 (Supabase default-grants trap on function creation) — §137 covers the initial-create case, §140 covers the DROP+CREATE-on-existing-function case where the trap re-arms.

§141 — Postgres CHECK constraints cannot contain subqueries. This includes `EXISTS (SELECT ...)`, scalar subqueries, and even subqueries against built-in functions like `unnest()` when wrapped in EXISTS. Postgres raises `0A000: cannot use subquery in check constraint` at constraint creation time. Per-element validation of array or jsonb fields — e.g., "every tag in `tags text[]` is ≤32 chars," "every jsonb option in `poll.options` has a non-empty `value` field" — must live in RPC body validation (raise exception on bad input before INSERT/UPDATE) rather than as a CHECK constraint. Discovered during Session 96 H2-MIG-1 attempting to add `CHECK (NOT EXISTS (SELECT 1 FROM unnest(tags) AS t WHERE length(t) > 32))` to the `newsletter_articles` table. The constraint was dropped; the validation moved to the `upsert_article` RPC body which raises `22023 invalid_parameter_value` with a clear message on overlong tags. Standing rule: array/jsonb per-element validation belongs in RPC bodies, not CHECK. Scalar-shape validation (e.g., `CHECK (status IN ('draft', ...))`, `CHECK (length(title) BETWEEN 1 AND 200)`) remains the correct CHECK use case. Pairs with §129 (search_path discipline) — both describe Postgres-specific gotchas that aren't obvious from MCP tool output alone.

§142 — `super_admin_action_types` INSERT schema discipline. The `super_admin_action_types` registry table has 9 columns with NOT NULL constraints on 3 of them: `action_type` (text PK), `category` (text NOT NULL with whitelist CHECK in: impersonation, org_management, user_management, admin_role_management, contract_management, content_authoring, platform_observability, usage_management, mfa_management, audit_reporting), `description` (text NOT NULL). Plus `tier` (text nullable) and 4 boolean columns with sensible defaults: `requires_reason`, `requires_target`, `is_destructive`, `surfaces_in_recent_actions`. Discovered during Session 96 H2-MIG-6 when the initial INSERT for the new `user_bio_updated` action_type omitted `description` (which was not surfaced by the Session 92 inventory and not visible in `pg_proc` recon since `super_admin_action_types` is a regular table not a function). Apply failed with `23502: null value in column "description"`. Re-applied with description added. Standing rule: always query `information_schema.columns WHERE table_name = 'super_admin_action_types'` before drafting any INSERT migration against this table. The CHECK constraint on `category` is itself a whitelist that requires migration to extend if a new category is ever needed — that constraint is named `super_admin_action_types_category_check` and must be DROPped + recreated with the extended whitelist (pairs with §99 whitelist update discipline). Pairs with §131 (recon-before-INSERT discipline generalizes).

§143 — Atom node + editable attrs MUST ship with a React NodeView in the same Lovable cycle. TipTap atom nodes (`atom: true`, no `content`) whose attributes are not editable through inline content (e.g., SectionRule's `number`, Byline's `entries[]`, Masthead's labels/glyph) require a React NodeView to surface edit affordances — without a NodeView, slash-inserting the atom produces a visibly-rendered placeholder with default-empty attrs and no UI to set them. Shipping atoms-without-NodeViews creates dead UX: author inserts a SectionRule, sees a generic divider, has no way to specify "01" as the number or "plain" vs "numbered" style. Standing rule: when a Lovable cycle adds an atom node with editable attrs, the cycle MUST also ship the matching React NodeView in the same change. If the cycle scope is too large to bundle both (e.g., bubble menu refactor + atom NodeView + 3 other nodes all in one cycle), the cycle should split — defer the atom node and its NodeView to a follow-up cycle together rather than ship the node alone. Pattern proven across Bundle A1a → A1b-1 → A1b-2: Bundle A1a deferred SectionRule + Masthead + Byline specifically because their NodeViews wouldn't fit; Bundle A1b-1 shipped SectionRule + Masthead + their NodeViews together; Bundle A1b-2 shipped Byline + its 220-LOC NodeView (split into 3 same-file subcomponents) together. Pairs with §139 (TipTap setContent imperative API) — both describe TipTap-specific design discipline where the React layer must explicitly model concerns the schema layer can't.

§144 — parseHTML rule priority for selector collisions across nodes/marks. Multiple TipTap extensions registered via `buildExtensions` can claim overlapping selectors (e.g., bare `aside`, bare `mark`, bare `hr`). When two rules could match the same DOM element, ProseMirror's parseDOM evaluation order is determined by the explicit `priority` field on each rule (default 50; higher wins). To force a more-specific rule to beat a more-generic one for shared root tags, set `priority: 51` (or higher) on the specific rule and leave the generic rule at default. Three patterns locked in Sessions 96-97: (a) Callout's `aside[data-newsletter-callout]` rule got `priority: 51` to win over Aside's `aside:not([data-newsletter-callout])` rule (priority 50) — belt-and-suspenders since Aside's `:not()` exclusion already prevents the collision, but the priority ensures deterministic behavior even if a future change loosens Aside's selector. (b) Accent's `mark.accent` rule got `priority: 60` to win over Highlight's bare `mark` rule (priority 50) — though Highlight was further scoped to `mark[data-newsletter-highlight]` to avoid the collision entirely, the priority provides redundant safety. (c) SectionRule's `hr.section-rule`, `hr[data-numbered]`, `hr.dot-divider` rules all got `priority: 60` to win over StarterKit HorizontalRule's bare `hr` rule (priority 50); critically, SectionRule does NOT register a bare `hr` selector — bare `<hr>` continues to fall through to HorizontalRule unaffected. Standing rule: when a new node's root tag is shared with another existing node, scope the new node's selector to a data-attr or specific class AND set explicit `priority: 51-60` on the more-specific node's rules for that root tag. Avoid registering bare root tags that StarterKit or other extensions already claim. Pairs with §145 (utility-class selectors banned) — both protect parseHTML rule integrity at the HTML-import boundary.

§145 — Utility-class selectors are forbidden in parseHTML. Selectors like `[class~="underline"]`, `[class~="bold"]`, `[class~="italic"]`, `[class~="inline"]`, `[class~="block"]`, `[class~="hidden"]`, `[class~="flex"]`, `[class~="grid"]` will match any HTML using Tailwind, Bootstrap, or similar utility-CSS frameworks regardless of authorial intent. A pasted HTML snippet containing `<p class="text-center underline mt-4">Lorem ipsum</p>` would incorrectly apply BrainWise's `newsletterUnderline` mark to the entire paragraph because of the Tailwind `underline` utility class. Discovered during Bundle A1a recon when the initial Underline mark parseHTML rule included `[class~="underline"]`. Removed; Underline now matches only `u`, `[style*="text-decoration:underline"]`, `[data-newsletter-underline]`. Standing rule: valid selector families for parseHTML are (a) BrainWise `data-newsletter-X` attribute selectors, (b) semantic HTML tags that aren't claimed by utility frameworks (`aside`, `kbd`, `sup`, `sub`, `mark`, `abbr`, `address`, `figure`, `figcaption`, `blockquote`), (c) BrainWise-specific compound class names that don't collide with utility vocabularies (`newsletter-callout`, `small-caps`, `byline`, `author-meta`, `eyebrow`, `kicker`, `category`, `lede`, `deck`, `standfirst`). Explicitly excluded class-name selectors (utility-framework collision risk): `underline`, `bold`, `italic`, `inline`, `block`, `hidden`, `flex`, `grid`, `text-center`, `text-left`, `text-right`, `text-uppercase`, `text-lowercase`, `font-bold`, `font-italic`, `text-sm`, `text-lg`, `text-xl`, `mt-X`, `mb-X`, `p-X`, `m-X`, any single-word styling vocabulary that appears in Tailwind/Bootstrap class libraries. The cost of including such a selector is silently-incorrect imports on every external HTML source; the benefit (catching the rare case where someone literally types `class="underline"` to mean BrainWise's underline mark) is negligible. Pairs with §144 (parseHTML priority).

§146 — Newsletter TipTap schema module is headless; React NodeViews wired in NewsletterEditor.tsx via EDITABLE_NODE_OVERRIDES, NOT in tiptap/nodes/. The `src/components/newsletter/tiptap/` module is consumed by three callers: (a) the editor (`editable: true`, full React NodeView surfaces), (b) the G6 read-only public reader (`editable: false`, no NodeViews), (c) the `convert_html_to_tiptap` Edge Function (Deno server-side via JSDOM, no React runtime). Callers (b) and (c) cannot tolerate React imports in the schema module — Edge Function runs in Deno without a DOM context for React reconciliation; reader bundles into the public-facing route where pulling unnecessary React tree weight inflates the initial paint. Pattern: `Node.create()` in `tiptap/nodes/` stays headless (no `addNodeView()` field on the spec). For any node needing a React NodeView, define a `.extend({ addNodeView() { return ReactNodeViewRenderer(View); } })` wrapper in `NewsletterEditor.tsx` as a Node*Edit constant (e.g., `NodeChecklistItemEdit = NewsletterChecklistItem.extend({ ... })`), and add the constant to the `EDITABLE_NODE_OVERRIDES` array. The editor's `useMemo` over extensions then swaps each base node for its wrapped equivalent by name (OVERRIDE_NAMES Set membership check). Pattern documented inline in NewsletterEditor.tsx header comment (lines 20-23 as of Session 98). Never put `addNodeView()` directly on a Node.create() definition in `tiptap/nodes/`. Discovered Session 98 during Bundle A2a-1 plan review when the initial build prompt for ChecklistItemNodeView wired `addNodeView()` on the headless NewsletterChecklistItem definition; corrected before any code shipped. Pattern was implicit in NewsletterEditor.tsx header comment but not yet §-numbered, so the same mistake had been worked around individually in prior cycles rather than locked as policy. Pairs with §143 (atom + NodeView ship discipline) — §143 dictates timing (same Lovable cycle), §146 dictates wiring location (editor module, not schema module). Applies to ALL future NodeView additions in the newsletter editor: A2a-1 (ChecklistItemNodeView), A2a-2 (DomainRowNodeView, IndexCardNodeView), A3b (CodeBlockNodeView via Option-W2 — extending StarterKit-bundled node by name), A5a (MathNodeView, TerminalNodeView, CodeDiffNodeView, ChartNodeView), A5c (AudioNodeView), A5d (ImageCompareNodeView) — all 10 new NodeView wirings in Session 98 followed this pattern.

§147 — SQL RPC signature changes require Edge Function audit. When a SQL RPC's signature changes (new param added, param removed, param renamed), every Edge Function that calls it via `.rpc(name, {...})` must be audited and redeployed. Edge Functions hardcode the param object passed to `.rpc()` — they don't pick up signature changes from SQL. Pattern observed twice: Session 95 Bug 1 (convert-html-to-tiptap v1→v2 dropped p_reason after finalize_asset_upload signature changed) and Session 99 v5→v6 deploy (request-asset-upload v5 didn't forward p_user_id after H2-MIG-9c added the param to request_asset_upload). Diagnose-before-prescribe protocol expands to: after every SQL RPC signature change, run `list_edge_functions` and check each function's source via `get_edge_function` for `.rpc('<rpc_name>'` to find callers. Audit BEFORE applying the SQL migration ideally; or immediately after as a follow-up migration / Edge Function deploy. Pairs with §107 (verify_jwt:true preservation on Edge Function redeploy) and §140 (triple-grant pattern on DROP+CREATE).

§148 — Bounded-suppression auto-render for article-level fields. When article-level scalar fields (eyebrow text, masthead publication, footer metadata flags, etc.) drive the rendering of synthetic TipTap nodes at reader time, the synthetic-node injection must inspect only a bounded window of the existing doc content — typically first N nodes for prepend candidates, last N nodes for append candidates — rather than scanning the entire document. Full-document scan would block legitimate mid-article use of the same node type (e.g., an author manually inserting `newsletterEyebrow` as a section kicker should not suppress the article-level eyebrow auto-prepend). Pattern locked Session 100 H3-NV-Auto: bounded suppression with N=2. Code shape: `const first2 = content.slice(0, 2).map(n => n.type); if (article.<field> && !first2.includes('<targetType>')) { toPrepend.push(...) }`. Same N applies to append checks against `content.slice(-2)`. The bound N is the smallest window that catches "author already put this at the top/bottom"; increasing N risks blocking legitimate mid-doc use. Synthesized nodes are constructed every render (no stable IDs needed — they're derived from article fields, not authored content). Auto-render is reader-only by default; editor preview path should NOT inject synthetic nodes since the author is the one filling the source fields and seeing them twice (in sidebar + injected in editor body) is confusing. Pairs with §143 (atom + NodeView ship discipline; auto-rendered atoms still use their normal NodeView in the reader path).

§149 — DB-row-as-source-of-truth pattern for TipTap atoms. Some atom nodes serialize only a foreign key in their TipTap attrs; the durable content lives in a dedicated DB table row identified by that FK. Poll is the precedent (Session 100 H2-FE-Pass 8): `NewsletterPoll` atom has a single attr `poll_id: string | null`; the row in `newsletter_polls` (created via `create_poll` RPC, updated via `update_poll`, read via `get_poll_results`) holds question/options/style/votes_visible/is_locked. Doc serializes only `poll_id`. Pattern indications: (a) the content is mutable independently of the article body (votes accumulate without doc changes), or (b) the content participates in cross-doc DB queries (admin "polls created by user X" listing requires a joinable table not embedded JSON in body_tiptap), or (c) the content has lifecycle semantics distinct from the article (poll archive separate from article archive). When using this pattern: (1) atom node spec has minimal attrs (FK + optional cache hints); (2) NodeView for editing splits Path A (poll_id null, render Create flow that calls the create RPC then writeBack via `updateAttributes({poll_id})`) and Path B (poll_id set, hydrate via direct table read since RPC may gate on published status that draft articles fail); (3) reader NodeView calls the canonical read RPC and renders from it; (4) RLS policies on the DB table must permit super-admin direct-table-read (editor authors are always super-admin) in addition to the public read RPC gate; (5) cascade-delete from article archive to row archive needs explicit RPC or trigger logic — atom delete from doc does NOT auto-archive the row. Tradeoffs vs attrs-embed: this pattern adds RPC roundtrips on every render but enables features (cross-article querying, lifecycle independence, large-content fields, vote/comment systems) that pure-attrs embedding cannot support. Pairs with §146 (NodeView wiring location) and §143 (atom + NodeView ship discipline).


*v98 - Session 95 CLOSE — Group G newsletter platform shipped end-to-end (G4-0 through G4-C + G5 + G6). Two real bugs surfaced during end-to-end test and FIXED in-session (Edge Function v1→v2 for finalize_asset_upload p_reason; forwardRef + useImperativeHandle pattern for TipTap content replacement). Four new §-numbered standing rules locked Session 95 (§136-§139). Standing rules §61-§135 unchanged. Group H — Newsletter visual vocabulary + layout-preserving HTML import — NEW initiative scoped + spec'd; Cycle H1 complete, H2-H6 remaining. Spec document `group-h-spec.md` (430 lines) referenced as authoritative source for Sessions 96-100.

§136 — Orphan-sweep parent enumeration discipline. The `reap_pending_uploads()` SECURITY DEFINER function performs three sweeps to identify orphaned `content_assets` rows: Sweep 1 finds assets with `status='pending'` older than 24h with no `content_asset_refs` row at all (never finalized); Sweep 2 finds assets where every `content_asset_refs` row points to a parent that no longer exists (parent cascade-deleted but ref row survived). Sweep 2 enumerates parents by joining `content_asset_refs` against every parent table — currently 8 nullable FK columns (content_item_id, lesson_block_id, module_id, curriculum_id, certification_path_id, resource_id, newsletter_article_id, podcast_episode_id). When a new parent type is added to `content_asset_refs` via ALTER TABLE ADD COLUMN, three things must update in the same migration: (a) the column itself, (b) Sweep 2's parent enumeration LEFT JOIN list (otherwise orphan-sweep misses the new parent type silently), (c) the cascade-delete function that recursively archives child assets when the parent is archived. Session 95 caught this during G4-B verification — Sweep 2 had been written without `newsletter_article_id` and `resource_id`, so orphaned newsletter image refs would have leaked. Fix migration `session95_reap_pending_uploads_parent_enumeration_fix` added both. Standing rule: any future content_asset_refs schema addition MUST update all three of (column, Sweep 2 enumeration, cascade function) in the SAME migration. Pairs with §99 (whitelist update discipline) and §71 (cascade archive contract).

§137 — Supabase default-grants trap on function creation. Postgres default privileges in Supabase's public schema include automatic EXECUTE grants to both `anon` and `authenticated` roles when ANY function is created. This is set via `ALTER DEFAULT PRIVILEGES` at database initialization time by Supabase tooling. Consequence: `REVOKE EXECUTE FROM PUBLIC` on a newly-created function is a NO-OP against role-specific default grants — anon and authenticated still hold EXECUTE because the grants came from default privileges, not from the PUBLIC pseudo-role. For super-admin-only RPCs (or any RPC where anon must be locked out), the migration MUST include explicit `REVOKE EXECUTE ON FUNCTION public.<fn>(...) FROM anon;` AFTER `CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION`, regardless of whether the function body contains `assert_super_admin()` or other internal gates. Discovered Session 95 during G4-B `list_admin_newsletter_articles` RPC — initial migration created the function with `assert_super_admin()` inside and explicit `GRANT EXECUTE TO authenticated`, but anon retained EXECUTE due to default-privilege trap. PostgREST then exposed the RPC to unauthenticated callers; only `assert_super_admin()` inside prevented data leakage but the exposed endpoint surface was wider than intended. Fix migration `session95_list_admin_newsletter_articles_revoke_anon` added the explicit REVOKE. Standing rule: every new function in public schema that should NOT be anon-callable MUST include explicit `REVOKE EXECUTE ON FUNCTION public.<fn>(...) FROM anon;` after creation. The double-defense (REVOKE + internal assert) is intentional — REVOKE shrinks the attack surface, assert_super_admin catches authenticated-but-not-super-admin callers. Pairs with §82 (explicit-grant discipline).

§138 — publish_article and schedule_article auto-snapshot landmark pattern. State transitions on newsletter articles that fundamentally change visibility (publish, schedule) should create discoverable landmarks in the version history. Pattern: after the UPDATE that transitions article status, call `_snapshot_article_version(p_article_id, p_version_type, p_version_name, p_reason)` with version_name following the convention `'{Type} v{N}'` where N is the count of prior versions of that same version_type plus one. Concrete: `publish_article` creates `'Published v1'`, `'Published v2'`, etc. as the article is published and re-published; `schedule_article` creates `'Scheduled v1'`, `'Scheduled v2'`, etc. Frontend version history sheet (G5) renders these as visually-distinguished landmark entries (orange badge for Published, teal badge for Scheduled, distinct from auto-save "Draft" badges and manual "Snapshot" badges). Rationale: when authors want to roll back to "the version that went out last week," they can find it by name; when they want to recover their pre-publish draft state, the auto-snapshot is the canonical rollback point. Locked Session 95 via migration `session95_publish_schedule_auto_snapshot_versions`. Standing rule: any future state transition that changes article visibility (e.g., if/when "republish to subscribers" becomes a separate action) should follow the same pattern — auto-snapshot named `{Type} v{N}`, increment N based on existing version count of that type. Pairs with §99 (action_type whitelist) and §130 (audit-row labeling).

§139 — forwardRef + useImperativeHandle pattern for TipTap content replacement. TipTap's `useEditor` React hook accepts `content` (and `initialContent`) only on first mount. Subsequent prop changes are silently ignored — the editor's internal ProseMirror state is not reactive to React prop updates. This is intentional in TipTap's design (the editor owns its state, React reads from it via `onUpdate`) but creates a problem when external operations need to replace the entire document (HTML import, restore-from-version, paste-from-template, etc.). The escape hatch is `editor.commands.setContent(next, { emitUpdate: true })` — imperative API that mutates the editor's document AND emits an update event so `onUpdate` fires and React state stays synchronized. To expose this imperative API across component boundaries: convert the editor component from a regular functional component to `forwardRef`, define an interface (e.g., `NewsletterEditorHandle`) with the methods to expose, and use `useImperativeHandle` to bind them to the ref. Parent components store a `useRef<NewsletterEditorHandle | null>(null)`, pass it via `ref` prop, and call methods like `editorHandleRef.current?.setContent(newBody)` to trigger replacement. The `emitUpdate: true` is critical — without it, `onUpdate` doesn't fire and React state diverges from editor state. Locked Session 95 via Bug 2 fix on NewsletterEditor + AdminNewsletterArticle. Standing rule: any future component that wraps a TipTap editor and needs to support external content replacement MUST use this forwardRef + useImperativeHandle pattern; do NOT attempt to make TipTap reactive to prop changes (will appear to work briefly during mount but break on subsequent re-renders). Pairs with §111 (RPC wrapper-shape discipline) as both describe contract-shape gotchas that compile-clean but fail at runtime.

Six migrations applied + verified Session 94, two Edge Functions touched (`sync-resend-audience` v1 NEW + ACTIVE; `resend-webhook` v2→v3 strictly-additive bounce/complaint subscriber-status sync). All §129 + §130 + §131 + §132 + §134 discipline held across every applied migration. Zero gaps found post-ship across G2.1–G2.4b. Twenty-eight Q-decisions locked Session 94 (Q7.A/B/C, Q8, Q9, Q11.A, Q12.A, Q13.A, Q14.A, Q15, Q16, Q17, Q19, Q20.α, Q22, Q25.A, Q27.A, Q28.B); two reopened and resolved differently during scoping (Q22 about audience_id storage made moot by Resend's Nov 2025 contacts overhaul discovery; Q14 rewrite from UPDATE→DELETE on abandoned-pending expiry to free email for re-subscribe).

§135 — Vault secrets vs Edge Function Secrets: two distinct stores, two distinct access patterns. Locked Session 94 across the newsletter G2 build covering three secrets that demonstrate the two patterns. **Edge Function Secrets** (configured via Supabase Dashboard → Edge Functions → Secrets) are accessed via `Deno.env.get('SECRET_NAME')` inside the Edge Function — fast, synchronous, no DB roundtrip required; this is where secrets that the Edge Function consumes directly live (e.g., RESEND_API_KEY which send-email and sync-resend-audience read internally; INTERNAL_FUNCTION_SECRET which every Class B Edge Function reads to validate the x-internal-secret header on inbound calls). **Vault secrets** (`vault.decrypted_secrets`) are accessed via `SELECT decrypted_secret FROM vault.decrypted_secrets WHERE name = '...'` from SQL — slower, requires DB roundtrip, used by SECDEF RPCs that need to pass a secret into a pg_net.http_post body or header (e.g., the SECDEF RPC calls Cloudflare siteverify with the secret in the form body; the SECDEF RPC calls an internal Class B Edge Function with INTERNAL_FUNCTION_SECRET in the x-internal-secret header). The pattern locked Session 94: SECDEF RPC reads secret from Vault, passes to pg_net.http_post body or header, Edge Function on the other side reads the same secret from Edge Function Secrets via Deno.env.get and does constant-time safeEqual comparison to verify. **Both stores must be populated when adding a new secret used on both sides** — adding to Vault only means the SQL side reads it but the Edge Function side gets undefined and rejects the request; adding to Edge Function Secrets only means the Edge Function reads it but SECDEF RPCs that need to pass it through pg_net get NULL from Vault. Three secrets at Session 94 close exemplify the pattern: INTERNAL_FUNCTION_SECRET (both stores — used by every Class B Edge Function reading the inbound header + every SECDEF RPC that calls one); CLOUDFLARE_TURNSTILE_SECRET (Vault only — subscribe_to_newsletter RPC posts to Cloudflare siteverify with this in the form body; the Edge Function side does not consume it because the Edge Function isn't in this flow); RESEND_API_KEY (Edge Function Secrets only — send-email and sync-resend-audience Edge Functions read this internally; no SECDEF RPC needs to pass the Resend key into pg_net because SQL never calls the Resend API directly). When adding a future secret, decide first which side reads it — if both, populate both stores in the same change.
