- (1) `session94_newsletter_subscribe_attempt_pruning_function_and_cron` (20260523184616) — `prune_newsletter_subscribe_attempts()` SECDEF deletes `newsletter_subscribe_attempts` rows older than 24h. Cron `prune_newsletter_subscribe_attempts_daily` at `15 6 * * *`. Per §131 slot-collision discovery, 6:15 confirmed free pre-migration. Uses `cron.schedule()` not `cron.schedule_in_database()` because the explicit-username 6-arg variant requires superuser the MCP role lacks; `cron.schedule()` produces identical job registration with username='postgres' assigned automatically by Supabase. Ships active. Smoke test on empty production table: `{success:true, deleted_count:0, cutoff:<now-24h>, pruned_at:<now>}`.

- (2) `session94_newsletter_pending_confirmation_expiry_function_and_cron` (20260523184829) — `expire_pending_newsletter_confirmations()` SECDEF initial implementation flipped pending_confirmation rows older than 7d to status='unsubscribed' via UPDATE. Cron at `25 6 * * *`. Per §131, 6:25 confirmed free. Discovered design flaw before drafting G2.3: flipping abandoned-pending to 'unsubscribed' collides with user-initiated unsubscribe (Q7.C locks unsubscribed addresses out of re-subscription via subscribe_to_newsletter's anti-enumeration silent no-op for unsubscribed-status rows; abandoned drafts would inherit that lockout despite the user never having actively unsubscribed).

- (3) `session94_newsletter_pending_confirmation_expiry_rewrite_to_delete` (20260523185102) — Q14.A correction: rewrote function body to DELETE the abandoned-pending row entirely. Rationale: `newsletter_subscribers` represents *current* subscription state; abandoned drafts are not current state. Email is freed for a fresh subscribe attempt. Audit trail preserved in `newsletter_subscribe_attempts` (rate-limit tracking) and `email_logs` (Resend webhook events) which the cron does not touch. Smoke verified body contains DELETE not UPDATE; returns `{success:true, deleted_count:N, cutoff:<now-7d>, expired_at:<now>}`.

- (4) `session94_newsletter_subscribe_RPCs` (20260523185716) — five RPCs in one migration with cross-RPC PERFORM dependencies handled by definition order: `_send_newsletter_confirmation_email_internal(uuid, text)` (private helper, defined first; locked from anon/authenticated/PUBLIC); `subscribe_to_newsletter(text, text, text)` (anon-callable; Q13.A anti-enumeration — generic success in all failure branches); `confirm_newsletter_subscription(text)` (anon-callable; Q15 distinct success/failure — token-click already exposes oracle, so distinct responses are appropriate UX); `unsubscribe_from_newsletter(text)` (anon-callable; idempotent); `list_newsletter_subscribers(text, integer, integer)` (super_admin only via assert_super_admin gate + §111 wrapper-shape return). Locked Q-decisions: Q7.A (existing pending → rotate token + re-send), Q7.B (existing confirmed → silent no-op), Q7.C (existing unsubscribed/bounced/complained → silent no-op preserving Resend reputation), Q8 (5/hr/IP rolling rate limit), Q9 Variant 2 (warmer/branded confirmation email copy), Q11.A (Turnstile verification via pg_net polling Cloudflare siteverify — 30-iteration 100ms-sleep loop polls net._http_response, total 3s max wait, fail-closed on timeout), Q12.A (synchronous email dispatch via send-email Edge Function), Q16 (32-byte gen_random_bytes → base64url raw token in URL only; SHA-256 hex hash persists in DB), Q17 (apex `brainwiseenterprises.com` for confirmation + unsubscribe URLs), Q19 (unsubscribe link in confirmation email footer for CAN-SPAM/GDPR transactional compliance), Q20.α (unsubscribe token generated once on first send if absent; rotates on re-send accepting prior unopened email's unsub link breaks). Pgcrypto search_path on all four token-handling RPCs includes `extensions` per §129. Anti-enumeration coverage in subscribe_to_newsletter: malformed email → generic success; turnstile invalid → generic success; rate-limited IP → generic success; existing confirmed/unsubscribed/bounced/complained → generic success (no email, no DB change). Frontend cannot distinguish branches.

- (5) `session94_newsletter_rpcs_revoke_public` (20260523185749) — follow-up REVOKE of default PUBLIC grants Postgres auto-creates on new functions. Original G2.3 migration had explicit GRANTs to anon + authenticated but did not REVOKE FROM PUBLIC; tightening for §82 explicit-grant discipline. Defense-in-depth on list_newsletter_subscribers which now has authenticated-only explicit grant on top of internal assert_super_admin gate.

- (6) `session94_newsletter_resend_audience_sync` (20260523190929) — `_sync_to_resend_audience_internal(uuid, text)` SECDEF helper reads INTERNAL_FUNCTION_SECRET from Vault, validates action enum ('add' | 'remove'), posts to sync-resend-audience Edge Function via pg_net.http_post with x-internal-secret header (best-effort sub-transaction wrap; never throws to caller). Then full-body CREATE OR REPLACE of `confirm_newsletter_subscription` and `unsubscribe_from_newsletter` swapping the TODO comments for `PERFORM public._sync_to_resend_audience_internal(v_subscriber_id, 'add'|'remove')` calls. Per Q27.A: best-effort, never blocks user flow.

**Two Edge Functions touched Session 94:**

- (a) NEW `sync-resend-audience` v1 — Class B per §107, verify_jwt:false, INTERNAL_FUNCTION_SECRET gate with constant-time safeEqual. Implements Resend's Nov-2025 contacts overhaul (discovered during recon): contacts are now global to the Resend account; no audience_id required for POST/PATCH/DELETE. `action='add'` → POST `/contacts` `{email, unsubscribed:false}` (idempotent — Resend re-creates or returns existing contact_id). `action='remove'` → PATCH `/contacts/<email>` `{unsubscribed:true}` (Q25.A soft-unsubscribe — keeps Resend contact record for analytics; Resend skips unsubscribed contacts on broadcasts automatically). On successful add, writes returned Resend contact_id back to `newsletter_subscribers.resend_contact_id` via service-role supabase client (non-fatal if writeback fails). End-to-end smoke verified: full chain Vault → pg_net → Edge Function → Resend POST → response → contact_id writeback works.

- (b) UPDATED `resend-webhook` v2→v3 strictly-additive extension. Pre-modification pull via get_edge_function per Lovable Credit Conservation Protocol diagnose-before-prescribe. Every pre-existing line preserved verbatim (Svix signature verification, header presence checks, timestamp freshness rejecting >5min replays, email_logs find-or-update OR `auth_or_external` insert branch). New newsletter-status-sync block APPENDED after the existing email_logs work, before the 200 ack response: when `statusEvent IN ('bounced', 'complained')` AND recipientEmail present, looks up `newsletter_subscribers` by lowercased email, flips status to 'bounced' or 'complained' if currently 'confirmed' or 'pending_confirmation' (idempotent — won't touch already-unsubscribed/bounced/complained rows). Per Q28.B: does NOT fire `_sync_to_resend_audience_internal` since Resend originated the event and already knows. Try/catch wrapped — any failure is logged via logStep and swallowed; the 200 ack to Resend is unaffected. Post-deploy smoke confirmed pre-existing behaviors intact: forged signature → 401 `{"error":"Invalid signature"}`; missing svix headers → 400; OPTIONS preflight → 200.

**Phase G3 SEO/AEO infrastructure deferred to post-G6 combined G3+RSS pass.** Three of the four originally-scoped routing paths evaluated and rejected during Session 94:

- Path D-2 (Cloudflare Worker subdomain proxy keeping DNS in Microsoft) — initially recommended after Path C rejection; rejected after web-search recon found Cloudflare's "Partial CNAME setup" (the only way to add a Worker subdomain without nameserver migration) requires Business or Enterprise plan ($200/month minimum). Search result directly quoted Cloudflare staff: "if you don't want to change nameservers, there's also Partial (CNAME) setup, but this requires a Business or Enterprise account."

- Path D-3 (full Cloudflare nameserver migration) — rejected on same DNS-migration risk that rejected Path A originally; moving Resend email DNS records (currently on Microsoft 365 DNS for `brainwiseenterprises.com`) to Cloudflare is doable but error-prone and Cole has declined this scope twice.

Cole's call: defer the G3 routing decision until after Lovable frontend cycles G4-G6 ship and there is real article content to validate SSR against, plus actual newsletter audience signal to justify the infrastructure investment. The infrastructure decision gets made once with full context. Path D-1 ugly-URL interim was rejected because it would create URL-change debt — Lovable G6 (public reader UI) will use clean `brainwiseenterprises.com/newsletter/<slug>` URLs from day one served by the SPA (not SSR'd); when G3 ships later, the URLs stay the same and only the rendering changes from SPA to SSR. **G9 RSS feed Edge Function also deferred to the same G3+RSS combined pass** — same URL-routing problem; building with ugly Supabase URL just to defer clean URL would create throwaway work. Remaining G9 sub-components (empty states, loading skeletons, error boundaries, a11y verification, mobile verification, cover image dominant-color extraction reuse §112, cover image cascade reuse §43/§50/§108) are all Lovable frontend work — fold into G6 reader UI Lovable cycle or separate G9 polish cycle post-G6.

*v96 - Sessions 92 + 93 CLOSE — Group G newsletter platform Phase G1 backend lift FULLY SHIPPED across two sessions (10 migrations total: 5 Session 92 + 5 Session 93 + 1 fix-up). **Phase G1 is DONE.** Six new §-numbered standing rules locked (§129-§134); §129-§131 candidates from Session 92, §132-§134 from Session 93. Standing rules §61-§128 unchanged. Session 92 was a partial close (context exhausted mid-G1.3b verification, 5 of ~10 G1 migrations shipped); Session 93 closed out remaining G1.3c through G1.5. Path-B inline-image asset tracking adopted mid-Session-93 per Cole's product call (handoff originally scoped narrower "extend walker" work; recon revealed walker structurally couldn't extend, leading to Q6 Lovable approval cycle and a TipTap-walker + rebind + cascade build with full content_assets integration from day one). Zero Lovable code cycles this session pair (all backend; G2 onward will reintroduce frontend prompts).

§129 — SECDEF functions calling pgcrypto must include `extensions` in search_path. Confirmed during Session 92 G1.2: `pgcrypto` v1.3 lives in `extensions` schema in Supabase (not `public`). Pattern locked for SECDEF functions calling `digest()` or `gen_random_bytes()`: `SET search_path = public, extensions, pg_temp`. Skipping `extensions` works only if extensions is in the default search_path before SECDEF locks it — fragile to future search_path policy changes. Two precedent functions exist: `corporate_employee_choose_individual` (correct, uses extensions in path) and `peer_access_request_create` (risky, doesn't). New pattern locked for G1 onward: explicit `extensions` in search_path always when calling pgcrypto. `import_newsletter_subscribers_bulk` (G1.2, calls both `digest()` and `gen_random_bytes()`) is the first newsletter-side application.

§130 — Smoke-test audit rows are unavoidable when testing super_admin RPCs because `super_admin_audit_log` has `block_audit_log_mutations()` trigger raising P0001 on any UPDATE or DELETE. Smoke-test audit rows persist permanently. Convention adopted: prefix `p_reason` with `'G<phase>.<step> smoke test - <detail>'` for self-identification. Session 92 + Session 93 left 28 smoke-test audit rows total in production — 5 Session 92, 23 Session 93 — all correctly labeled. Auditing concern is mitigated by reason-prefix discoverability; alternative (deferring smoke until staging-branch exists) blocks shipping work. Standing query for self-audit of smoke residue: `SELECT action_type, reason, created_at FROM super_admin_audit_log WHERE reason LIKE 'G%.%X smoke test%' ORDER BY created_at;` — should return only correctly-prefixed rows, never any with mismatched session/phase tags.

§131 — pg_cron job slot collision discovery before scheduling new jobs. Existing job `process_due_scheduled_assignments_daily` at `20 6 * * *` was at risk of colliding with the originally-planned newsletter cron slots Session 92. Discovery query: `SELECT jobname, schedule, active FROM cron.job ORDER BY schedule;` before any new `cron.schedule()` call. Newsletter cron jobs rescheduled to non-colliding minutes: `prune_newsletter_subscribe_attempts` at 6:15 (G2), `expire_pending_newsletter_confirmations` at 6:25 (G2), `prune_newsletter_draft_versions` at 6:35 (G1.3e). Working sets are disjoint (no shared lock contention with assignments cron). Discipline: query `cron.job` first when adding any cron-driven feature.

§132 — Pre-migration schema/constraint recon discipline. Before drafting any migration that INSERTs/UPDATEs/calls into a table or schema object not freshly authored in the current session, query three sources: (a) `information_schema.columns` for nullability/defaults (catches NOT NULL columns omitted from INSERT), (b) `pg_constraint` for CHECK predicates including whitelists (catches new values omitted from existing whitelist constraints), (c) `pg_proc` for available function signatures (catches assumed API surface not actually present, e.g. `cron.alter_job` vs direct `UPDATE cron.job`). Session 93 alone hit three migration apply errors that were all preventable via this recon: (1) G1.3c first apply failed at INSERT into `super_admin_action_types` because `description` column is NOT NULL with no default and was omitted from INSERT — caught + corrected via re-apply with description column added; (2) G1.3e first apply failed at `UPDATE cron.job SET active = false` with `42501 permission denied` because migration role doesn't own `cron.job` table directly — corrected via switch to `cron.schedule_in_database(..., active => false)` which uses the function API (separate §134 rule for the specific cron-disable pattern); (3) G1.4 smoke test surfaced (not migration-time, but same root cause) that `_archive_asset_internal` failed with `23514 content_assets_archive_reason_check` because `'newsletter_article_archived'` was not in the 8-value archive_reason whitelist — corrected via fix-up migration adding the 9th value. All three failures cost time + transaction rollbacks that pre-migration recon would have prevented entirely. Standing query pattern for any cross-session migration: `SELECT column_name, data_type, is_nullable, column_default FROM information_schema.columns WHERE table_schema='public' AND table_name=<target>;` + `SELECT conname, pg_get_constraintdef(oid) FROM pg_constraint WHERE conrelid='public.<target>'::regclass;` + (when cron-related) `SELECT proname, pg_get_function_arguments(oid) FROM pg_proc WHERE pronamespace=(SELECT oid FROM pg_namespace WHERE nspname='cron');`. Pairs with §99 (action_type whitelist) and §96 (relax-RPC-validation requires matching CHECK-constraint audit): all three reinforce that PostgreSQL function evolution touches multiple layers atomically, and validation/signature changes must be discovered before draft, not after apply failure.

§133 — Newsletter inline image TipTap nodes MUST carry `attrs.asset_id` referencing a `content_assets` row; `src` is derived at render time, never canonical. Locks Cole's Q6.2 product decision (Session 93 G1.4) into a discoverable contract for downstream authors. Rationale: only this shape survives Storage path migrations, CDN swaps, signed-URL transitions, and bucket renames without rewriting every `body_tiptap` document. The render-time join (`content_assets` → derive Storage URL → emit `<img src>`) is the same pattern lesson blocks already use via `useLessonBlockAssetUrls` / `resolveThumbnailUrls`, so G6's reader page has prior art. Three integration sites must honor this contract: (1) `convert-html-to-tiptap` Edge Function (G2): when paste-time rehosting external images into `newsletter-article-images` Storage bucket, the function MUST also insert a `content_assets` row with `asset_kind='image'`, `is_library_asset=false`, `status='active'`, and emit the TipTap image node with `attrs.asset_id` set to the new `content_assets.id` — `attrs.src` may be set for display but is non-canonical and ignored by the walker. (2) Native TipTap editor image-upload toolbar (G4): same pattern — upload handler inserts a `content_assets` row + emits node with `attrs.asset_id`. (3) Public reader page (G6): renders by joining `content_assets` → derives Storage URL via `id`-based bucket path → emits `<img src>`. The walker `_walk_tiptap_for_image_asset_refs` reads only `attrs.asset_id` (validates UUID format); nodes with missing/non-uuid `attrs.asset_id` are silently skipped (graceful degradation per Lovable R-Q6.2a — authoring bugs shouldn't block save). The rebind RPC `_rebind_newsletter_article_asset_refs` does FK-safety pre-check (skips with NOTICE if asset not active per R-Q6.2b). If any of these three sites drift from the contract, the asset cascade walker will not see inline images and §71's cascade-archive will leave orphans. Discipline: any future change touching newsletter inline image handling MUST cite §133 and confirm the `attrs.asset_id` invariant holds.

§134 — pg_cron disable-at-ship pattern. To register a cron job in disabled state from a migration, use `cron.schedule_in_database(name, schedule, command, database, username, active => false)` — the 6-arg function variant with `active boolean`. Never use `cron.schedule()` followed by `UPDATE cron.job SET active = false WHERE jobname = '...'` — the UPDATE requires elevated permissions on `cron.job` that are not available to the migration role (fails with `42501 permission denied for table job`). The function API path has appropriate permissions. To enable a cron job later (after observation period or feature flag flip), use `cron.alter_job((SELECT jobid FROM cron.job WHERE jobname = '...'), active := true)` — again the function API, not direct table UPDATE. Discovered Session 93 G1.3e first apply attempt; locked as standing rule because every disabled-at-ship cron use case will hit the same permission boundary. Pairs with §131 (slot collision discovery): together they govern all pg_cron migration discipline. Concrete from Session 93: `prune_newsletter_draft_versions` registered via `cron.schedule_in_database('prune_newsletter_draft_versions', '35 6 * * *', $$SELECT public.prune_newsletter_draft_versions();$$, 'postgres', NULL, false)` — landed disabled cleanly, Cole enables after 2-week monitoring period via `cron.alter_job`.

*v92 - Session 88 CLOSE — Phase 11 Members surface frontend FULLY SHIPPED. **Phase 11 is DONE.** Three new standing rules locked: §125 (DROP-then-CREATE discipline for additive PL/pgSQL params — `CREATE OR REPLACE` only replaces identical signatures, additive optional params create ambiguous overloads that must be cleaned up with DROP RESTRICT in the same migration sequence), §126 (Lovable can ship adjacent backend changes when load-bearing — frontend-only prompts need explicit "do not modify any RPC" guardrails when backend ownership must stay with Claude; conversely when adjacent backend is permitted the prompt must explicitly authorize it and list which RPCs may be touched), §127 (caller-owns-mutation + description slot for multi-step modals reusing single-step primitives — use the shared dialog's `description: React.ReactNode` slot for the multi-step content with `<span className="block">` wrappers to avoid `<div>` inside `<p>` hydration errors). One process note: Chrome MCP cannot do CSS viewport emulation (`resize_window` resizes the host browser window but `window.innerWidth` stays at host resolution); mobile testing requires code-driven analysis of responsive Tailwind class usage in the deployed source as the correct fallback for responsive testing.

§125 — Adding optional params to existing PL/pgSQL functions requires DROP-then-CREATE, not CREATE-OR-REPLACE. `CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION` only replaces functions with identical argument signatures. Adding a new optional param creates a NEW function and leaves the old in place. PostgreSQL then has two overloads with overlapping named-args sets, and PostgREST's overload resolution becomes ambiguous when a call comes in with the original arg count — the planner cannot choose between exact match on the old and default-fill on the new, returning `42725 procedure ... is not unique`. Correct sequence for additive param evolution: (a) `CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION name(existing_params, new_param TYPE DEFAULT NULL)` — creates the new function alongside the old; (b) test the new function in isolation; (c) `DROP FUNCTION name(old_signature) RESTRICT` — RESTRICT (default) fails loud if anything depends on the old signature; CASCADE would silently chain into views or triggers and must never be used for this pattern; (d) re-test: existing N-named-arg callers resolve to the (N+1)-arg via default fill, and (N+1)-named-arg callers resolve directly. Skipping step (c) leaves intermittent `42725 is not unique` errors at runtime that present as flaky behavior (sometimes resolves, sometimes errors) depending on the planner's choice. Pairs with §96 (relax-RPC-validation requires matching CHECK-constraint audit): both reinforce that PostgreSQL function evolution touches multiple layers atomically, and validation/signature changes must touch ALL the layers in the same migration sequence. Concrete example from Session 88: `search_impersonation_targets` extended from 14 to 15 args by adding `p_specific_user_id uuid DEFAULT NULL`. Migration 1 ran `CREATE OR REPLACE` which created the 15-arg overload alongside the existing 14-arg. PostgREST then failed on existing 14-named-arg callsites because both overloads were ambiguous candidates. Migration 2 `DROP FUNCTION ... (14-arg signature) RESTRICT` cleared the overload; all callers (14-named-arg legacy + 15-named-arg new) now resolve cleanly to the canonical 15-arg via default-fill. Standing query before any additive RPC migration: `SELECT proname, pg_get_function_arguments(oid) FROM pg_proc WHERE proname = 'name';` returns all overloads — if more than one row, plan a DROP for the obsoleted one.

§126 — Lovable can ship adjacent backend changes when load-bearing. Surface: during a frontend cycle whose prompt scope said "frontend only", Lovable proactively extended `search_impersonation_targets` from the existing 3-arg form to the 14-arg form to fix a fallback `directMember` query bug that the prompt did not flag — outside the prompt's stated scope, but minimum-coupled correct fix for a load-bearing bug. Accepted by Claude post-ship; the backend extension would have been needed regardless. Locked pattern: future frontend-only Lovable prompts that need backend ownership to stay with Claude (because Claude needs to verify backward-compat, run smoke tests via Supabase MCP, or because the migration must be audited via the standing `apply_migration` workflow) include an explicit "DO NOT modify any RPC or migration" guardrail. Conversely, when Lovable is permitted to ship adjacent backend changes, the prompt explicitly authorizes it and lists the exact RPC or table names that may be touched. Don't trust prompt-scope discipline alone to prevent adjacent edits — call out what's allowed and what isn't. Trade-off: explicit guardrails add prompt length but eliminate post-ship surprise; the surprise cost (verification overhead + risk of incomplete migration sequences from §125) outweighs the prompt-bloat cost. Concrete from Session 88: cycle 1 prompt was "skeleton only, all actions stubbed" and Lovable proactively extended `search_impersonation_targets` to a 14-arg form — accepted because it was a minimum-coupled fix. Subsequent cycles (2a, 2b parts 1+2, 11.D, 11.D.2, 11.E.2) included explicit "DO NOT modify any RPC" or "Backend changes outside this list are out of scope" guardrails. Cycle 11.E permitted exactly one backend change (drop the 2-arg overload) and called it out explicitly.

§127 — Caller-owns-mutation + description slot for multi-step modals reusing single-step primitives. When a complex action surface needs multi-step UI (target picker + extra fields + amber inline gate hint, etc.) but the codebase already has a clean single-step primitive (the JustifiedActionDialog from §121), do not build a parallel multi-step dialog. Instead: pass the multi-step content through the dialog's `description: React.ReactNode` slot. Critical implementation rule: shadcn's `DialogDescription` wraps its content in a `<p>` element, so the multi-step content must use `<span className="block">` wrappers — NOT `<div>` — for layout. A `<div>` nested inside the `<p>` produces invalid HTML and triggers a React hydration warning (and in strict mode, a re-render); `<span className="block">` produces the same visual block layout without the nesting violation. Throw-then-mapError pattern for non-reason validation: the multi-step content sets state outside the dialog (target selection, optional fields), and the dialog's `onSubmit` callback (which only receives the reason string by design) reads that state and throws a typed error if any pre-condition isn't met. The dialog's `mapError` prop translates the thrown error to user-facing copy. Concrete example from Session 88 cycle 11.D.2: `MemberDrawerAssignments.tsx` uses 4 launcher components (CertPathLauncher, CurriculumLauncher, ModuleLauncher, MentorLauncher), each wrapping JustifiedActionDialog with its own target picker + due date + amber inline gate hint rendered inside the description slot. The launcher's `onSubmit(reason)` reads the picker state, validates, and throws `{ code: 'no_target_selected' }` if needed; the dialog catches the throw and renders "Please pick a target before submitting" via mapError. This pattern unlocks single-shared-dialog reuse for genuinely multi-step actions without duplicating the dialog's validation/loading/no-op handling.

§128 — Radix Collapsible state-driven child visibility requires `className="group"` on Root + `group-data-[state=X]:hidden` on children. The bare `data-[state=X]:hidden` Tailwind variant reads the state attribute from the element it's applied to, NOT from a Radix parent Root. Children of `<Collapsible.Root>` have no state attribute of their own — only the Root carries `data-state="open" | "closed"`. So a child marked `<div className="data-[state=open]:hidden">` silently fails to hide when the Collapsible opens. The fix mirrors the existing navigation-menu.tsx codebase precedent: mark the Root with the `group` Tailwind class (`<Collapsible className="group">`), then descendants use `group-data-[state=X]:hidden` to read the Radix state from the marked ancestor. Without the `group` marker on Root, child visibility silently does nothing on state changes. The pattern enables the "preview-when-closed, full-content-when-open" UI shape: place the preview text in a sibling of CollapsibleContent (NOT inside it — CollapsibleContent is the auto-toggling region) marked `group-data-[state=open]:hidden`, and a Show/Hide label inside CollapsibleTrigger using two spans `<span className="group-data-[state=open]:hidden">Show full</span><span className="group-data-[state=closed]:hidden">Hide</span>` to swap the trigger copy. Caught in Cycle B Pass 2 review during Session 89 before ship would have silently broken the WrittenSummary iteration history collapse on preview-in-Root pattern. Standing check before any Collapsible refactor: grep the file for `data-[state=` and verify every occurrence is `group-data-[state=` and that the parent Root carries `className="group"`.

Process note (not §-numbered) — Chrome MCP cannot do CSS viewport emulation. The `resize_window` tool resizes the host browser window but the page's CSS viewport stays at the host resolution. `window.innerWidth` queried via `javascript_tool` returns 2560 (or whatever the host is) regardless of how you resize. Tailwind responsive classes (`sm:`, `md:`, `lg:`) evaluate against the actual viewport, so a Chrome MCP audit at simulated 375px width cannot actually exercise the `<sm` breakpoint code paths. Mobile responsive testing via Chrome MCP must combine two methodologies: (1) in-browser visual inspection at the host viewport for what IS visible, plus (2) code-driven analysis of the deployed source — grep responsive Tailwind class usage and reason about behavior at each breakpoint. JavaScript-based contrast measurement DOES work cleanly via canvas-pixel-extraction (`ctx.fillStyle = oklab(...)` then `getImageData` to read the rendered RGB the CSS engine computed), which is how all four status pill contrast ratios were verified in cycle 11.E.2. The viewport limitation is specifically about media-query evaluation, not about reading rendered styles.

The Members surface at `/super-admin/members` shipped end-to-end across 8 cycles in Session 88: cycle 1 (page + table + drawer skeleton, 13 new files, 2 modified), cycle 1.5 (backend patch — 15th param on `search_impersonation_targets` for by-id narrowing of full-page route fallback query), cycle 2a (JustifiedActionDialog primitive + 4 single-row actions wired through the caller-owns-mutation pattern from §121), cycle 2b parts 1+2 (10 new files in `src/components/members/bulk/` covering BulkAssign/BulkUnassign/BulkOverrideCompletion modals + BulkAssignMentorModal with per-trainee cert resolution + ScheduleAssignmentModal + BulkImportModal + useBulkChunkRunner hook with useRef cancel flag), cycle 11.D (6 legacy files deleted including the 2050-line LearningAdmin.tsx, two routes converted to `<Navigate>` redirects, brand tokens migrated to `color-mix` per §-numbered palette discipline), cycle 11.D.2 (Assignments tab wired with 4 launcher components reusing cycle 2b RPCs with single-user payloads via the §127 caller-owns-mutation + description slot pattern), cycle 11.E (backend 2-arg overload dropped via DROP RESTRICT, 2 dead files deleted, learning-tree-types.ts extracted), cycle 11.E.2 (a11y + mobile audit pass — 7 fixes across 5 files: pagination aria-labels, overflow-x wrapper, mobile column-hiding ladder via responsive Tailwind, drawer Active badge + Mentor switch aria-labels, row actions aria-label including user name, bulk modal viewport-shrink class). Five backend migrations applied this session: `phase11c_cycle1_5_add_specific_user_id_param`, `phase11c_cycle1_5_drop_legacy_14arg_search_impersonation_targets`, `phase11e_drop_legacy_search_impersonation_targets_2arg` (Session 88 specific), plus M1-M5 from Session 87 as baseline. Audit findings doc at `/home/claude/round-11e-audit/findings.md` covers 12 items — 7 shipped in 11.E.2, 5 deferred to a v2 polish ticket (mobile column-hiding refinement based on analytics; row hover-reveal opacity keyboard discoverability — current `opacity-0 group-hover:opacity-100` is invisible to keyboard users until they Tab to the row; Mentor body text contrast bump from 4.79:1 marginal to 7:1+; filter chip horizontal scroll on narrow viewports; page header button stacking polish; inconsistent button labeling pattern where Toggle Sidebar / Log Out / drawer Close use label-on-inner-span instead of `aria-label` on the button itself). All status pills pass WCAG AA contrast (Active 5.32:1, Certified 5.32:1, In Progress 5.93:1, Mentor 4.79:1) — measured via JavaScript canvas-pixel-extraction. The drawer header is NOT a green+teal pairing violation (initial visual concern was wrong; both Active and Certified pills render forest green `#2D6A4F` per the cycle 11.D brand-token migration).


*v91 - Session 87 CLOSE — Phase 11 Members surface consolidation design + backend phase SHIPPED. Two new standing rules locked: §121 (caller-owns-mutation pattern for shared action dialogs) and §122 (jsonb-on-row prefs vs table-of-prefs decision criterion). Two process notes from this session that remain candidates for §-numbering after Phase 11 ships: bulk RPC cap matches existing codebase pattern with frontend chunking shipping independently as UX improvement (not as timeout safety); saved view detachment uses Linear pattern with leading `●` dot indicator and three-button switch dialog. 5 backend migrations applied + verified live (M1 `add_users_ui_preferences_column`, M2 `extend_search_impersonation_targets`, M3 `create_list_user_audit_history_rpc`, M4 `create_completion_bulk_rpcs`, M5 `add_completion_export_rpc`). Coach gate audit performed: 4 checks all clean — `grant_additional_free_attempts` gates on super_admin + impersonation_allows only (no account_type check); `coach_certifications` RLS "coaches read own" uses `user_id = auth.uid()` not account_type filter; 33 functions reference both account_type and coach in body but none affect the Members Coach tab; `_sync_is_practitioner_coach_on_account_type` trigger auto-sets the flag when account_type becomes coach OR brainwise_super_admin (explains why all 10 coaches + 2 super_admins have `is_practitioner_coach=true`). EXPLAIN ANALYZE on `list_user_audit_history` confirmed planner picks existing `idx_super_admin_audit_log_affected_user_created` partial composite index (Index Scan, 0.051ms exec, 3 buffer hits). `auth.users.last_sign_in_at` accessible via SECDEF — postgres role has SELECT on auth.users. Two Lovable review passes incorporated (substantive engagement, 16 + 5 adoptions). Three pushbacks accepted with evidence: bulk RPC cap stays at 500 (Supabase project `statement_timeout = 2min`, not Lovable's assumed 8s PostgREST cancellation); no new audit index needed (existing partial composite covers); "Last login" rename instead of new `last_active_at` infra (defer infra to v2).

§121 — caller-owns-mutation pattern for shared action dialogs. When a "shared" dialog component would otherwise require a discriminated union of action types (each branch with different RPC, payload shape, React Query invalidation keys, error mapping, permission gating), invert ownership: dialog provides visual consistency + UX consistency + justification-field handling + validation + submitting state + error display + no-op handling + success toast. Caller passes the mutation function as a prop, and owns RPC selection + payload construction + post-action React Query invalidation + post-success cleanup. The shared component is a thin shell, not a switch statement. Trade-off: callers carry slightly more per-callsite code, but the cleanup logic is genuinely caller-specific (different RPCs invalidate different query keys), so the asymmetry is honest rather than hidden. Concrete API shape from Session 87 Phase 11 planning: `interface JustifiedActionDialogProps { open, onOpenChange, title, description?, onSubmit: (reason: string) => Promise<{changed: boolean, note?: string}>, mapError?: (raw: string) => string, successTitle, noopTitle?, confirmLabel? }`. The `onSubmit` callback receives the validated justification string and returns a result object the dialog uses to decide between success toast and no-op toast (when `changed: false`). Pattern explicitly considered and rejected for Phase 11: single component with action-type discriminated union (would produce ~400-line switch statement, harder to extend, lower test isolation per action). Rule: when "share" is about UX consistency rather than logic consistency, share the UX shell and let callers own the logic.

§122 — jsonb-on-row prefs vs table-of-prefs decision criterion. For per-user UI preferences scoped to a single admin surface, a `column-on-users jsonb` is fine. Migrate to a dedicated `user_ui_preferences` table when EITHER (a) 5+ admin surfaces have persisted prefs OR (b) any query-into-preferences requirement emerges (e.g., "find all users whose saved view filters by org X" — that's a query-into-the-jsonb, which the column pattern cannot serve). Until those conditions trigger, the column is simpler: one migration, no FK join, no auth model question. Required column-comment contract: write-from-frontend / read-whole-blob-on-mount / never query into the jsonb (no GIN indexes, no `jsonb_path_query` in WHERE clauses, no `->` extracts in indexes). Include schema-version field at the top level of the surface key (e.g., `{"members": {"version": 1, ...}}`) so the frontend can detect old payloads and either migrate-in-place-on-write or fall back to defaults when the shape evolves. Concrete example from Session 87 Phase 11: `users.ui_preferences jsonb NOT NULL DEFAULT '{}'::jsonb` stores `{"members": {"version": 1, "default_view": "...", "saved_views": [...]}}`. Migration to a table is genuinely cheap when the day comes (one migration + one hook swap), so deferring is correct — but the deferral must be explicit, not implicit. Anti-pattern: starting with a jsonb column "because it's simpler" and then GIN-indexing it three months later because "we needed to query by preference value" — by that point the table migration is doubly expensive (data move + index rebuild + RPC swap). Rule: jsonb is fine for single-surface row-scoped settings written and read whole; the moment you query into it, you owe yourself a table.

Phase 11.B migrations ship notes — Members surface backend (Session 87). **M1 `add_users_ui_preferences_column`**: single ADD COLUMN with locked `'{}'` default + NOT NULL + comprehensive column comment documenting the write-whole/read-whole contract from §122. Round-trip smoke test via `||` jsonb concatenation operator passed cleanly. **M2 `extend_search_impersonation_targets`**: DROP RESTRICT + CREATE on the 3-arg form (not CASCADE — fail loud if anything depends on the old return shape) → new 14-arg signature with 7 new returned columns (`is_mentor`, `active_assignment_count`, `certification_count`, `worst_certification_status`, `account_status`, `last_sign_in_at` from `auth.users`, `show_coach_tab`) and 11 new optional filter+sort params (all NULL-default so existing 4 callsites pass only 3 args and continue working). The `active_assignment_count` is the sum of `user_curriculum_assignments WHERE status='active'` + `user_module_assignments WHERE status='active'` + `coach_mentor_assignments WHERE trainee_user_id=u.id AND ended_at IS NULL` — trainee-side mentor relationships, not mentor-side. `worst_certification_status` priority is `revoked > in_progress > certified` (revoked is "worst" because it requires re-action). Sort columns supported: name / email / account_type / organization / account_status / worst_certification_status / active_assignments / certification_count / last_login — dynamic ORDER BY via CASE on `p_sort_column` and `p_sort_direction`. Two-CTE structure: `filtered` applies row-level filters then `refiltered` applies the post-computed filters (`p_has_active_assignments`, `p_certification_statuses`, `p_last_active_within`) that depend on the aggregated counts/status from `filtered`. `auth.users` SELECT works because SECDEF runs as function owner (postgres role has SELECT on auth.users). `last_sign_in_at` from `auth.users` only updates on password sign-in, NOT on JWT refresh — frontend column header renamed to "Last login" with tooltip "Last password sign-in. Does not reflect active sessions." for honest semantics. **M3 `create_list_user_audit_history_rpc`**: SECDEF `list_user_audit_history(p_user_id, p_limit=50, p_offset=0, p_categories[]=NULL)` filtering `super_admin_audit_log` by `affected_user_id = p_user_id`. Joins `users` for actor resolution with `'Unknown admin'` fallback when `super_admin_user_id IS NULL`. Category bucket computed via CASE on `action_type`: `role` (mentor_role_changed), `completion` (content_item/module/curriculum completion), `certification` (granted/revoked/free_attempts), `permission` (mentor/curriculum/module assignment + org admin), `impersonation` (started/action/denied/ended), `other` (fallback). Existing index `idx_super_admin_audit_log_affected_user_created` partial composite `(affected_user_id, created_at DESC) WHERE affected_user_id IS NOT NULL` is the optimal index for this query — EXPLAIN ANALYZE confirmed planner pick. **M4 `create_completion_bulk_rpcs`**: three SECDEF wrappers following `assign_curriculum_bulk` template (BEGIN/EXCEPTION/END per user_id, max 500, return `{operation, requested, succeeded, failed, results[]}` shape). `set_curriculum_completion_bulk` is the tricky one — single-user `set_curriculum_completion` keys on `p_assignment_id` not `p_curriculum_id`, so the wrapper resolves each user's assignment via `WHERE user_id = v_uid AND curriculum_id = p_curriculum_id AND status IN ('active', 'completed') ORDER BY CASE status WHEN 'active' THEN 0 ELSE 1 END, assigned_at DESC LIMIT 1`. Users without a matching assignment record `'no_curriculum_assignment_for_user'` as a per-user failure, allowing the bulk to continue. Impersonation gate inherited from wrapped single-user RPC's `assert_impersonation_allows('permission_change')` — bulk wrapper calls `assert_super_admin()` once at top, does NOT re-call the impersonation gate. **M5 `add_completion_export_rpc`**: SECDEF `get_user_completion_export(p_user_ids uuid[])` returning a flat per-user-per-item rowset via UNION ALL across 4 tier CTEs (cert_path from `coach_certifications`, curriculum from `user_curriculum_assignments`, module from `user_module_assignments`, content_item from `content_item_completions`). Content_item rows include `parent_path` via LEFT JOIN to `modules` for the breadcrumb context. Frontend builds CSV from the result; max 500 users.

Session 87 process notes (candidate §-numbered rules, not yet promoted). **Note A (bulk RPC cap + frontend chunking discipline)**: when wrapping single-user RPCs into bulk wrappers, the cap matches the existing bulk pattern in the codebase for consistency (current: 500, matches `assign_curriculum_bulk` etc). Frontend chunking + progress UI ships independently as a UX improvement, NOT as a backend timeout workaround — conflating the two leads to confused code comments and brittle scaling assumptions. Chunks of 50-100 per batch are pragmatic for progress feedback; cancel aborts the loop on frontend (each chunk's RPC commits independently, so canceling does not roll back already-committed batches). Post-cancel UI must be honest: "Cancelled. {N} of {total} processed." not "Cancelled. Nothing was changed." Verify the project's actual `statement_timeout` before assuming PostgREST cancellation timing — Supabase projects often have `2min` configured, not the assumed `8s`. **Note B (saved view detachment, Linear pattern)**: when a UI surface has both saved views and inline filter controls (chips, column toggles, sort), chip toggles detach the active view into an unsaved state rather than overwriting the saved view in place. Indicator: leading `●` dot before view name (VS Code/Figma convention; italics reads as "system view" not "dirty"). Discard requires confirmation when 3+ filter/column changes detected (single-chip discard is silent). View-switch while detached uses three-button dialog [Cancel] [Discard] [Save and switch] — two-button forces a context switch to save first, three-button respects the genuine three-way choice. Both notes are real patterns from Phase 11 design; promote to §-numbered rules after Phase 11.C ships and they're operationally validated.

Three super-admin surfaces consolidated into single Members page: `/super-admin/learning-admin` (2038 lines, 4 inline functions — Trainees / Assign-Unassign / MentorRole / CompletionControl), `/super-admin/users` (278 lines), `UserDetailsModal` (313 lines). Structural problem: five copies of the same search-table-pagination-dropdown pattern. Replacement: single data table + filter chips + multi-select + side drawer with Learning / Assignments / Coach (conditional) / Audit tabs. Industry-standard pattern (Linear, Notion, Absorb, Docebo April 2026); competitor recon at `phase-11-learners-surface-decisions.md` covers 10+ LMS platforms. 14 design decisions locked end-to-end; frontend cycles planned as 3-cycle split (1 = skeleton with stubbed actions, 2a = JustifiedActionDialog + single-row actions, 2b = bulk modals + mentor-bulk-assign + audit polish) plus 11.D cleanup. Mentor bulk-assign included in v1 with custom per-trainee certification resolution modal — the certification axis is load-bearing for the operation to make sense (a mentor isn't generically "the mentor for these N people"; they're "the mentor for these N people on this specific certification program each"). Coach tab visibility derived as `is_practitioner_coach=true OR account_type='coach'` — the OR is defensive but equivalent to just `is_practitioner_coach=true` given the `_sync_is_practitioner_coach_on_account_type` trigger. Frontend rendering details locked: per-row overflow menu `group-hover:opacity-100 md:opacity-0 md:group-hover:opacity-100` (desktop hover, touch always-visible); drawer responsive via shadcn Sheet native `className="w-full sm:max-w-[720px]"` (no manual breakpoint code); ContentItemArtifactPanel uses `max-h-[60vh] overflow-y-auto` + sticky internal header to make inline expansion viable; saved views persist last-selected across sessions via `default_view` field; columns are PART of each saved view (not separate global preference). Legacy nav entries during cycle 1 are renamed to "Legacy: Users" / "Legacy: Learning Admin" with deprecation banners on the pages themselves linking to specific equivalent locations in Members (e.g., "Completion controls have moved to Members → {user} → Learning tab.").
