New process patterns from rounds 2-5: stale-TODO discovery (deferred-to-X comments require verification, not load-bearing trust), audit discipline (claims about presence/absence/count of code need literal grep verification before being written into specs or self-checks; Round 5 applied this proactively with zero verification catches), and the resources-subsystem-as-positive-example pattern (subsystems built with type discipline and a11y attention from day one need substantially less polish work than subsystems that grew organically). The `results_available` notification firing point shipped: AFTER INSERT OR UPDATE trigger on `facet_interpretations` (`WHEN section_type = 'facet_insights_all'`) compares `jsonb_array_length(facet_data)` against `assessment_results.facet_insights_all_total`; on match, fires `notify_user('results_available', ...)` for taker and (if `ordered_by_coach_id` is set) coach, with shared `dedup_key = 'results_available:' || assessment_result_id` (per-user unique index permits both rows). PTP-only v1 (gated by `instrument_id = 'INST-001'` plus presence of `facet_insights_all_total`); NAI/AIRSA/HSS silently pass through, deferred to future sessions. Paired-PTP behavior: Option A — one notification per half (per `assessment_result_id`); UI-side collapse from Session 85 Option C2 handles the user-facing single-entity view.

§119 — completion-watcher trigger pattern. When a notification needs to fire at "true completion" of a server-side process whose completion threshold is already maintained by the producing Edge Function (count column, status column, etc.), prefer a Postgres AFTER INSERT/UPDATE trigger reading that threshold over editing the EF. Conditions: (a) the threshold column already exists and is reliably populated by the EF; (b) the completion contract is enumerable from data already in the database — not derived implicitly from EF code; (c) the trigger can be safely deployed before the receiving notification type is activated (dry-run mode via `is_v1_active = false` short-circuits `notify_user`). Pattern: AFTER INSERT OR UPDATE trigger with WHEN-clause filter, SECDEF function performing threshold check, defensive orphan + type guards, per-recipient `BEGIN/EXCEPTION` isolation, `dedup_key` on `notify_user` for fire-once-per-target. Reversible via DROP TRIGGER + flag flip. Concrete example: Session 86 `fire_results_available_on_full_facets()` reads `assessment_results.facet_insights_all_total` and `facet_interpretations.facet_data` array length to detect PTP report completion without touching `calculate-scores`, `generate-report`, or `generate-facet-interpretations`. Constraints: the pattern only works when the EF already populates the threshold; if it does not, this pattern collapses into the harder "rearchitect the EF to write a completion marker" problem.

§120 — palette color semantics depend on actor identity, not label text. When deciding whether a UI element should use the "in-progress" color (`--bw-teal`/`--info`) versus the "pending/warning" color (`--bw-amber`/`--warning`), the determining factor is *who is doing the work*, not the literal label. "In Progress" displayed to a user actively engaged with their own learning content → teal (user is the actor). "In Progress" or "Submitted for review" displayed to a user waiting on someone else's action → amber (someone else is the actor; this is a pending state from the viewer's perspective). Concrete examples from Session 86: Tile.tsx pill on My Learning (user actively working) → teal. ModuleDetail Clock icon on in-progress content items (user actively working) → teal. WrittenSummaryViewer "Submitted for review (pending)" (waiting on mentor) → amber, kept intentionally. CoachInvoices "In Progress" status badge (waiting on client to complete paid assessment) → judgment call, kept as teal by product decision for consistency-of-color across the app despite the waiting-state nature. Palette audits via string-search (e.g., "find every `--bw-amber`") are the right tool to surface candidates but the wrong tool to decide which to flip; each candidate requires a one-line semantic read on actor identity.

Phase 10 round 1 (My Learning tab) ship notes: backend additions to `get_user_learning_state` (flat `estimated_minutes`, `instrument_codes`, `recommended_next.content_item_title`) via surgical edits to existing function and both `_compute_recommended_next_for_*` helpers. Frontend type discipline reinforced: inline `UserLearningState` interface with `as unknown as <Interface>` boundary cast replaces `as any` casts on the two RPC calls (§111). Nested `curriculum` and `modules` typed loosely with code comment marking the loose typing as minimal-scope deferral, not intentional discipline. New Tile props `recommendedNextLabel` and `inlineCtaLoading` are optional and additive — existing consumers (CertPathDetail, CurriculumDetail, ResourceGridTab) inherit no behavior change. Per-entity enroll-loading lock implemented via `enrollingId: string | null` component-level state, cleared in `finally` block; per-entity by design — global lock punishes legitimate sequential enrollments. Render order locked: `!userId` → error → loading → welcome shell → normal (error must precede welcome shell to prevent transient RPC errors masquerading as first-time-user state).

Phase 10 round 2 (CertPathDetail.tsx) ship notes: single-file polish round, no backend. §111 type discipline applied to the four `as any` sites: main RPC return cast as `CertPathDetailResponse`, derived state annotated with named interfaces, enroll RPC response handled via `EnrollResponse` union (`EnrollPaymentRequired | Record<string, unknown> | null`) with type-assertion narrow inside the if-condition because TypeScript can't auto-narrow on a `.status` discriminator across a `Record<string, unknown>` arm. Two `as unknown as` boundary casts remain — the input-side `as never` casts on RPC argument calls (Supabase generated-types union suppression) were intentionally left untouched; they're a separate concern from output-side wrapper typing and belong to a future round addressing supabase-types generation. New process pattern: **stale-TODO discovery**. Round 2 found a TODO comment marking "Resume CTA deep-link to content viewer" as deferred to Group W "once viewers ship" — but content viewer infrastructure (`ContentItemViewer.tsx`, route `/learning/content-item/:contentItemId`) had already shipped, with `ModuleDetail.tsx` already deep-linking to it. The TODO had become stale without anyone noticing. Lesson: when reviewing a "deferred" comment during polish, do one search to verify the deferral target still applies. Stale TODOs are silent technical debt — they read as accurate until verified. Round 3+ should treat every "TODO: deferred to Group X" comment in scope as a candidate for verification, not as a load-bearing assertion.

Phase 10 round 3 (CurriculumDetail.tsx + ModuleDetail.tsx paired) ship notes: two-file polish round, no backend, single Lovable cycle. The three detail-page surfaces (CertPathDetail/CurriculumDetail/ModuleDetail) are architecturally near-clones — same hero gradient pattern, same loading/error/CTA structure, same `paidNudgeState` shape, same enroll handler wrapped around an RPC call with `payment_required` branch. This makes paired polish efficient (one mental model applies twice) but also concentrates the §111 violations identically across all three files. The full detail-page family is now consistently typed and behaviorally aligned: `CertPathDetailResponse`/`CurriculumDetailResponse`/`ModuleDetailResponse` interfaces with `EnrollResponse` discriminated unions, `isEnrolling` per-page state with try/finally locks, `navigate(-1)` with `/resources` fallback on Back buttons, retry buttons on error states, `role="status"` + aria-label on loading spinners, brand glyph comments above brain icons, `line-clamp-2` on hero h1s, content-item-level Resume deep-linking. ModuleDetail's content item row got an additional `aria-label="Open content item: {title}"` for screen reader users (unique to ModuleDetail because only it surfaces the per-content-item click target). Round 3 also surfaced four stale TODO Group W comments in ModuleDetail — all already worked, all were vestigial; cleanup removed them.

**Audit discipline pattern (Session 86 process note, not §-numbered).** Across rounds 2 and 3, Claude made four audit/spec claims about code that were falsified by grep before execution: a "stale TODO" that pointed at infrastructure which had already shipped, "dead code" that had an active callsite, a "self-check expected count" off by one because a callsite was missed during enumeration, and a "deferred" classification that recovery showed had moved past its deferral target. Each was caught by Lovable pre-flight verification or post-merge grep; recovery cost was one round trip per miss. The pattern is consistent: claims about presence/absence/count of code (dead code, callsites, TODO targets, match counts) need literal grep verification before they're written into a spec or self-check. Pattern-match-and-claim is the failure mode; grep-then-claim is the correction. This applies symmetrically to Claude's audit work and to any code-claim Claude makes in a spec — the discipline that's applied to Lovable's reading of files (read first, then write) applies equally to Claude's claims about files (grep first, then claim). Round 5 audit applied this discipline proactively (every expected self-check count was grep-verified against the live file before being written) — zero verification catches needed.

Phase 10 round 5 (ResourceGridTab.tsx + ResourceReader.tsx) ship notes: smallest Phase 10 round of Session 86. The resources subsystem was built with proper TypeScript interfaces from day one (`src/components/resources/types.ts` exports `Resource`/`ResourceTab`/`GetUserResourcesResult`/`UpgradeEntityType`), so neither file had `as any` casts to fix — §111 work was zero. The polish scope was narrowly a11y (search aria-label, two loading-state role/aria-label/aria-hidden additions), error resilience (try/catch wrap on `handleFileDownload`, Retry buttons on VideoPlayer error and resource-not-found branches), back-button consistency (three sites in ResourceReader aligned to the Round 2-3 `navigate(-1)` with `/resources` fallback pattern), and one decision-tree clarifying comment above `handleResourceClick` documenting the 5-branch routing precedence. Two patterns previously fixed in other rounds were already correct in this subsystem: empty state correctly distinguishes filter-empty from real-empty (My Learning round 1 had to add this; ResourceGridTab had it from the start at lines 126 vs 148), and `FileDownloadCard` already had the disabled + Loader2 spinner pattern that Rounds 2-3 applied to enroll buttons. The takeaway: subsystems built with type discipline and a11y attention from the start need substantially less polish work than subsystems that grew organically. New code in BrainWise should follow the resources-subsystem pattern of typed interfaces + a11y attributes from day one rather than requiring a polish round to retrofit.*

*v89 - Session 85 CLOSE — production bug cluster session (five fix workstreams shipped end-to-end and verified). §114 added (UI cert-status gates must distinguish "no cert" from "in-progress with active cert-pool credit"). §115 added (tier-archive cascades must whitelist the tier's `archive_reason` in the CHECK constraint before the cascade trigger can write). §116 added (thumbnails are public-tier per §84; RLS on metadata when bytes are world-readable is the wrong protection model; SECURITY DEFINER RPC enforcing "entity published AND not archived" at the API layer is the correct architecture). §117 added (`coach_clients_client_view` is for client callers exclusively; coach callers query the base table). §118 added (paired-PTP collapse uses mutually-paired check, not instrument equality — each side's `paired_assessment_id` must mirror the other to qualify for collapse). Surgical-edit process discipline locked (not §-numbered): when a complex RPC needs a small change, diff against the live function definition and edit surgically; never rewrite from memory. Six backend migrations, one new SECURITY DEFINER RPC. No Edge Functions deployed via MCP this session. No new tables, no new buckets, no rollup-trigger changes. (1) §114 NEW — **UI cert-status gates must distinguish "no cert" from "in-progress with active cert-pool credit."** Standing rule surfaced from Session 85 Bug 1 (Caroline / Patrice / Ryan blocked from ordering assessments despite holding cert-pool credit). The `coach_certifications` table carries both a `status` field (`in_progress` / `certified` / `revoked` / etc.) AND a `free_assessment_uses` jsonb field tracking remaining cert-pool credit per instrument. The two are orthogonal. A coach can be `in_progress` with non-zero `free_assessment_uses` — they have not yet completed certification curriculum but they have been granted cert-pool credit (typically because they paid for or were sponsored to the cert path and are working through it). The locked rule: any UI gate that asks "can this coach do X" must consider BOTH fields together: `canDoFeature = (status = 'certified') || (status = 'in_progress' && hasActivePool(instrument_id))`. The existing gates that only checked `certified` produced the Bug 1 pattern — a coach who legitimately holds pool credit cannot use it because the UI does not consider them eligible to take the action that would consume it. Pairs with §110 (entitlement_source = `free_cert_pool` on the resulting assessment row) and §111 (the cert-pool branch is one of four entitlement sources). Applies forward to any feature where multiple status/credit fields together determine eligibility — subscription tier + remaining-credit, role + active-assignment, cert-status + cert-pool, etc. The mistake to avoid is treating one field as the gate when it is one of several inputs to the gate. (2) §115 NEW — **Tier-archive cascades must whitelist the tier's `archive_reason` in the CHECK constraint before the cascade trigger can write.** Standing rule surfaced from Session 85 Bug 2 (module archive cascade rolling back the whole transaction). The platform's archive cascade pattern (§43, §50, §108) traverses parent-to-child writing an `archive_reason` to dependent `content_assets` rows when a parent entity is archived. The CHECK constraint on `content_assets.archive_reason` is a positive whitelist. When a new tier-archive cascade is added (or extended to a new parent type), the trigger writes an archive_reason value that must already be in the whitelist or the INSERT/UPDATE fails the CHECK and the entire enclosing transaction aborts. The locked rule: every new tier-archive cascade ships in one migration that extends the CHECK whitelist FIRST and then enables the cascade. The migration ordering matters because the cascade may fire at deploy time on existing rows (a `BEFORE INSERT` trigger on a populated table) and a CHECK failure during deploy is a much worse failure mode than during normal operation. Session 85's instance: `content_assets.archive_reason` CHECK had 5 values (`content_item_archived`, `lesson_block_replaced`, `replaced_by_author`, `manual_archive`, `orphaned_pending_expired`); the migration extended to 8 by adding `module_archived`, `curriculum_archived`, `certification_path_archived`. Applies forward to any CHECK-constrained reason/state field that participates in cascade triggers — `archive_reason`, `audit_action_type` (already covered by §99), `notification_type`, etc. The systematic risk is the same in all of them: triggers write enum-like values into CHECK-constrained columns, and adding a new value to the trigger without adding it to the CHECK silently breaks the cascade at runtime. Pairs with §99 (same pattern for `super_admin_action_types` whitelist). (3) §116 NEW — **Thumbnails are public-tier per §84; RLS on metadata when bytes are world-readable is the wrong protection model.** Standing rule surfaced from Session 85 Bug 3 Symptom 2 (trainee tier-thumbnail blank rendering). The platform's storage tier model (§84) classifies thumbnail buckets as PUBLIC — their bytes are world-readable via direct URL. When the asset bytes are public, applying RLS to the asset metadata row (e.g., `content_assets`) to constrain WHO can read the metadata creates a structural mismatch: anyone who knows the asset URL can fetch the bytes, but only some viewers can read the metadata describing the asset. The Session 85 bug surfaced because `content_assets_trainee_read` RLS policy anchored its EXISTS chain on `content_items`, and tier thumbnails (cert_path, curriculum, module, resource) have `content_item_id IS NULL`. Trainees could not read the metadata, even though they could have fetched the bytes if given the URL. The fix is architectural, not a policy patch: the correct protection model for public-tier metadata is a SECURITY DEFINER RPC that enforces the REAL access predicate at the API layer. For tier thumbnails, the real predicate is "entity is published AND not archived" — which is a property of the entity, not the viewer. The RPC `get_thumbnail_urls_for_entities(p_entity_type text, p_entity_ids uuid[])` shipped Session 85 implements this: it branches per entity_type, validates `is_published = true AND archived_at IS NULL` on the parent entity, and returns the asset metadata for any authenticated caller when the predicate holds. Resource thumbnails are the exception — they mirror the `get_user_resources` is_visible rules with super_admin bypass, because resource visibility itself is per-viewer. The locked rule: when an asset's bytes are public, do not apply viewer-scoped RLS to the metadata; expose the metadata via a SECDEF RPC that enforces the actual access predicate (typically a property of the parent entity, not the viewer). RLS on metadata is the right model only when the bytes are private (lesson-assets, content-item-file-uploads, etc. per §84/§108). Pairs with §84 (storage tier classification) and §108 (private-bucket RLS floor — the inverse case). (4) §117 NEW — **`coach_clients_client_view` is for client callers exclusively; coach callers query the base table.** Standing rule surfaced from Session 85 Bug 4 (Cheryl couldn't see Edgar's results). The view-as-gate pattern (§89) creates a SECURITY DEFINER view with a WHERE clause acting as the authorization gate; for `coach_clients_client_view`, that clause is `WHERE client_user_id = auth.uid()`. The clause projects only rows where the CALLER is the client — which is correct for the client surface (MyResults, Onboarding, PrivacySettings, InstrumentSelection's purchase-history query) but returns ZERO rows when a coach is the caller, because their auth.uid() does not match the client_user_id slot on any row. The Session 85 bug: `MyResults.tsx` line 437 queried the view unconditionally, including when the page was loaded in coach-view mode (`isCoachView && targetUserId` present). The coach call returned empty, the page flashed empty, the user reported "I can't see the results." The locked rule: any frontend query against a view-as-gate must consider WHICH caller class the view is gating for. If the page is reachable by multiple caller classes (client viewing self, coach viewing client, super-admin impersonation), the query path must branch — `isCoachView ? .from("coach_clients") : .from("coach_clients_client_view")`. Coach callers query the base table because the base table's RLS already permits coaches to read rows where they are the coach (and the base-table SELECT policy for clients was dropped in Session 73 per §89 — clients have NO base-table SELECT path, which is why the view exists). The systematic diagnostic for "this query returns empty for one caller class but not another" is to read the view definition and check the WHERE clause against the calling identity. Pairs with §89 (the view-as-gate pattern itself) and reinforces the standing discipline of verifying RLS/view behavior under impersonation for every caller class the surface supports. (5) §118 NEW — **Paired-PTP collapse uses mutually-paired check, not instrument equality.** Standing rule from Session 85 Bug 5 (Option C2 UX consistency). The PTP instrument supports paired professional+personal contexts — two `assessments` rows (one per context) linked bidirectionally via the `paired_assessment_id` column on each side. The UX collapse pattern presents a paired PTP as ONE user-visible entity in coach tile lists and client dropdowns. The naive collapse predicate "any two PTP rows with the same instrument_id and same user" would erroneously collapse two professional retakes into one (a user can take Professional twice). The correct predicate is mutual pairing: row A's `paired_assessment_id` equals row B's id AND row B's `paired_assessment_id` equals row A's id. The DB stores the link bidirectionally — when a paired pair is created, both rows' `paired_assessment_id` columns are populated. Retakes do NOT mirror — a second Professional rating has its own `paired_assessment_id` pointing at its own (possibly empty) personal companion, not at any prior Professional rating. The locked rule: any collapse, grouping, or "show as one entity" UX pattern over paired-context data must use mutually-paired check as the predicate. The check generalizes to any future paired-context instrument (AIRSA already uses a different paired mechanism — self+supervisor — with its own `paired_assessment_id` linkage; future instruments with multi-context support should adopt the same bidirectional storage and mutual-pairing predicate). Pairs with the standing PTP context model (§-prior reference — the `assessments.context_type` enum carries `professional` / `personal` / `both`). (6) **Surgical-edit process discipline (not §-numbered, but locked operationally).** When a non-trivial RPC, trigger, or stored procedure needs a small change, the correct approach is: (a) read the live function body via `pg_get_functiondef(oid)` or via the migration history in `supabase_migrations.schema_migrations`; (b) diff the proposed change against the read body; (c) write a migration that applies only the surgical edit. Full rewrites from memory introduce regression risk — Session 85 hit this on `get_user_learning_state`, where a full-rewrite attempt accidentally introduced a `GROUP BY` bug. Recovery was clean (caught during verification before any production traffic hit it, restored the known-good version from the migration history, applied a surgical edit). The discipline: every non-trivial RPC change starts with reading the current definition; the rewrite-from-memory shortcut is forbidden for functions with cross-CTE / window-function / GROUP-BY logic. Verification of any RPC change uses a separate `execute_sql` query that actually invokes the function — `apply_migration` success only confirms the SQL parsed, not that the function returns the expected shape. Pairs with §94 (read the deployed function body before modifying). (7) **RPC wrapper shape discipline (§111 reinforce).** Session 85 backend work confirmed the discipline held: every RPC returning a wrapper object (e.g., `{items: [...], unread_count: N}`) had a proper TypeScript interface at the call site, unwrapped explicitly to `.items` etc., never cast wrapper-to-array via `as unknown as`. The Session 84 lesson (§111 from architecture-reference v88 was actually a different rule — payment-source discriminator; the wrapper-shape lesson is standing operational rather than §-numbered) holds: define proper wrapper interfaces matching RPC return shapes; never bypass type checking with `as unknown as` casts. (8) **New RPC shipped Session 85 — `get_thumbnail_urls_for_entities(p_entity_type text, p_entity_ids uuid[])`.** SECURITY DEFINER, search_path locked, accepts any authenticated caller. Returns `[{entity_id uuid, asset_id uuid, bucket text, path text, dominant_color text}]`. Branches per entity_type: `cert_path` / `curriculum` / `module` require `is_published = true AND archived_at IS NULL` on the parent entity (gate at the API layer per §116); `resource` branch mirrors `get_user_resources` is_visible rules with super_admin bypass. Called from 5 frontend sites: `MyLearningTab.tsx`, `ResourceGridTab.tsx`, `CertPathDetail.tsx`, `CurriculumDetail.tsx`, `ModuleDetail.tsx` via new helpers `resolveTierThumbnailUrls` and `resolveTierThumbnailRows` in `src/lib/assetUrls.ts`. (9) **`get_user_learning_state` RPC surgical edit (Bug 3 Symptom 1).** LEFT JOIN to `certification_paths` added in `v_assignments` CTE; flat `name`/`description`/`thumbnail_asset_id` columns added in `v_assignment_rows` via `COALESCE(cp_*, curriculum_*)` so the My Learning tab can render cert-path and curriculum tiles uniformly; same flat fields propagated to `v_module_assignment_rows`. The three migrations: `session85_get_user_learning_state_project_flat_tile_fields` (BROKEN — full-rewrite attempt with GROUP BY bug), `session85_revert_get_user_learning_state_to_z_m4` (rollback to last-known-good from migration history), `session85_get_user_learning_state_add_flat_tile_fields` (surgical edit). Process discipline lesson logged above. (10) **`content_assets_trainee_read` RLS policy alignment (Bug 3 supporting fix).** `status = 'active'` → `status IN ('active', 'completed')` to align with the actual lifecycle of asset references on completed entities. This was an unrelated edge case discovered during Symptom 2 recon; the policy was rejecting reads on assets attached to completed (vs. still-active) entities. The proper fix for tier thumbnails is the §116 RPC pattern, not this RLS extension; the RLS extension covers other valid access paths that genuinely need to see completed-tier asset metadata. (11) **`content_assets.archive_reason` CHECK extension (Bug 2).** 5-value whitelist → 8-value whitelist; added `module_archived`, `curriculum_archived`, `certification_path_archived` per §115. (12) Standing rules §61-§113 unchanged. No new tables, no new buckets, no rollup-trigger changes. No movement Session 85 on AIRSA Phases 3e-8, SOC 2 written policies, Action-Oriented Voice Redesign, pricing-reads refactor, corporate contract renewal schema change, Clarity Engine. (13) **Edge Function versions at Session 85 close:** unchanged from Session 84 — no Edge Functions deployed via MCP this session. Owed to GitHub `cbastianBWE/brainwise-blueprint` per §92: unchanged carryover from Session 84 (`compute-dominant-color` v2, `finalize-asset-upload` v4, `stripe-webhook` v27, `content-item-file-upload` v2, `identity-mutation`, `learning-admin-import` v1, `draft-text` v7, `get-content-item-video-url` v1, `content-item-ai-assist` v1, `skills-practice-attachment-upload` v1, `get-lesson-block-asset-urls` v1, and the `create-checkout`/`customer-portal` drift). (14) **Cohorts formally deferred indefinitely.** Q11 scoped them as schema-seam only (`cohorts` + `cohort_members` tables exist for forward compatibility); v1 UI was always a non-goal. Group C is closeable without them. Re-opening requires a deliberate product decision, not implicit creep at Group C closeout. (15) Session 85 close artifacts: build-queue.md v93 entry, this v89 architecture-reference entry (§114, §115, §116, §117, §118 + surgical-edit process discipline), session-85-to-86.md handoff. Markdown only — Session-74 decision. Cole uploads manually to `cbastianBWE/brainwise-internal-docs` (flat repo root); GitHub MCP is READ-ONLY.*

*v88 - Session 84 CLOSE — coach entitlement bugs (Cheryl phantom-credit + Patrice unreachable cert-pool gate) + hero banner thumbnail redesign + CSS bug fix. §110 added (entitlement_source as additive enum CHECK column distinguishing payment source on assessments; trigger logic gates on it). §111 added (coach_client_id discriminator on assessment_purchases distinguishing self-purchase from purchaser-for-client; consumer queries MUST filter `coach_client_id IS NULL`). §112 added (dominant_color pipeline pattern — private-bucket service-role storage transform via `storage.download({transform})`, fire-and-forget on finalize, idempotent helper with non-fatal failure). §113 added (CSS `background-image` accepts only `<url>` and `<gradient>` — a bare hex color is invalid and voids the whole declaration; use `background-color` for solids, split-property pattern for gradient-over-solid-color compositions). Five backend migrations, three Edge Function deploys. No new tables, no new buckets, no rollup-trigger changes. (1) §110 NEW — **Entitlement-source enum on assessment rows distinguishes payment paths.** Standing pattern: when a row can be created through multiple legitimate payment paths and downstream business logic differs by path (free vs paid, self vs coach-paid, cert-pool vs purchase), the row carries an additive `entitlement_source` text column with a CHECK constraint enumerating the paths. Session 84's instance: `assessments.entitlement_source` CHECK in (`free_cert_pool`, `paid_purchase`, `coach_paid_client`, `self_pay_coach_invite`). Why a column not a derived field: the source is the EFFECTIVE-TIME truth about HOW this assessment was paid for, and that truth is needed by triggers and analytics long after the originating context is gone. Deriving it later from joins (purchase rows, cert-pool rows, coach_clients rows) is fragile because the originating row may have been archived, mutated, or otherwise lost its discriminating attribute. The locked sub-rule: a trigger that decrements a finite resource (cert-pool credit, prepaid coupon, etc.) MUST gate on `entitlement_source` — never on the row's mere existence. Session 84's bug-C: `link_assessment_to_coach_client` branch (b) decremented `coach_certifications.free_assessment_uses` on ANY self-completion including paid purchases, because the trigger could not distinguish the source. The fix: gate branch (b) by `NEW.entitlement_source = 'free_cert_pool'`. The column is `NULL`able by design — pre-existing rows from before the column was added are unaffected, and the trigger only fires when the column is explicitly stamped. The frontend MUST stamp this column at row-creation time (or shortly after, via atomic UPDATE guard `.is("entitlement_source", null)`). Pairs with §111 — the two columns are read together to drive entitlement decisions. Applies forward to any future row that can be paid through multiple paths and needs path-aware downstream logic. (2) §111 NEW — **coach_client_id discriminator on assessment_purchases distinguishes self-purchase from purchaser-for-client.** Standing pattern: when a table represents a transaction that can be initiated by a user EITHER for themselves OR for another user, the table carries a nullable FK column identifying the "for-whom" party, and ALL consumer queries that read the table for "what has THIS USER paid for THEMSELVES" MUST filter `<for_whom_fk> IS NULL`. Session 84's instance: `assessment_purchases.coach_client_id uuid` (nullable FK indexed). When NULL, the row represents the buyer purchasing for themselves. When non-NULL, the row represents the buyer (a coach) purchasing FOR a client listed in `coach_clients`. The bug-A pattern surfaced when the consumer query forgot the filter: `consume_assessment_purchase` RPC and `InstrumentSelection.tsx:101` both read `user_id = me` with NO `coach_client_id` filter, so the buyer's coach-bought rows were treated as free credit for the buyer's own assessment. The fix: every SELECT in `consume_assessment_purchase` got `AND coach_client_id IS NULL`; the frontend purchases query got `.is("coach_client_id", null)`. The write side mirrors: `stripe-webhook` v27 coach_order + coach_bulk_order branches write `coach_client_id` so the discriminator is set at row creation. The pattern generalizes to ANY transaction table where the buyer and the recipient can differ: gifted subscriptions, prepaid bundles, sponsored seats, family-plan invitations, gift cards. The discriminator pattern is preferable to maintaining two separate tables (one for self-purchases, one for purchases-for-others) because the rows share most fields and most analytics queries; an additive nullable FK is cheap. The standing rule: when adding a transaction table or extending an existing one, ask "can the buyer and the recipient ever differ?" — if yes, add the discriminator FK on day one and write every consumer query with the filter from day one. The cost of retrofitting after launch (Session 84 had to backfill 8 rows + audit 5 SELECT blocks across an RPC + audit 1 frontend query) is real. Pairs with §110 — entitlement_source on the resulting `assessments` row distinguishes WHICH payment path created it, while coach_client_id on the `assessment_purchases` row distinguishes WHO the purchase was for. (3) §112 NEW — **Dominant-color pipeline pattern for thumbnail-derived background colors on private buckets.** Standing pattern for any feature where a UI surface needs a color derived from an image asset stored in a private bucket. Composition: (a) **Additive nullable text column on the asset table** — `content_assets.dominant_color text NULL` (NULL = not yet computed, the column carries a hex color when populated). (b) **Service-role storage transform** — the helper Edge Function uses a service-role client and calls `storage.download({transform:{width:N,height:N,resize:"cover"}})` to fetch a downsampled version of the asset. The transform parameter is Pro-plan-only and accepts `width >= 1`. Service-role bypasses storage RLS, so the function works on private buckets where a client-side `createSignedUrl` path would require an access-check RPC. (c) **Pure-JS image decoder** — use `jsr:@unpic/pixels@1.2.3` in Deno/Supabase Edge Runtime. The package handles JPEG and PNG with no native deps, which matters because Supabase Edge Functions run on Deno and cannot link native binaries. (d) **Idempotent helper Edge Function** — `compute-dominant-color` v2 checks if `dominant_color` is already set on the target row and returns early if so. This makes a backfill loop safe to retry, makes the fire-and-forget invocation safe to run twice if the upload-finalize path is racey, and makes the helper safe to call manually from a maintenance query. (e) **Non-fatal failure semantics** — when the helper fails (bad image bytes, decode error, transient network), it returns 200 with `{success:false, reason}`, not an error status. The reason: the helper is called fire-and-forget from `finalize-asset-upload`; a 4xx/5xx would surface as a failed upload to the user even though the underlying upload succeeded. Color extraction is a nice-to-have, not a precondition for the asset to be usable. (f) **Fire-and-forget invocation from the upload-finalize path** — `finalize-asset-upload` v4 invokes `compute-dominant-color` for image uploads inside a try/catch that swallows errors. The asset's primary lifecycle (upload, finalize, ref-link) never depends on the color computation. (g) **pg_net rate-limiting on backfill loops** — when running a backfill that iterates over many assets and invokes the helper for each, stagger with `pg_sleep(0.5)` between dispatches. pg_net's async invocation has tight per-instance rate limits and a tight loop will hit them and drop requests silently. Session 84's instance covered 30 of 31 image assets; the one remaining NULL is an orphan library asset not referenced anywhere. Applies forward to any pipeline that derives lightweight metadata from an asset (dominant color, image dimensions, color palette, thumbnail dimensions, audio duration, video first-frame). Standing rule: pipelines that derive optional metadata from a primary asset should be idempotent, fire-and-forget, non-fatal-on-failure, and run on the same path as upload-finalize so the asset is ready-to-render the moment it lands. (4) §113 NEW — **CSS `background-image` accepts only `<url>` and `<gradient>` values; a bare hex color invalidates the whole declaration.** Standing rule and the failure mode it produces. The CSS spec defines `background-image` as accepting one or more `<image>` values where `<image>` is `<url>` or `<gradient>` (`linear-gradient`, `radial-gradient`, etc.) — NOT `<color>`. A bare hex like `#481a69` placed into `background-image`, e.g. `background-image: linear-gradient(...), #481a69;` makes the entire declaration invalid, and the browser silently falls through to whatever the underlying layer's background is. The Session 84 failure mode: heroes were composed with `background-image: ${overlay}, ${dominantColor}` expecting the gradient overlay to darken a solid color background. Because the bare hex is invalid in `background-image`, the gradient was discarded too, the transparent overlay showed the underlying page navy, and every hero rendered navy regardless of the extracted dominant color. The locked pattern: solid colors go in `background-color`; gradients and URLs go in `background-image`. When compositing a gradient OVER a solid color, use BOTH properties — the gradient (with alpha) renders ON TOP of the solid color because the CSS background stacking order paints background-color underneath background-image. The split-property idiom: ``` const heroBackgroundImage = hasColor ? overlay : `${overlay}, ${fallbackGradient}`; const heroBackgroundColor = hasColor ? dominantColor : "transparent"; <div style={{ backgroundImage: heroBackgroundImage, backgroundColor: heroBackgroundColor }} />``` The `transparent` value when there's no solid color preserves the layered-gradient-only path. The standing diagnostic for "this color isn't rendering" on a `background-image` declaration is: open browser devtools, inspect the computed style, see the declaration is missing or shows the invalid-value warning. Five minutes once the diagnostic is run; otherwise the bug looks like a query/data problem and burns hours. Applies anywhere CSS background compositions mix solids and gradients — modal overlays, card backgrounds, hero banners, button states, hover treatments. (5) **Edge Function `compute-dominant-color` v2.** NEW this session, deployed `verify_jwt:false`, Class B `X-Internal-Secret` auth. Reads a row from `content_assets`, downloads the asset via service-role storage transform at 16×16 cover, decodes via `jsr:@unpic/pixels`, computes the dominant color, writes back to `content_assets.dominant_color`. Idempotent (skips if already set). Non-fatal failure (returns 200 with `{success:false, reason}`). v1→v2 switched from public-render-URL to service-role storage.download for private-bucket support. Owed to GitHub `cbastianBWE/brainwise-blueprint` per §92 at `supabase/functions/compute-dominant-color/index.ts`. (6) **Edge Function `finalize-asset-upload` v4.** Fire-and-forget `compute-dominant-color` invocation on image uploads, catch-wrapped. Owed to GitHub per §92. (7) **Edge Function `stripe-webhook` v27.** coach_order + coach_bulk_order branches now write `coach_client_id` to `assessment_purchases` per §111. Owed to GitHub per §92. (8) **Standing property recorded — the editor thumbnail-loss-on-republish bug is editor-side, NOT cascade-side.** Audit log analysis (`super_admin_audit_log` action_type=`certification_path_updated`) reconstructed a real user-reported "thumbnail disappeared" event: upload succeeded, then 39 seconds later a `publishing` action wrote `thumbnail_asset_id=null` with `after_value` showing null. The `_archive_thumbnail_ref_and_maybe_asset` cascade correctly archived the orphan. The cascade is working as designed (§43 ordering, §50 thumbnail-asset linking). The bug is in the editor — local thumbnail state is lost between upload and save/publish across all five thumbnail-bearing editors (CertPathEditor, CurriculumEditor, ModuleEditor, ContentItemEditor, ResourceEditor) because they share the FileUploadField + state + upsert pattern. Logged to build queue with two candidate fixes (confirmation dialog on null-where-was-not-null, or refetch-before-submit merge). Standing diagnostic note: when a user reports "X disappeared," the first query is the audit log — every state-changing super-admin action writes before/after JSON, and the reconstruction is usually conclusive within one query. (9) Standing rules §61-§109 unchanged. No new tables, no new buckets, no rollup-trigger changes. No movement Session 84 on AIRSA Phases 3e-8, SOC 2 written policies, Action-Oriented Voice Redesign, pricing-reads refactor, corporate contract renewal schema change, Clarity Engine. (10) **Edge Function versions at Session 84 close:** `compute-dominant-color` v2 NEW (verify_jwt:false), `finalize-asset-upload` v4 (verify_jwt:false), `stripe-webhook` v27 (verify_jwt:false). All other Edge Functions unchanged from Session 83 close. Owed to GitHub `cbastianBWE/brainwise-blueprint` per §92: this session's three (`compute-dominant-color` v2, `finalize-asset-upload` v4, `stripe-webhook` v27) plus the unreconciled carryover from prior sessions (`content-item-file-upload` v2, `identity-mutation`, `learning-admin-import` v1, `draft-text` v7, `get-content-item-video-url` v1, `content-item-ai-assist` v1, `skills-practice-attachment-upload` v1, `get-lesson-block-asset-urls` v1, and the `create-checkout`/`customer-portal` drift). *v87 - Session 83 CLOSE — super-admin manual completion control + reverse-recount fix + security-scan triage pass. §108 added (private content buckets always get `storage.objects` RLS policies even under Edge-Function service-role mediation; path-segment ownership over table-join). §109 added (derived parent status is recomputed from children, never hard-written). Five backend migrations, one Edge Function v1->v2 deploy. No new tables. No rollup-trigger changes — the existing forward-only rollup chain is untouched. (1) §108 NEW — **Private content buckets always get a `storage.objects` RLS policy floor, even when access is mediated by a service-role Edge Function.** Standing rule surfaced from the Session 83 security pass. The platform\'s storage pattern (§84/§95) is two-layer: storage RLS policies as the floor AND service-role Edge Functions as the access path. Two content buckets created in Session 77 — `content-item-file-uploads` and `skills-practice-attachments` — were created with the Edge Function layer but WITHOUT any `storage.objects` policies. This is not exploitable on its own (RLS enabled + zero policies = default deny; and the Edge Functions use a service-role client that bypasses storage RLS entirely), but it is an incomplete setup, not a design: every other content bucket (`lesson-assets`, `learning-admin-imports`, `departure-exports`) has its policies. The locked rule: a private bucket gets its `storage.objects` policies at creation time, in the same migration that creates the bucket, REGARDLESS of whether an Edge Function will be the live access path. The Edge Function is the convenience path; the RLS policy is the floor that constrains any future direct `supabase.storage.from()` call a developer adds by reflex. A missing floor is a latent footgun — the next direct call either fails silently with no backstop or gets "fixed" by a hastily-added permissive policy that leaks. Sub-rule — **ownership is expressed by path-segment match, not a table join.** When bucket object paths embed the owning user\'s id (the standing convention — `request_asset_upload` and the trainee-upload Edge Functions all build `.../{userId}/...` paths), the ownership predicate is `(storage.foldername(name))[N] = auth.uid()::text`, exactly the pattern the pre-existing `departure-exports` policies use. `storage.foldername()` is 1-based. A table-join policy on `storage.objects` (joining back to `content_item_completions` or `skills_practice_iterations` to prove ownership) runs a correlated subquery on every object access and is more fragile; the path already carries the identity, so use it. Session 83\'s instance: migration `storage_policies_content_and_skills_buckets` added eight policies. `content-item-file-uploads` paths are `{contentItemId}/{userId}/{file}` so the user is path segment 2; all four policies key on segment 2. `skills-practice-attachments` paths are `{contentItemId}/{role}/{userId}/{file}` so the user is segment 3 and the role (`trainee`/`mentor`) is segment 2; the SELECT policy keys on segment 3 ALONE — intentionally, because a trainee is already entitled to see both their own `trainee/`-role file and the `mentor/`-role feedback file that sits under their own id segment (`get_content_item_for_viewer` surfaces `skills_mentor_attachment_url` to the trainee). The INSERT/UPDATE/DELETE policies additionally require segment 2 = `trainee` so a trainee can only write their own `trainee/` files; mentor writes go through the Edge Function as service-role and bypass RLS, so the write policies need no mentor branch. The asymmetry (SELECT broad on segment 3, writes narrowed to the trainee role segment) is deliberate and matches the real entitlement model. (2) §109 NEW — **Derived parent status is recomputed from children, never hard-written.** Standing rule surfaced from the Session 83 reverse-recount bug. In the learning hierarchy, a module\'s status and a curriculum\'s status are DERIVED — they are a function of the completion state of their children (a module is complete when its required content items are complete; a curriculum is complete when its required modules are complete). The forward rollup trigger chain already encodes this for the completed direction. The locked rule: ANY operation that changes a derived parent\'s status must do so by recomputing it from the current child state — never by hard-writing a chosen status value onto the parent row. The Session 83 bug: the first cut of `set_module_completion` and `set_curriculum_completion`, on the "mark incomplete" path, hard-wrote a downgraded status (`not_started` / `active`) directly onto the parent. That produced incoherent states no consumer can render correctly — a `not_started` module sitting above six `completed` required items. The reason hard-writing is wrong is structural, not cosmetic: a derived value has exactly one correct source (its inputs), and any code path that writes it from somewhere else creates a second, conflicting source of truth. The fix (migration `manual_completion_reverse_recount_fix`) rewrote both reverse branches to recount the parent from its children inline. A corollary falls out of this: "mark a parent incomplete" when every child is still complete is a NO-OP — the honest recompute yields `completed`, because that is what the children say — and the RPC returns `changed:false` with an explanatory `note` rather than forcing an incoherent downgrade. The way to make a parent incomplete is to make a child incomplete; the parent follows. This rule applies to any future derived-status field — rollup counters, aggregate progress percentages, computed gates: change the inputs, let the derivation run; never write the derived value directly. Pairs with the standing forward-rollup design (the rollup triggers ARE the recompute for the completed direction) and with the discipline of verifying a migration\'s effect with a separate `execute_sql` — the bug got through the original verification because the test matrix exercised reverse-from-below but never reverse-at-the-tier. (3) **Super-admin manual completion control — three public RPCs.** `set_content_item_completion`, `set_module_completion`, `set_curriculum_completion` — SECURITY DEFINER, search_path locked, `assert_super_admin` + `assert_impersonation_allows(\'permission_change\')` + reason >=10 chars, idempotent, audit-logged via three new `super_admin_action_types` rows added per §99 in the same migration. The curriculum RPC is keyed per-assignment, not per-curriculum, because a curriculum can be assigned more than once to the same user. Forward marks the full subtree complete and CAN certify via the existing rollup; reverse is target-plus-ancestor recompute (§109), never touches children, and can NEVER un-certify — a reverse that would drop a curriculum under an already-certified cert path is refused (`manual_incomplete_blocked_certified_cert_path`). The cert tier reuses the existing `grant_certification`/`revoke_certification` RPCs rather than writing `coach_certifications.status` directly. Three internal helper functions back the public RPCs and are service_role-only (REVOKE from authenticated). (4) **Edge Function `content-item-file-upload` v2.** The `read` action gained an OPTIONAL `target_user_id` param; when present and not equal to the caller it is forwarded to `get_content_item_for_viewer`, which gates on super_admin/mentor. Absent, v2 is byte-identical to v1. Enables a super admin to view another learner\'s uploaded file in the new completion-control artifact inspector. Deployed `verify_jwt:false` (Class A custom auth, unchanged). (5) **Standing property recorded — the assessment paywall remains frontend-only** (unchanged from v86 §7; no Session 83 change). (6) Standing rules §61-§107 unchanged. No new tables, no new buckets, no rollup-trigger changes. No movement Session 83 on AIRSA Phases 3e-8, SOC 2 written policies, Action-Oriented Voice Redesign, pricing-reads refactor, corporate contract renewal schema change, Clarity Engine. (7) **Edge Function versions at Session 83 close:** `content-item-file-upload` v2 ACTIVE (verify_jwt:false). All other Edge Functions unchanged from Session 82 close. Owed to GitHub `cbastianBWE/brainwise-blueprint` per §92: `content-item-file-upload` v2 at `supabase/functions/content-item-file-upload/index.ts`, plus the unreconciled carryover from prior sessions (`identity-mutation`, `learning-admin-import` v1, `draft-text` v7, `get-content-item-video-url` v1, `content-item-ai-assist` v1, `skills-practice-attachment-upload` v1, `get-lesson-block-asset-urls` v1, and the `create-checkout`/`customer-portal` drift). (8) Session 83 close artifacts: build-queue.md v91 entry, this v87 architecture-reference entry (§108, §109), session-83-to-84.md handoff. Markdown only — Session-74 decision. Cole uploads manually to `cbastianBWE/brainwise-internal-docs` (flat repo root); GitHub MCP is READ-ONLY.*

*v86 - Session 82 CLOSE — Mentor-role feature (standalone eligibility flag) + actor-flow/coach-invitation email fixes. §106 added (standalone capability-flag pattern, distinct from emergent-relationship roles). §107 added (server-side email-sender RPC pattern for browser code that must trigger an internal-secret-protected Edge Function). Four backend migrations, one view change, no new tables, no new buckets, no rollup-trigger changes. (1) §106 NEW — **Standalone capability flag vs. emergent-relationship role.** Standing pattern for deciding how to represent "is this user allowed to do X." Two shapes exist on the platform: an *emergent role*, where a capability is inferred from the existence of relationship rows (a mentor is a user with a `coach_mentor_assignments` row — §84/v84); and a *standalone capability flag*, an explicit boolean column the user either has or does not. Session 82's decision: the mentor capability needed BOTH. The relationship rows still answer "which trainees does this mentor mentor," but they cannot answer "is this user eligible to be a mentor at all" — and that second question is what gates the `/mentor` route, the sidebar entry, and the `assign_mentor` RPC. The locked rule: when a capability must be (a) gate-able before any relationship row exists, and (b) grant-able/revoke-able by an admin as a deliberate act, it needs a standalone flag — an emergent-from-relationships definition is insufficient. Session 82 added `users.is_mentor` (boolean, NOT NULL, default false). This does NOT contradict v84 — v84 said there is no `mentor` *account_type*, which remains true; `is_mentor` is a capability column, not an account type. The account types are still super_admin, coach, company_admin, corporate_employee, individual, org_admin. The flag is independent of `account_type` AND independent of `coach_mentor_assignments`. Frontend mirrors this: `accountRoles.ts` derives an `isMentor` boolean exactly the way `isPractitionerCoach` is derived, and a `MentorGuard` route guard allows on `isMentor || isSuperAdmin`. (2) §107 NEW — **Server-side email-sender RPC for browser-triggered internal-secret-protected functions.** Standing pattern for the recurring failure where frontend code calls the `send-email` Edge Function directly and it fails because `send-email` is gated by `INTERNAL_FUNCTION_SECRET` (§verify_jwt remediation, Session 33) which a browser cannot and must not hold. The wrong fix is to weaken `send-email`'s gate. The locked pattern: a SECURITY DEFINER RPC does the privileged `net.http_post` to `send-email` server-side, reading the secret from the Vault (`vault.decrypted_secrets`, name `INTERNAL_FUNCTION_SECRET`) — exactly the `notify_user` pattern. The browser calls the RPC; the RPC holds the secret. Three sub-rules: (a) **Email HTML construction is NOT privileged — only the secret-protected call is.** The frontend may build the email HTML and pass it to the RPC as a parameter (Session 82 chose this for `create_actor_debrief_order` — a new `p_email_html` param — rather than reproducing the BrainWise email template as a fragile PL/pgSQL string literal). (b) **The email send must never roll back the business operation.** Wrap the `net.http_post` in `BEGIN...EXCEPTION WHEN OTHERS` and report the outcome in the return JSON (`email_dispatched` / `dispatched`) — an email hiccup must not undo a valid order or invitation. (c) **A generic email-sender RPC must be role-gated.** A wide-open RPC that sends BrainWise-branded mail to any address is an abuse surface. `send_coach_invitation_email(p_to, p_subject, p_html, p_email_type)` — the generic sender added Session 82 — is restricted to coach / practitioner-coach / super-admin. Caveat documented: `email_dispatched:true` confirms `net.http_post` *queued* the request with the correct URL/headers/secret; `net.http_post` is asynchronous and this does not by itself confirm `send-email` returned 200. The two Session-82 instances: `create_actor_debrief_order` (inlined the `net.http_post` block as the fast fix) and `send_coach_invitation_email` (the generic primitive). Standing note: `create_actor_debrief_order` could later be refactored to call `send_coach_invitation_email` so the `net.http_post` block is not duplicated. (3) **`users.is_mentor` column.** Boolean, NOT NULL, default false. Backfilled `true` for the one existing approved mentor. A small read-helper accompanies it with clean grants. (4) **New RPC `set_mentor_role`.** One RPC grants AND revokes via a boolean `p_is_mentor`; SECURITY DEFINER, `assert_super_admin` + `assert_impersonation_allows('permission_change')` + reason ≥10 chars; logs one `mentor_role_changed` audit action with before/after JSON; idempotent (`changed:false` on a redundant call). The `mentor_role_changed` action_type (category `admin_role_management`, tier2, MFA + justification, mutation, impersonation-denylisted) was INSERTed in the SAME migration per §99. `assign_mentor` was updated to reject an un-approved mentor with `mentor_not_approved`. (5) **`create_actor_debrief_order` — 5-arg signature.** Adds `p_email_html` (DEFAULT NULL, backward-safe); sends the invitation email server-side per §107; old 4-arg overload DROPPED so all calls resolve to the 5-arg version. (6) **`coach_clients_client_view` — exposes `invitation_source`.** Additive column on the `security_invoker` view so the frontend can distinguish actor-debrief rows (`invitation_source = 'actor_debrief'`, null payment intent by design) from genuine self-pay rows. (7) **Standing property recorded — the assessment paywall is frontend-enforced only.** `start_assessment` was read in full Session 82 and has no payment gate; the "paywall" on the assessment page is purely a frontend display decision. Not a security hole in itself (assessment-taking is not the monetized artifact — results/reports are), but worth knowing: any backend-only caller of `start_assessment` bypasses the paywall. (8) Standing rules §61–§105 unchanged. No rollup-trigger changes, no new tables. No movement Session 82 on AIRSA Phases 3e-8, SOC 2 written policies, Action-Oriented Voice Redesign, pricing-reads refactor, corporate contract renewal schema change, Clarity Engine. (9) **Edge Function versions at Session 82 close:** no Edge Function code was changed this session — `send-email` was untouched (the fix routed AROUND it via RPCs, not through a redeploy). All Edge Functions unchanged from Session 81 close. Owed to GitHub per §92 unchanged from Session 81. Cole uploads manually to `cbastianBWE/brainwise-internal-docs` (flat repo root); GitHub MCP is READ-ONLY.*

*v85 - Session 81 CLOSE — Group V certification work + production-bug firefighting. §105 added (adopt-instead-of-throw idempotency for enrollment-style RPCs whose target row may be pre-created by an upstream flow). One backend migration, one Edge Function fix. No new tables, no new buckets, no rollup-trigger changes. (1) §105 NEW — **Adopt-instead-of-throw idempotency for enrollment RPCs whose key row is pre-created upstream.** Standing pattern for the case where an RPC's job is to create a parent record plus its dependent rows, but a *different* flow legitimately pre-creates the parent record on its own for an unrelated reason. The naive idempotency guard — "if the parent row already exists, throw a duplicate error" — is wrong here, because the parent row existing is the NORMAL state, not a duplicate. Session 81's instance: `enroll_user_in_certification_path` creates a `coach_certifications` row plus the cert path's `user_curriculum_assignments`. But the coach-invite acceptance flow ALSO creates a bare `coach_certifications` row on every invite — by design, because `certification_type` on that row drives assessment-ordering gating. The old guard threw `user_already_has_active_certification_of_this_type` whenever a cert row of the type existed, which made enrollment impossible for any invited coach. The locked pattern: (a) **Look up the existing parent row instead of blindly inserting.** If an `in_progress`/`certified` cert row of the type exists, ADOPT it — use its id as the parent for the dependent rows. Never create a second parent row; never UPDATE or mutate the adopted row (it may carry state — e.g. a `certified` status — that this RPC has no business changing). (b) **If no parent row exists, create one** — the original behavior, unchanged. (c) **Dedup the dependent rows in code.** For each dependent row the RPC would create, skip it if an equivalent active row already exists (matched on the natural key — for Session 81, `user_id + curriculum_id + source='certification_path' + status='active'`). This makes the RPC safe to call repeatedly and safe on a partially-populated parent. Note: this dedup MUST be in code when the table has no UNIQUE constraint enforcing it — `user_curriculum_assignments` has only a PK, so nothing in the DB prevents duplicate assignments; the RPC is the only guard. (d) **Preserve the original duplicate error for the genuine no-op.** If the parent row was adopted AND zero new dependent rows were created because they all already existed, THEN it is a true redundant call — throw the original error. The error is not deleted, it is narrowed to the case it actually describes. (e) **Return a flag distinguishing adopt from create** (`cert_row_adopted: true|false`) so callers and audit logs can tell which path ran. The pattern generalizes to any "create parent + children, but parent may pre-exist" RPC — enrollment, subscription provisioning, workspace setup. The decision rule: if an upstream flow legitimately owns parent-row creation for its own reasons, the downstream RPC adopts; it does not throw, and it does not fight the upstream flow by trying to "fix" or replace the row. Pairs with §94 (read the deployed RPC body before rewriting — the full `enroll_user_in_certification_path` body was read via `pg_get_functiondef` first) and the standing discipline of verifying a migration's effect with a separate `execute_sql` rather than trusting `apply_migration` success. (2) **Password reset — `identity-mutation` Edge Function fix.** The implicit auth flow delivers password-recovery tokens in the URL hash. An Edge Function that needs to act as the recovering user must call `setSession({access_token, refresh_token})` to load a real session before `updateUser` — `getClaims` validates a token statelessly and will succeed, but `updateUser` needs a loaded session and fails with "Auth session missing!" without one. Standing note for any Edge Function performing an authenticated mutation on behalf of a user arriving via an email link: the frontend must forward both tokens in the request body, and the function must `setSession` before the mutation. The corrected function was deployed with the impersonation-gate helper INLINED (no `_shared/` import) — consistent with §80: a function deployed via MCP must have its shared helpers inlined or the bundler fails with "Module not found". (3) Standing rules §61–§104 unchanged. No movement Session 81 on AIRSA Phases 3e-8, SOC 2 written policies, Action-Oriented Voice Redesign, pricing-reads refactor, corporate contract renewal schema change, Clarity Engine. (4) **Edge Function versions at Session 81 close:** `identity-mutation` redeployed with the `setSession` fix (inlined impersonation gate). All other Edge Functions unchanged from Session 80 close. Owed to GitHub `cbastianBWE/brainwise-blueprint` per §92: `identity-mutation` (NOT currently in the repo at all — deployed direct, never committed; needs a fresh `supabase/functions/identity-mutation/index.ts`), plus the unreconciled carryover (`learning-admin-import` v1, `draft-text` v7, `get-content-item-video-url` v1, `content-item-ai-assist` v1, `skills-practice-attachment-upload` v1, `content-item-file-upload` v1, `get-lesson-block-asset-urls` v1, and the `create-checkout` / `customer-portal` drift past last-committed v56/v41). (5) Session 81 close artifacts: build-queue.md v89 entry, this v85 architecture-reference entry (§105), session-81-to-82.md handoff. Markdown only — Session-74 decision, no `.docx`. Cole uploads manually to `cbastianBWE/brainwise-internal-docs` (flat repo root); GitHub MCP is READ-ONLY.*

*v84 - Session 80 CLOSE — Group C Phase 6 mentor portal + super-admin Learning Admin v1→v2 shipped. §104 added (transaction-local GUC actor-bypass pattern for RPCs that must run in a cron/no-JWT context while preserving fail-closed behavior for user calls). One new table, one new storage bucket, one new Edge Function, one new pg_cron job, and a body of new RPCs. (1) §104 NEW — **Transaction-local GUC actor-bypass for cron-reachable RPCs.** Standing pattern for the case where an RPC that normally derives its actor from `auth.uid()` and enforces `assert_super_admin()` must ALSO be reachable from a pg_cron context — which has no JWT, so `auth.uid()` is null and the super-admin assertion would fail. The naive fixes are both bad: dropping the auth check opens the RPC to anyone; forking a separate cron-only copy duplicates business logic that will drift. The locked pattern: (a) **A transaction-local GUC carries the actor.** The cron processor sets a custom GUC — Session 80 uses `app.scheduled_assignment_actor` — via `set_config('app.scheduled_assignment_actor', '<uuid>', true)` where the third argument `true` scopes the setting to the current transaction only. (b) **Each guarded function reads the GUC and branches.** At the top of the auth section: `IF current_setting('app.scheduled_assignment_actor', true) IS NOT NULL THEN` use that UUID as the actor and SKIP the `auth.uid()` null-check and `assert_super_admin()`; `ELSE` run the normal user-facing gate unchanged. The `true` second argument to `current_setting` makes a missing GUC return null instead of erroring. (c) **Fail-closed is preserved for user calls.** When the GUC is unset — every normal user request — the function behaves exactly as before; the bypass branch is unreachable. Verified Session 80: with the GUC unset, the guarded functions still reject a non-super-admin and still reject a null actor. (d) **The GUC is set only by trusted callers.** Only `process_due_scheduled_assignments()` — itself a SECDEF function invoked by the pg_cron job — sets the GUC, and it sets it per row inside its own transaction, so the actor is scoped to one assignment's processing and cannot leak. (e) **Defense-in-depth still holds underneath.** The functions' own `WITH CHECK` RLS and table constraints are unchanged; the GUC bypass only skips the *actor-identity* gate, not the data-integrity gates. Session 80 applied this to five functions — `assign_curriculum_directly`, `assign_module_directly`, `enroll_user_in_certification_path`, `assign_mentor`, `log_super_admin_action` (so the cron-context audit row is attributed to the stored actor rather than failing on a null `auth.uid()`). `notify_user` needed no change — it has no `auth.uid()` dependency. The pattern generalizes to any future "this RPC must also run on a schedule" requirement: a transaction-local GUC + a read-and-branch guard is the standing answer, never a forked cron copy. Pairs with the Session-73 lesson that SECDEF RPCs which call `log_super_admin_action` must reach it with a usable actor — here the actor arrives via the GUC instead of a JWT-bearing client. (2) **Mentor is not a role — it is a relationship row.** There is no `mentor` account_type and none should be added. A user is a mentor of a trainee if and only if a `coach_mentor_assignments` row links them. The account types remain super_admin, coach, company_admin, corporate_employee, individual, org_admin. Mentor-facing surfaces gate on the existence of `coach_mentor_assignments` rows (and super admin sees all), not on an account_type check. The new `has_lms_permission` helper and `list_mentor_trainees` RPC encode this. (3) **New table `scheduled_assignments`.** Holds a future-dated learning assignment until a cron processor applies it. 15 columns, RLS super-admin-only, 3 indexes, named CHECK constraints (including a justification ≥10 chars) and a status enum `pending`/`processing`/`completed`/`partial`/`failed`/`cancelled`. Written via `create_scheduled_assignment`, read via `list_scheduled_assignments`, cancelled (pending rows only) via `cancel_scheduled_assignment`, processed by `process_due_scheduled_assignments()`. The `create` RPC rejects a past `scheduled_for` date (SQLSTATE 22023) — verified. (4) **New pg_cron job `process_due_scheduled_assignments_daily`** at `20 6 * * *`, active. Invokes `process_due_scheduled_assignments()`, which loops due `pending` rows, sets the §104 GUC per row, calls the single-target `*_directly` / `assign_mentor` / `enroll_user_in_certification_path` functions, and stamps each row's terminal status with per-row isolation. (5) **New bulk-assignment RPC family.** Seven thin-loop RPCs (`assign_curriculum_bulk`, `assign_module_bulk`, `enroll_users_in_certification_path_bulk`, `assign_mentor_bulk`, `unassign_curriculum_bulk`, `unassign_module_bulk`, `unassign_mentor_bulk`) — each loops the corresponding single-target function with per-element exception isolation, caps at 500 elements, and returns the standard `{operation,requested,succeeded,failed,results[]}` shape. `list_all_learning_assignments()` is the cross-trainee read backing the unassign UI (three arrays — curriculum/module/mentor — active rows only). This standard bulk shape (`requested`/`succeeded`/`failed`/`results[]` with per-row `status`+`detail`) is now the platform convention for any bulk admin operation. (6) **Mentor-pair resolution RPCs.** `get_mentorable_certifications(p_mentor_user_id, p_trainee_user_id)` returns a trainee's certifications filtered to those the given mentor is qualified to mentor — the qualification rule (mentor holds a `certified` credential whose type matches, or `ai_transformation_ptp_coach` covering `ptp_coach`/`ai_transformation_coach`, or `my_brainwise_coach` covering all) is lifted verbatim from `assign_mentor` so the two never disagree. `assign_mentor_pairs_bulk(p_mentor_user_id, p_pairs jsonb, p_reason)` takes `{trainee_user_id, certification_id}` pairs (each trainee carries its own certification id — a single shared `p_certification_id` cannot express this), loops `assign_mentor`, per-row isolation. Standing note: a mentor must be `certified`; the trainee's certification being mentored is normally `in_progress` and that is correct — `assign_mentor` does not require the trainee's certification to be `certified`. (7) **New Edge Function `learning-admin-import` v1** — ACTIVE, `verify_jwt:true`, Class A (`auth.getClaims`, `userClient`/`adminClient` split, built on the `set-account-type` pattern). The frontend parses an xlsx with SheetJS and POSTs JSON rows; the function resolves names/emails to IDs (zero-match and ambiguous-match both fail that row), dispatches to the bulk RPCs as the authenticated super admin, and returns a per-row report. Backed by a new private `learning-admin-imports` storage bucket (10MB, xlsx/csv) and the `get_learning_import_reference()` RPC that feeds the downloadable template's reference sheet. (8) `get_content_item_for_viewer` gained an additive `written_submission` block (latest written submission's id/content/char_count/iteration_number/submitted_at + review fields) — additive, no overload, consistent with the §101 completion-cascade additive-field discipline. (9) No rollup-trigger changes. Standing rules §61–§103 unchanged. NO movement Session 80 on: Group V certification page, AIRSA Phases 3e-8, SOC 2 written policies, Action-Oriented Voice Redesign, pricing-reads refactor, corporate contract renewal schema change, Clarity Engine. (10) **Edge Function versions at Session 80 close:** `learning-admin-import` v1 NEW ACTIVE (verify_jwt:true, Class A). All other Edge Functions unchanged from Session 79 close. Owed to GitHub `cbastianBWE/brainwise-blueprint` per §92: `learning-admin-import` v1, plus the unreconciled carryover (`draft-text` v7, `get-content-item-video-url` v1, `content-item-ai-assist` v1, `skills-practice-attachment-upload` v1, `content-item-file-upload` v1, `get-lesson-block-asset-urls` v1, and the `create-checkout` / `customer-portal` drift past last-committed v56/v41). *v83 - Session 79 CLOSE — lesson_blocks trainee viewer shipped; Group W complete. §102 added (trainee viewer reuses the authoring `BlockRenderer` via a `mode` prop — supersedes the Session-78 separate-renderer decision). §103 added (paged-section progression: continue-delimiter `button_stack` blocks are consumed, not rendered). **Three backend changes, all migrations applied and separately verified.** (a) Migration `add_cascade_to_complete_lesson` — `complete_lesson`'s return jsonb gains the `cascade` block via `public._compute_completion_cascade(v_caller_id, p_content_item_id)`, bringing it in line with the six Session-78 completion RPCs; §101 now covers all seven completion RPCs. (b) **New RPC `get_lesson_block_assets_for_trainee(p_content_item_id uuid, p_user_id uuid DEFAULT NULL)`** — migration `add_get_lesson_block_assets_for_trainee`. SECURITY DEFINER, SET search_path. Access model mirrors `get_content_item_video_asset`: self with an active-or-completed `user_curriculum_assignments` row on a curriculum containing the parent module, OR mentor via `coach_mentor_assignments`, OR super admin. Reuses the existing `_walk_block_config_for_asset_refs` helper to enumerate nested asset refs. GRANT to `authenticated` + `service_role`, REVOKE anon/PUBLIC. This settled the Session-78 open question — a parallel `_for_trainee` RPC was built rather than widening the super-admin-gated `get_lesson_block_assets`, because the two access models are different enough that a single role-branching function would be less clear (§94 read-before-rewrite discipline still applied — the super-admin function body was read first to confirm a clean parallel was simpler than a widen). (c) Migration `widen_lesson_trainee_read_policies_to_completed` — three RLS policies (`lesson_blocks_trainee_read`, `content_assets_trainee_read`, `content_asset_versions_trainee_read`) widened from `uca.status = 'active'` to `uca.status IN ('active','completed')` via in-place `ALTER POLICY`. **Note for future RLS work: Postgres has no `CREATE OR REPLACE POLICY` — an existing policy is modified in place with `ALTER POLICY` (or DROP+CREATE).** This aligns the lesson-blocks trainee read path with `get_content_item_for_viewer`'s already-`('active','completed')` access model — a trainee who has completed a curriculum must still be able to re-open its lessons. **New Edge Function `get-lesson-block-asset-urls` v1** — deployed `verify_jwt:false` (Class A custom auth, own `getClaims`), NO `_shared/` imports so the repo source and the deployable source are byte-identical (avoids the §80 inline-divergence problem). A JWT-bound client calls `get_lesson_block_assets_for_trainee` for the access check, then a service-role client signs the `lesson-assets` private-bucket paths (the §95 pattern: storage RLS stays locked, SECDEF-RPC + service-role-Edge-Function proxy is the trainee read path). Returns `{assets:[{asset_id,signed_url,mime_type,asset_kind}],expires_in_seconds}`. **§102 NEW — the trainee lesson_blocks viewer reuses the authoring `BlockRenderer.tsx` via a `mode` prop; it does NOT use a separate renderer.** This SUPERSEDES the Session-78 locked decision (a fully separate from-scratch `LessonBlockRenderer.tsx` sharing only CSS). The shipped design: `BlockRenderer.tsx` takes a new `mode="trainee"` prop plus two optional props — `onBlockComplete` and `savedProgress` — that no-op when `mode` is the authoring default. Rationale for the override: component reuse guarantees pixel-identical trainee and authoring output and structurally eliminates the visual-drift risk a parallel renderer carries; the orchestration-divergence concern that motivated the separate-renderer decision is satisfied by the `mode` prop and the no-op props, not by code duplication. Standing rule: when a trainee surface must render exactly what an authoring surface renders, prefer a `mode`-discriminated single component over a forked renderer — the forked renderer's only advantage (orchestration isolation) is achievable with a prop, while its cost (two code paths that silently drift) is permanent. The authoring AI-pane components (`src/components/super-admin/lesson-blocks/ai-pane/`) are NOT part of `BlockRenderer` and remain super-admin-gated; the trainee viewer correctly exposes no AI authoring surface. **§103 NEW — paged-section lesson progression: continue-delimiter blocks are consumed, not rendered.** The lesson_blocks viewer renders ONE section at a time (Model B), not one continuous scroll. Section boundaries are authored `button_stack` blocks that contain an `action_type:"continue"` button; the viewer's sectioning pass CONSUMES these delimiter blocks (they are not rendered as content) and the viewer's own Continue control replaces them. Navigation is fully open — Continue/Previous step linearly and the sidebar TOC jumps to any section with no locking; only final lesson completion is gated, on `allGatedComplete && allSectionsVisited` (`visitedSections` is a `Set<number>` seeded `{0}`, updated on every section change). A lesson with zero continue-delimiter blocks renders as a single section (graceful fallback). Furthest-position persistence is monotonic: a `furthestSectionRef` only advances, the debounced `upsert_lesson_progress` early-returns when the current index is behind it, and resume sets the ref to the resumed index. This supersedes the §3.8 scope-doc text (single-scroll + scroll-to-bottom gate); `content-item-viewer-scope.md` §3.8 should be updated to the paged-section Model B design. (1) **Group W is COMPLETE** — lesson_blocks was the 8th and final content item viewer. The X→Y→Z→V→W arc now has X, Y, Z, W done; **V (the Certification page) is the only group not started.** (2) **Frontend completion/progress seams.** `useCompletionReporter` gained `reportProgress(rpcName, rpcArgs)` — a raw RPC call with no query invalidation, no cascade read, no `isReporting` flip — alongside the unchanged `reportCompletion`. `reportProgress` and the new `useLessonBlockAssets` hook are the SCORM/API export seams for incremental-progress viewers; export tooling itself stays post-launch (the v1 viewer ships only the seams, per scope §2.3). The lesson_blocks viewer is the one viewer that reports progress repeatedly before final completion; the Session-78 `useCompletionReporter` refactor was confirmed to support this cleanly because `reportProgress` is a separate path that does not touch the cascade machinery. (3) **Single source of truth for interactive-block state.** sessionStorage was removed from all four interactive renderers — `lesson_block_progress.completion_data` is authoritative. Each renderer seeds in-memory `useState` lazily from a `savedProgress` prop; a `completionFiredRef` suppresses re-firing the completion effect on an already-complete block. The block-progress query is attempt-scoped (`.eq("attempt_number", currentAttempt)`, `attempts_count` in the query key); `start_lesson_reattempt` resets `content_item_completions` but does not delete prior `lesson_block_progress` rows, so attempts are isolated by `attempt_number`. (4) **Pre-existing bug corrected in the shared `BlockRenderer`:** `MatchTrainee`'s `rightsSorted` used a deterministic `client_id` sort, not a shuffle — match questions were trivially solvable by row position. Fixed with `stableShuffle(pairs, \`${blockClientId}:${question.client_id}:match-right\`)`; the `:match-right` seed suffix avoids collision with the ranking/timeline shuffle seeds. Because the fix is in the shared renderer it also corrects the authoring preview. (5) No new tables, columns, or buckets. No rollup-trigger changes. Standing rules §61-§101 unchanged. NO movement Session 79 on: AIRSA Phases 3e-8, SOC 2 written policies, Action-Oriented Voice Redesign, pricing-reads refactor, corporate contract renewal schema change, Clarity Engine.
